Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Conditions of Zakat: Who Must Pay?
Ruling on the obligation of zakat and its conditions, with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for zakat obligation according to the Hanafi school and identify which categories are exempt from zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat is due only on the free, adult, sane Muslim who owns nisab for a full year.

This lesson establishes the foundational conditions for zakat. The Hanafi school specifies clear exemptions for minors, the insane, and the mukatab, based on strong hadith evidence. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The opening statement declares that zakat is wajib (obligatory). Note the hukm level: wajib in Hanafi terminology.
Zakat is often called fard in other schools, but Hanafi matn uses wajib.
2
List the conditions for obligation
The text states: free (hurr), Muslim, sane (aqil), adult (baligh), owner of nisab with complete ownership (milk tam), and passage of a full year (hawl).
These are shurut al-wujub (conditions of obligation), not shurut al-sihha.
3
Identify the exempt categories
Three are explicitly exempted: minor (sabiyy), insane (majnun), and mukatab (a slave with emancipation contract).
The mukatab is exempt because his property is not fully his own.
4
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith of Ali (raf' al-qalam) establishes that children and insane persons are not legally accountable, thus no obligation.
This hadith is a general principle in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note the authority weight
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi position, and is mufta bihi.
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الزَّكَاةِ
الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِّ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغِ إِذَا مَلَكَ نِصَابًا مِلْكًا تَامًّا وَحَالَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَوْلُ شُرُوطُ وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى صِبِيٍّ وَلَا مَجْنُونٍ وَلَا مُكَاتَبٍ زَكَاةٌ
وَجْه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغ 
عَنْ جَابِرٍ, قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْمُكَاتَبِ زَكَاةٌ حَتَّى يُعْتَقَ» (سنن الدار قطني بَابُ لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْمُكَاتَبِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى يُعْتَقَ، نمبر: 1960)
وَجْه : (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغ 
عَنْ عَلِيٍّ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ : " رُفِعَ الْقَلَمُ عَنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ : عَنِ النَّائِمِ حَتَّى يَسْتَيْقِظَ، وَعَنِ الصَّبِيِّ حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ، وَعَنِ الْمَجْنُونِ حَتَّى يَعْقِلَ " (أبو داود: بَابٌ فِي الْمَجْنُونِ يَسْرِقُ أَوْ يُصِيبُ حَدًّا، نمبر: 4403، كتاب الحدود : 4403 / ابن ماجة: بَابُ طَلَاقِ الْمَعْتُوهِ وَالصَّغِيرِ وَالنَّائِمِ، نمبر: 2042)
وَجْه : (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغِ 
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ, قَالَ:
«لَا يَجِبُ عَلَى مَالِ الصَّغِيرِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى تَجِبَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ». (سنن الدار قطني، نمبر: 1981)
وَجْه (٤) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِّ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ 
عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ» (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ : مَنْ قَالَ : لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ: 10126)
وَجْه:(١) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ 
عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ خَطَبَ النَّاسَ فَقَالَ: «أَلَا مَنْ وَلِيَ يَتِيمًا لَهُ مَالٌ فَلْيَتَّجِرْ فِيهِ، وَلَا يَتْرُكْهُ حَتَّى تَأْكُلَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ» ( الترمذي : بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ مَالِ اليَتِيم، 641)
وَجْه (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِم الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغ 
سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الخُدْرِيَّ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقٍ صَدَقَةٌ» (بخاري : بَابُ زَكَاةِ الوَرِقِ،: 1447)
اصول : زکوۃ اسلام کا ایک اہم رکن ہے قرآن کریم میں تقریبا ۸۰ جگہ نماز کے ساتھ زکوۃ کا ذکر ملتا ہے۔ اصول : زکوۃ کے وجوب کے شرائط : ۱ آزاد ۲ عاقل بالغ ۴ مسلمان ۵ نصاب کا مالک ہو ۶ نصاب پر ملک مکمل ہو مالے مال پر حولان حول ہو جائے۔
Book of Zakat. Zakat is obligatory upon the free Muslim, sane, adult, when he owns a nisab with complete ownership, and a year passes over it. Conditions of obligation of zakat. And there is no zakat upon a minor, nor an insane person, nor a mukatab. Evidence (1): Hadith of Jabir: 'There is no zakat on the property of a mukatab until he is freed.' Evidence (2): Hadith of Ali: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' Evidence (3): Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Zakat is not obligatory on the property of a minor until prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' Evidence (4): Saying of Ibrahim: 'There is no zakat on the property of an orphan until he reaches puberty.' Evidence (1) of al-Shafi'i: Hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Whoever is the guardian of an orphan with wealth, let him trade with it and not leave it until it is consumed by sadaqah.' Evidence (2): Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five camels, less than five silver ounces, less than five wasqs.' Principle: Zakat is an important pillar of Islam; it is mentioned about 80 times with prayer in the Quran. Conditions of obligation of zakat: 1) free, 2) sane, adult, 4) Muslim, 5) owner of nisab, 6) complete ownership, 7) one lunar year passes.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri begins the Book of Zakat with a clear ruling statement: zakat is wajib (obligatory) upon a person who meets five conditions: (1) free (not a slave), (2) Muslim, (3) sane (aql), (4) adult (baligh), (5) owner of a nisab with full ownership (milk tam), and (6) a full lunar year (hawl) passes over that nisab. It then explicitly exempts three categories: minors (sabiyy), insane persons (majnun), and mukatab (a slave who has made a contract for emancipation). The exemption of minors and insane is based on the hadith of 'raf' al-qalam' (the pen is lifted), meaning they are not legally responsible. The exemption of mukatab is because he is still a slave and his property is not fully his. The text then provides several hadith proofs supporting these conditions. It also presents the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that zakat is obligatory on the wealth of an orphan (or minor) based on the hadith instructing guardians to trade the orphan's wealth so it is not consumed by sadaqah (i.e., zakat). The Shafi'i school holds that zakat is due on the wealth of minors and insane persons, and the guardian must pay it. The Hanafi school responds by prioritizing the hadiths that explicitly exempt minors and insane, considering the Shafi'i evidence as weak or interpretable. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes the conditions: free, sane, adult, Muslim, owner of nisab, complete ownership, passage of one year.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakah): The obligatory charity due on specific wealth under specific conditions.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation (approx. 85g gold or 595g silver).
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to purchase his freedom in installments.
الحول (al-hawl): The passage of one full lunar year over the nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a condition for zakat obligation?
A) Being Muslim
B) Being free
C) Being a traveler (musafir)
D) Being an adult

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only obligatory when all six conditions are met; minors, insane, and mukatab are explicitly exempt.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Zakat for Minors: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on the obligation of zakat and its conditions, with hadith proofs and dispute with Shafi'i on zakat for orphans.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on zakat for minors and insane persons, citing their respective proofs, and explain the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school exempts minors and insane from zakat, while Shafi'i obligates it; the key is legal accountability.

This lesson dives into a well-known ikhtilaf. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith of raf' al-qalam, while the Shafi'i school uses a hadith about an orphan's property. Understanding this dispute clarifies the role of legal capacity (ahliyyah) in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
No zakat is due on the wealth of minors, insane persons, or mukatab.
Based on the hadith of Ali and Ibn Abbas.
2
State the Shafi'i position
Zakat is obligatory on the wealth of minors and insane persons; the guardian must pay it.
Based on the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb.
3
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Hadith of Ali (raf' al-qalam) establishes no accountability. Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'No zakat on minor's wealth until prayer becomes obligatory.'
These are explicit in exempting minors.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proofs
Hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Whoever is guardian of an orphan with wealth, let him trade it lest it be consumed by sadaqah.' This implies zakat is due.
Also hadith of Abu Sa'id on nisab thresholds.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i hadith is weak (mursal or disputed chain) or interpreted as a recommendation to trade, not an obligation of zakat. The explicit exemptions take precedence.
Hanafi usul prioritizes explicit texts over implied ones.
6
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis do not pay zakat on behalf of minors; Shafi'is do. This affects the orphan's wealth management.
This is a clear practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الزَّكَاةِ
الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِّ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغِ إِذَا مَلَكَ نِصَابًا مِلْكًا تَامًّا وَحَالَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَوْلُ شُرُوطُ وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى صِبِيٍّ وَلَا مَجْنُونٍ وَلَا مُكَاتَبٍ زَكَاةٌ
وَجْه: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغ

وَجْه : (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغِ 
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ, قَالَ:
«لَا يَجِبُ عَلَى مَالِ الصَّغِيرِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى تَجِبَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ». (سنن الدار قطني، نمبر: 1981)

عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى يَحْتَلِمَ» (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ : مَنْ قَالَ : لَيْسَ فِي مَالِ الْيَتِيمِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ: 10126)

عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ خَطَبَ النَّاسَ فَقَالَ: «أَلَا مَنْ وَلِيَ يَتِيمًا لَهُ مَالٌ فَلْيَتَّجِرْ فِيهِ، وَلَا يَتْرُكْهُ حَتَّى تَأْكُلَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ» ( الترمذي : بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ مَالِ اليَتِيم، 641)

سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الخُدْرِيَّ، قَالَ : قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقٍ صَدَقَةٌ» (بخاري : بَابُ زَكَاةِ الوَرِقِ،: 1447)

Book of Zakat. Zakat is obligatory upon the free Muslim, sane, adult, when he owns a nisab with complete ownership, and a year passes over it. Conditions of obligation of zakat. And there is no zakat upon a minor, nor an insane person, nor a mukatab. Evidence (1): Hadith of Jabir: 'There is no zakat on the property of a mukatab until he is freed.' Evidence (2): Hadith of Ali: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he becomes sane.' Evidence (3): Hadith of Ibn Abbas: 'Zakat is not obligatory on the property of a minor until prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' Evidence (4): Saying of Ibrahim: 'There is no zakat on the property of an orphan until he reaches puberty.' Evidence (1) of al-Shafi'i: Hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb: 'Whoever is the guardian of an orphan with wealth, let him trade with it and not leave it until it is consumed by sadaqah.' Evidence (2): Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five camels, less than five silver ounces, less than five wasqs.' Principle: Zakat is an important pillar of Islam; it is mentioned about 80 times with prayer in the Quran. Conditions of obligation of zakat: 1) free, 2) sane, adult, 4) Muslim, 5) owner of nisab, 6) complete ownership, 7) one lunar year passes.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri begins the Book of Zakat with a clear ruling statement: zakat is wajib (obligatory) upon a person who meets five conditions: (1) free (not a slave), (2) Muslim, (3) sane (aql), (4) adult (baligh), (5) owner of a nisab with full ownership (milk tam), and (6) a full lunar year (hawl) passes over that nisab. It then explicitly exempts three categories: minors (sabiyy), insane persons (majnun), and mukatab (a slave who has made a contract for emancipation). The exemption of minors and insane is based on the hadith of 'raf' al-qalam' (the pen is lifted), meaning they are not legally responsible. The exemption of mukatab is because he is still a slave and his property is not fully his. The text then provides several hadith proofs supporting these conditions. It also presents the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues that zakat is obligatory on the wealth of an orphan (or minor) based on the hadith instructing guardians to trade the orphan's wealth so it is not consumed by sadaqah (i.e., zakat). The Shafi'i school holds that zakat is due on the wealth of minors and insane persons, and the guardian must pay it. The Hanafi school responds by prioritizing the hadiths that explicitly exempt minors and insane, considering the Shafi'i evidence as weak or interpretable. The Urdu principle at the end summarizes the conditions: free, sane, adult, Muslim, owner of nisab, complete ownership, passage of one year.

Key Terms
الزكاة (al-zakah): The obligatory charity due on specific wealth under specific conditions.
النصاب (al-nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to purchase his freedom.
اليتيم (al-yateem): An orphan, a child who has lost his father before puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the Shafi'i proof for zakat on orphan's wealth?
A) The hadith is weak in chain.
B) The hadith contradicts the Quran.
C) The hadith applies only to adults.
D) The hadith is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi exemption of minors from zakat is based on the principle of legal accountability (raf' al-qalam), and the Shafi'i position is a legitimate but opposed view.

Zakat — Almsgiving

Conditions for Zakat Obligation: The Hanafi Position and Shafi‘i Dispute
Opening ruling of Kitab al-Zakat listing conditions and supporting proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for zakat obligation in the Hanafi school, identify the three categories exempted by default, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding orphans' wealth.

Core Idea
Zakat is fard only on those with complete legal capacity and ownership; children, the insane, and mukatab slaves are exempt.

This lesson opens the Book of Zakat from al-Quduri's matn. The author lists the conditions that trigger the obligation of zakat, then explicitly excludes three categories. The commentary provides hadith proofs and contrasts with the Shafi'i school, which holds that orphans' wealth is subject to zakat. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate dalil and apply the Hanafi method of tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Zakat is declared fard (obligatory) upon qualifying individuals. Note that al-Quduri uses 'wajib' generically, but the Hanafi school treats it as fard due to qat'i evidence.
2
List the six conditions for obligation
The text states five: free, Muslim, sane, adult, and possessing nisab with complete ownership. A year passing (hawl) is the sixth condition stated separately.
These conditions are cumulative; all must be present for zakat to be wajib.
3
Identify the three exempted categories
The text explicitly exempts a child (sabi), an insane person (majnun), and a mukatab (slave contracting freedom). No zakat upon them even if nisab is owned.
4
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Four proofs are cited: hadith of Jabir (no zakat on mukatab), hadith of Ali (pen lifted from three), hadith of Ibn Abbas (no zakat on child's wealth until prayer obligatory), and saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.
The hadith of Ali is the strongest: 'raf' al-qalam' establishes lack of legal capacity.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-argument
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb where the Prophet commands guardians to trade with orphan's wealth lest charity consume it. This implies zakat is due on orphan's wealth.
6
Evaluate the Hanafi response and thamarah
The Hanafi response: the Shafi'i hadith does not explicitly order zakat; it encourages preserving wealth. The authentic and explicit hadith (raf' al-qalam) take precedence. The practical consequence is that Hanafi guardians do not pay zakat on orphan's wealth, while Shafi'i guardians must.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf resolved by tarjih based on strength of evidence.

Source Text

وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «لَا يَجِبُ عَلَى مَالِ الصَّغِيرِ زَكَاةً حَتَّى تَجِبَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ». (سنن الدار قطني، نمبر: 1981)

وجه: (١) دليل الشافعي الحديث لثبوت الزَّكَاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ خَطَبَ النَّاسَ فَقَالَ: «أَلَا مَنْ وَلِيَ يَتِيمًا لَهُ مَالٌ فَلْيَتَّجِرْ فِيهِ، وَلَا يَتْرُكْهُ حَتَّى تَأْكُلَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ» (الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ مَالِ الْيَتِيم، 641)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ عَلَى الْحَرِ الْمُسْلِمِ الْعَاقِلِ الْبَالِغ سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ قَالَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسِ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقٍ صَدَقَةٌ» (بخاري: بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْوَرِقِ،: 1447)

Book of Zakat. Zakat is obligatory upon the free, Muslim, sane, adult when he possesses a nisab with complete ownership and a year has passed over it. These are the conditions of obligation of zakat. And there is no zakat upon a child, nor an insane person, nor a mukatab. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that zakat is obligatory upon the free, Muslim, sane, adult: From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no zakat on the wealth of the mukatab until he is freed.' (2) The hadith... From Ali, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The pen is lifted from three: from the sleeper until he wakes, from the child until he reaches puberty, and from the insane until he regains sanity.' (3) The hadith... From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Zakat is not obligatory on the wealth of a child until prayer becomes obligatory upon him.' (4) The saying of the Tabi'i... From Ibrahim, he said: 'There is no zakat on the wealth of the orphan until he reaches puberty.' (1) The evidence of al-Shafi'i: the hadith... From Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) addressed the people and said: 'Indeed, whoever is in charge of an orphan's wealth, let him trade with it and not leave it until charity consumes it.' (2) The hadith... I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity on less than five camels, nor on less than five uqiyas, nor on less than five wasqs.' Principles: Zakat is an important pillar of Islam. In the Holy Quran, zakat is mentioned alongside prayer in approximately 80 places. Principles: Conditions for obligation of zakat: 1 free, 2 sane adult, 4 Muslim, 5 owner of nisab, 6 complete ownership of nisab, and a year passes over the wealth.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is the opening of Kitab al-Zakat (Book of Zakat) from al-Quduri's matn, followed by its commentary with hadith evidence and usul principles. The author first states the ruling: Zakat is wajib (obligatory) upon a person who meets five conditions: (1) free (not a slave), (2) Muslim, (3) sane, (4) adult (baligh), and (5) possesses a nisab (minimum threshold) with complete ownership, and (6) one lunar year has passed. Then he adds three categories upon whom zakat is not obligatory: a child (sabi), an insane person (majnun), and a mukatab (a slave who has contracted to purchase his freedom). The commentary then provides four pieces of evidence: (1) The hadith of Jabir that there is no zakat on the wealth of a mukatab until he is freed, implying that ownership is not complete. (2) The hadith of Ali that the pen of accountability is lifted from three: the sleeper, the child, and the insane, indicating that zakat is an act of worship requiring intention and capacity. (3) The hadith of Ibn Abbas that zakat is not obligatory on a child's wealth until prayer is obligatory upon him, linking obligation to puberty. (4) The saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, a prominent Tabi'i, that there is no zakat on an orphan's wealth until puberty. These support the Hanafi position. Then the text presents the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i: the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb where the Prophet commands guardians to trade with orphan's wealth lest charity consume it, implying zakat is due on it. This is a valid opposing dalil. Finally, the usul note in Urdu reiterates the conditions and emphasizes the importance of zakat. The Hanafi school responds that the hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb is weak in transmission or can be interpreted to mean that the guardian should trade to preserve the wealth, not that zakat is obligatory; the clear and authentic ahadtih take precedence. Thus, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that zakat is not obligatory on those lacking full legal capacity.

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers the obligation of zakat, as specified in the Shariah (e.g., 85g gold, 200 dirhams silver).
ملك تام (milk taamm): Complete ownership where the owner has full disposal over the wealth and it is not encumbered by debts or lack of legal capacity.
حول (hawl): The passage of one complete lunar year from the moment the nisab is acquired and held continuously.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted in writing with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments; his ownership is incomplete.
صبي (sabi): A child who has not reached puberty; legal obligations (taklif) do not apply.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person lacking intellectual capacity; the pen of accountability is lifted.
رفع القلم (raf' al-qalam): The lifting of the pen of accountability; meaning that such individuals are not subject to legal obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A child who owns nisab for a year

D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Zakat is only obligatory on those who are free, Muslim, sane, adult, and have complete ownership of nisab for a year; children, the insane, and mukatab slaves are exempt according to the Hanafi school, based on the principle of legal capacity (raf' al-qalam).

Effect of Debt on Zakat Obligation
Ruling on how debt affects zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi rule that zakat is due only on the surplus wealth after deducting immediate debts, and identify the proof from the saying of Caliph Uthman.

Core Idea
Debt cancels zakat on the portion of wealth it covers; only surplus qualifies if ≥ nisab.

This passage from al-Quduri addresses a practical financial question: does a person owe zakat on wealth that is partially or fully offset by debt? The ruling is clear: debts are deducted from total wealth, and zakat is due only on the surplus if it reaches the nisab threshold. The author supports this with a strong proof—the direct instruction of Caliph Uthman (radiAllahu anhu). This lesson will guide you through the ruling, its evidence, and the Hanafi rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is zakat obligation. The ruling states: if debt equals or exceeds wealth, no zakat; if wealth exceeds debt, zakat is due on the surplus after deducting debt, provided the surplus reaches nisab.
Zakat is fard 'ayn on the surplus, not on gross wealth.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites a saying (qawl) of Caliph Uthman in a sermon: 'Pay your debt first, then pay zakat on what remains.' This is a Companion saying, accepted as proof in Hanafi usul.
The proof is transmitted in Musannaf Abdurrazzaq and Muwatta Malik.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Uthman’s instruction to pay debt first implies that debt is a primary obligation that takes precedence over zakat. Zakat is only due on wealth that is free from debt, i.e., the surplus.
The imperative 'let him pay' indicates the ranking: debt first, then zakat on remainder.
4
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some Shafi'is hold that debts do not prevent zakat; one must pay zakat on total wealth and then pay debts. The Hanafi position prioritizes debt repayment.
The thamarah (practical difference) is whether zakat is due on gross or net wealth.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is strengthened by the Companion saying and the principle that zakat is due only on 'extra' (fadil) wealth. The mufta bihi is to deduct debts and pay zakat on the surplus.
Later Hanafi works generally uphold this view for immediate debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ يُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَالُهُ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ زَكَّى الْفَاضِلَ إِذَا بَلَغَ نِصَابًا
وجه: (١) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ يُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ سَمِعْتُ عُثْمَانَ يَخْطُبُ وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّ هَذَا شَهْرُ زَكَاتِكُمْ، فَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ فَلْيُؤَدِّهِ، ثُمَّ لِيُؤَدِّ زَكَاةَ مَا فَضَلَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق: بَابُ لَا زَكَاةَ إِلَّا فِي فَضْلِ: 7086 / موطأ إمام مالك: الزكوة في الدين: 284)
اصول: اولا قرض کو مال سے منہا کرنے کے بعد مال نصاب کے برابر ہو تو زکوۃ واجب ہے ورنہ نہیں.
And whoever has a debt that encompasses his wealth, then there is no zakat upon him. And if his wealth is more than the debt, he pays zakat on the surplus when it reaches nisab. Evidence: (1) The saying of the Companion to establish: 'And whoever has a debt that encompasses his wealth, there is no zakat upon him.' I heard Uthman giving a sermon saying: 'Indeed, this is your month of zakat. So whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then let him pay zakat on what remains.' (Mussanaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab La Zakat illa fi Fadl: 7086 / Muwatta Imam Malik, Zakat al-Dayn: 284) Principle: First, after deducting the debt from the wealth, if the remaining wealth equals nisab, then zakat is obligatory; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about the interaction of debt and zakat. The author states that if a person has debt that covers all his wealth (i.e., total debt equals or exceeds total assets), then no zakat is due. If the wealth exceeds the debt, then zakat is due on the surplus (al-fadil) provided it reaches the nisab threshold. The authority is a saying of Caliph Uthman (radiAllahu anhu) in a sermon, where he instructs people to first pay their debts and then pay zakat on the remainder. This is a practical directive from a Companion that aligns with the Hanafi principle that debts are considered a hindrance to zakat obligation because the debt effectively negates the 'complete ownership' condition. The usul note in Urdu reiterates: the debt is deducted from the wealth first; if the remainder equals nisab, zakat is obligatory; otherwise not. Note: This ruling applies to debts that are due and demandable (not deferred long-term loans). Also, if the debt does not encompass all wealth, only the surplus after debt is subject to zakat. The Hanafi position is that debts prevent zakat on wealth that is offset by the debt.

Key Terms
دين (dayn): A debt or financial liability that is due; the amount a person owes.
فاضل (fadil): Surplus; the remaining wealth after deducting all debts.
يحيط بماله (yuhitu bi malihi): Surrounds his wealth; meaning the debt covers or equals the total wealth.
قول الصحابي (qawl al-sahabi): The saying of a Companion of the Prophet (sahabi), considered a valid source of proof in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No zakat because debt covers part of wealth
B) Zakat is due on $10,000
C) Zakat is due on $7,000 (surplus after debt)
D) Zakat is due only on $3,000

Key Takeaway
Debts are deducted from total wealth before calculating zakat; the obligation applies only to the surplus if it reaches nisab.

Zakat Exemption for Essential Needs (Hawa'ij Asliyyah)
Ruling on items not subject to zakat due to being essential needs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six categories of items exempt from zakat and explain the hadith proofs that support their exemption.

Core Idea
Essential personal-use items are exempt from zakat even if they exceed nisab in value.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn lists specific categories of wealth that are not subject to zakat because they are considered essential needs (hawa'ij asliyyah). The Hanafi school firmly exempts residential houses, clothing, furniture, riding animals, servants, and weapons for personal use. The author cites four hadith to support this principle, including the famous hadith that the best charity is from surplus wealth. Understanding this exemption is crucial for correctly calculating one's zakat obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six exempt categories
Read the matn and list the six types of items mentioned: residential houses, body garments, household furniture, riding animals, service slaves, and weapons for use.
Note that these are all for personal use, not for trade.
2
Understand the concept of hawa'ij asliyyah
The principle is that wealth needed for basic living is not surplus and therefore not subject to zakat. The Urdu note in the passage summarizes: 'Zakat is not obligatory on items of basic needs.'
This is a distinct Hanafi concept; other schools may define surplus differently.
3
Analyze the four hadith proofs
Review each hadith and determine how it supports the exemption. The first hadith (Bukhari) emphasizes 'surplus wealth'; the second (Muslim) exempts slaves and horses; the third and fourth (Abu Dawud, Daraqutni) exempt working animals from zakat.
Each hadith reinforces that essential, non-productive assets are not zakatable.
4
Apply the condition: personal use vs. trade
The exemption holds only if the items are genuinely for personal use. If an item is converted to trade (e.g., buying a house explicitly to resell), it becomes zakatable. This condition is implicit in the term 'isti'mal' (use).
The principle of 'niyyah' (intention) is critical here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ وَأَثَاثِ الْمَنَازِلِ وَدَوَابِّ الرُّكُوبِ وَعَبِيدِ الْخِدْمَةِ وَسِلَاحِ الِاسْتِعْمَالِ زَكَاةً
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ سَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «خَيْرُ الصَّدَقَةِ مَا كَانَ عَنْ ظَهْرِ غِنًى، وَابْدَأْ بِمَنْ تَعُولُ» (بخاري: بَابُ لَا صَدَقَةَ إِلَّا عَنْ ظَهْرِ غِنًى، نمبر: 1426)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ فِي عَبْدِهِ وَلَا فَرَسِهِ صَدَقَةٌ» (مسلم شريف، لَا زَكَاةَ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ الخ، 982)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ أَحْسَبُهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «وَفِي الْبَقَرِ فِي كُلِّ ثَلَاثِينَ تَبِيعٌ، وَفِي الْأَرْبَعِينَ مُسِنَّةٌ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْعَوَامِلِ شَيْءٌ» (سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر: 1572)
وجه: (٤) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِي الْإِبِلِ الْعَوَامِلِ صَدَقَةٌ» (سنن الدار قطني: بَابُ ليس في العوامل صدقة، نمبر: 1921)
اصول: حوائج اصلیہ کی اشیاء میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔
And there is no zakat on residential houses, body garments, household furniture, riding animals, service slaves, and weapons for use. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing: 'And there is no zakat on residential houses and body garments.' Abu Hurairah (may Allah be pleased with him) heard the Prophet (peace be upon him) say: 'The best charity is that which is given from surplus wealth, and start with those whom you support.' (Bukhari, Bab La Sadaqata illa 'an Zahri Ghina, no. 1426) (2) The hadith... From Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no charity for a Muslim on his slave nor his horse.' (Muslim, no. 982) (3) The hadith... From Ali, Zuhair said: I think from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'And on cattle, for every thirty a tabi' (one-year-old), and for every forty a musinnah (two-year-old), and nothing on working animals.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab fi Zakat al-Sa'imah, no. 1572) (4) The hadith... From Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity on working camels.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1921) Principle: Zakat is not obligatory on items of basic needs (hawa'ij asliyyah).
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage lists specific categories of wealth that are not subject to zakat because they are considered essential needs (hawa'ij asliyyah). The author enumerates: (1) residential houses (dour al-sukna), (2) clothing for the body, (3) household furniture, (4) riding animals (dawabb al-rukub), (5) service slaves (jane servants), and (6) weapons for use. The commentary provides four hadith proofs: (a) The hadith of Abu Hurairah that the best charity is from surplus wealth (ghina) and one should start with dependents, implying that basic needs are not surplus and thus not zakatable. (b) The hadith that there is no sadaqah on a Muslim's slave or horse, indicating that items used for service or riding are exempt. (c) The hadith from Ali about cattle zakat, which specifically exempts working animals (al-'awamil) from zakat, analogically, other working tools are exempt. (d) The hadith about working camels, reaffirming the same principle. The usul note in Urdu summarizes: Zakat is not obligatory on items of basic needs (hawa'ij asliyyah). This is a fundamental Hanafi principle: wealth that is necessary for daily life and sustenance is not zakatable. The exemption applies regardless of the value, as long as the items are genuinely for personal use, not for trade.

Key Terms
حوائج أصليہ (hawa'ij asliyyah): Basic necessities of life, such as shelter, clothing, household items, transportation, servants, and tools for work.
دور السكنى (dour al-sukna): Houses used for residence, not rented out or intended for sale.
دواب الركوب (dawabb al-rukub): Riding animals used for personal transportation, not for trade or hire.
عوامل/عوامِل (awamil): Working animals used for ploughing, hauling, etc., not for their milk or meat as stock.
سلاح الاستعمال (silah al-isti'mal): Weapons kept for personal use (defense, hunting), not for trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following items would be exempt from zakat according to this passage?
A) A car used for personal commuting
B) A house rented out for income
C) Gold jewelry used for personal adornment (but note: Hanafi position on jewelry differs)
D) A horse used for racing as a business

Key Takeaway
Essential personal-use items (hawa'ij asliyyah) are exempt from zakat, supported by multiple hadith, as long as they are not used for trade.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Intention (Niyyah) Required for Zakat Payment
Ruling that intention is necessary when paying zakat, either at payment or at setting aside

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two valid times for making intention in zakat and explain the consequence of giving all wealth as charity without intending zakat.

Core Idea
Zakat requires intention; you may intend when paying or when setting aside.

This lesson establishes that intention (niyyah) is a condition for the validity of zakat payment. The Hanafi school allows making intention either at the time of payment or when setting aside the obligatory amount. The proof is the prophetic hadith 'actions are judged by intentions.' The passage also addresses a special case: if a person gives away all his wealth as voluntary charity without intending zakat, the obligation drops—but this is not a loophole to avoid zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying zakat. The ruling is that it is not valid (la yajuz) without intention. Intention is a condition (shart) for the payment.
Zakat is an act of worship; all acts of worship require intention in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' (actions are judged by intentions) reported by Umar ibn al-Khattab.
This hadith is mutawatir in meaning and considered qat'i in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith is general: every action is evaluated by its intention. Zakat is an action; therefore, it requires intention to determine that it is for zakat and not for voluntary charity.
This is a straightforward application of the general principle.
4
Analyze the subsidiary ruling
The text mentions: if someone gives all his wealth as sadaqah without intending zakat, the obligation drops (saqat). This is because the wealth is no longer in his possession.
This does not mean one can deliberately avoid zakat; it is a specific situation where the wealth is completely divested.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The operative position is that intention must be present at payment or at setting aside. Setting aside (azl) is a facilitation for gradual distribution.
The intention must accompany the act of setting aside or payment; it cannot be made earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ أَوْ مُقَارَنَةٍ لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ الْوَاجِبِ وَمَنْ تَصَدَّقَ بِجَمِيعِ مَالِهِ وَلَمْ يَنْوِ الزَّكَاةَ سَقَطَ عَنْهُ فَرْضُهَا
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ سَمِعْتُ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَلَى الْمِنْبَرِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ» (بخاري شريف: باب كيف كان بدء الوحي إلى رسول الله، نمبر: 1)
اصول: زکوۃ کی ادائیگی میں نیت ضروری ہے۔
And it is not permissible to pay zakat except with an intention that accompanies the payment or that accompanies the setting aside of the obligatory amount. And whoever gives all his wealth as charity and does not intend zakat, his obligation of zakat drops (is fulfilled). Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing: 'And it is not permissible to pay zakat except with intention.' I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) on the pulpit say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Verily, actions are (judged) by intentions.' (Bukhari: Bab Kayfa kana bad' al-wahy, no. 1) Principle: Intention is necessary in the payment of zakat.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage addresses the necessity of intention (niyyah) for zakat. The author states two valid times for making niyyah: (1) at the time of actual payment (ada'), (2) at the time of setting aside (azl) the obligatory amount. This is to facilitate those who may be paying gradually or setting money aside. The ruling also clarifies that if a person gives away all his wealth as sadaqah (voluntary charity) without specifically intending zakat, then the previous zakat obligation is lifted (saqat) because the wealth is gone and the obligation pertained to that wealth. However, this does not mean one can avoid zakat by giving charity; it is a specific situation where a person had not paid zakat yet, then gave away all wealth voluntarily without zakat intention — since the wealth is no longer in his possession, the zakat obligation on that wealth is dropped. But scholars caution that this should not be done deliberately to avoid zakat; the normal ruling is to pay zakat with intention. The proof is the famous hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' which establishes that the validity of deeds depends on intention. Since zakat is an act of worship (ibadah), it requires niyyah to distinguish it from mere charity. The usul note in Urdu confirms that intention is necessary in zakat payment.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform the act of worship; it distinguishes one act from another.
أداء (ada'): Payment; the act of giving zakat to the entitled recipients.
عزل (azl): Setting aside or isolating the obligatory amount of zakat from one's remaining wealth.
سقوط (suqut): Falling away; the obligation is lifted/dropped because the wealth is gone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must the intention (niyyah) for zakat be made according to this passage?
A) Only at the time of paying the zakat
B) Only at the time of setting aside the zakat money
C) Either at the time of payment or at the time of setting aside the obligatory amount
D) Intention is not required for zakat

Key Takeaway
Intention is essential for zakat; it can be made at payment or at setting aside; giving all wealth as charity drops the obligation but does not fulfill zakat.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Zakat: Debt Deduction, Exempt Assets, and Requirement of Intention
Matn from al-Quduri on zakat rulings with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings on zakat: deduct all debts before assessing zakat, exempt hawa'ij asliyyah (essential assets) from zakat, and require niyyah concurrent with payment or setting aside.

Core Idea
Debt first, then zakat on surplus; essential assets are exempt; intention is required.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn on zakat establishes three foundational principles of Hanafi zakat law. First, if a person has debt equal to or exceeding their wealth, no zakat is due; otherwise, zakat is obligatory on the surplus after debt, provided it reaches the nisab. Second, essential personal assets—such as one's home, clothing, furniture, riding animal, domestic servants, and personal weapons—are not subject to zakat. Third, the payment of zakat must be accompanied by the intention (niyyah) to fulfil the obligation, either at the time of payment or when setting aside the amount. These rulings are supported by hadith, including the statement of Uthman on the minbar, and usul principles that clarify the priority of debt and the scope of exempt property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three distinct rulings
Read the matn and separate the passage into three sections: (1) debt and zakat, (2) exempt assets, (3) necessity of niyyah. Note the precise wording of each ruling as a memorization anchor.
The matn uses 'wa man kana alayhi dayn...' for debt, 'wa laysa fi dur al-sukna...' for exempt assets, and 'wa la yajuzu ada al-zakat illa bi niyyah...' for niyyah.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For the debt ruling, identify the proof (athar of Uthman). For exempt assets, note the multiple hadith: Abu Hurayra on 'charity from surplus', Abu Hurayra on no sadaqah on slave/horse, Ali on no zakat on working cattle, Amr ibn Shu'ayb on working camels. For niyyah, the hadith of Umar: 'Actions are but by intentions.'
The text labels each proof as 'wajh (1)', etc. This scaffolding helps you link each ruling to its specific evidence.
3
Understand the Hanafi usul principles
Note the usul notes in Urdu: 'hawa'ij asliyyah ki ashya mein zakat wajib nahi hai' and 'qarz ko maal se munha karne ke baad maal nisab ke barabar ho to zakat wajib hai warna nahi'. These principles are the underlying legal maxims: (a) basic needs are exempt, (b) debt is subtracted before assessing nisab.
These principles are transmitted through the Zahir al-Riwayah and are binding in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the debt ruling to a concrete scenario
Take a scenario: A person has 50,000 in total wealth but owes 30,000 in debt. After deducting debt, surplus is 20,000. If this surplus reaches the nisab (e.g., 20 mithqal gold: roughly 85g), then zakat is wajib on the 20,000. If debt were 50,000 or more, no zakat.
This illustrates the Hanafi position that debt is a prior claim on wealth, unlike some other schools.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
Note that the Shafi'i school does not deduct debts that are not due within the year. This means a Shafi'i may pay zakat on the full wealth even if long-term debts exist. Understand that the Hanafi position is based on the hadith of Uthman and the principle that debt prevents the full ownership (milk tamm) required for zakat.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is significant: a Hanafi may pay less zakat or none at all in a given year compared to a Shafi'i with the same assets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الزَّكَاةِ
وَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنْ يُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ مَالُهُ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ الدَّيْنِ زَكَّى الْفَاضِلَ إِذَا بَلَغَ نِصَابًا ٣ وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ وَأَثَاثِ الْمَنَازِلِ وَدَوَاتِ الرَّكُوبِ وَعَبِيدِ الْخِدْمَةِ وَسِلَاحِ الِاسْتِعْمَالِ زَكَاةً : وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ أَوْ مُقَارَنَةٍ لِعَزْلِ مِقْدَارِ الْوَاجِبِ وَمَنْ تَصَدَّقَ بِجَمِيعِ مَالِهِ وَلَمْ يَنْوِ الزَّكَاةَ سَقَطَ عَنْهُ فَرْضُهَا
. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ يُحِيطُ بِمَالِهِ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ \ سَمِعْتُ عُثْمَانَ يَخْطُبُ وَهَوَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّ هَذَا شَهْرُ زَكَاتِكُمْ، فَمَنْ كَانَ عَلَيْهِ دَيْنٌ فَلْيُؤَدِّهُ، ثُمَّ لِيُؤَدِ زَكَاةَ مَا فَضَلَ» (مصنف عبد الرزاق : بَابُ لَا زَكَاةَ إِلا فِي فَضْلِ : 7086/ مؤطا إمام مالك: الزكوة في الدين: 284) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ \ سَمِعَ أَبَا هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «خَيْرُ الصَّدَقَةِ مَا كَانَ عَنْ ظَهْرِ غِيَّ، وَابْدَأْ بِمَنْ تَعُولُ» (بخاري : بَابُ لاَ صَدَقَةَ إِلَّا عَنْ ظَهْرِ غِنِّى، نمبر: 1426)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ إِن رسول الله قال: ليس على المسلم في عبده ولا فرسه صدقة (مسلم شريف ، لا زَكَاةَ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِ الخ، 982) وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ \ عَنْ عَلِي ، - قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ : أَحْسَبُهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ قَالَ ...... قَالَ: «وَفِي الْبَقَرِ فِي كُل ثَلَاثِينَ تَبِيعٌ، وَفِي الْأَرْبَعِينَ مُسِنَّةٌ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْعَوَامِلِ شَيْءٌ» ، سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1572)
وجه:(۴) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي دُورِ السُّكْنَى وَثِيَابِ الْبَدَنِ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ, عَنْ أبِيهِ, عَنْ جَدِهِ, عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِي الْإِبِلِ الْعَوَامِلِ صَدَقَةٌ» . (سنن الدار قطني : بَابُ ليس في العوامل صدقة، نمبر: 1921) توجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَدَاءُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَّا بِنِيَّةٍ مُقَارِنَةٍ لِلْأَدَاءِ \ سَمِعْتُ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَلَى الْمِنْبَرِ قَالَ : سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ، (بخاري شريف: باب كيف كان بدء الوحي إلى رسول الله، نمبر: 1)
اصول : حوائج اصلیہ کی اشیاء میں زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے۔ اصول : اولا قرض کو مال سے منہا کرنے کے بعد مال نصاب کے برابر ہو تو زکوۃ واجب ہے ورنہ نہیں ۔
The Book of Zakat. Whoever has a debt that encompasses all his wealth, there is no zakat upon him. If his wealth is more than the debt, he gives zakat on the surplus when it reaches the nisab (3). There is no zakat in dwellings for residence, clothes for the body, household furniture, riding animals, slaves for service, and arms for use. It is not permissible to pay zakat except with an intention concurrent with payment or concurrent with setting aside the obligatory amount. Whoever gives in charity all his wealth without intending zakat, the obligation of zakat falls from him. Proof (1): Statement of the Companion for establishing: 'Whoever has a debt encompassing his wealth, there is no zakat upon him.' I heard Uthman giving a sermon saying: 'This is the month of your zakat, so whoever has a debt, let him pay it, then pay zakat on what remains.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: Chapter of No Zakat Except on Surplus: 7086/Muwatta Imam Malik: Zakat on Debt: 284) Proof (1) (sic): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no zakat in dwellings for residence and clothes for the body.' He heard Abu Hurayra from the Prophet (PBUH): 'The best charity is what is given from surplus wealth, and start with those you support.' (Bukhari: Chapter of No Charity Except from Surplus, no. 1426) Proof (2): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no zakat in dwellings for residence and clothes for the body.' From Abu Hurayra: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no sadaqah upon a Muslim for his slave or his horse.' (Muslim: No Zakat on the Muslim..., 982) Proof (3): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no zakat in dwellings...' From Ali (Zuhayr said I think from the Prophet) that he said: 'In cattle, for every thirty a one-year-old, for every forty a two-year-old, and there is nothing on working animals.' (Abu Dawood: Chapter on Zakat of Pasturing Animals, no. 1572) Proof (4): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no zakat in dwellings...' From Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, from the Prophet: 'There is no sadaqah on working camels.' (Dar Qutni: Chapter of No Zakat on Working Animals, no. 1921) Proof (1) (again) for establishing: 'It is not permissible to pay zakat except with intention concurrent with payment.' I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab on the pulpit say: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Actions are but by intentions.' (Bukhari: Chapter of How Revelation Began, no. 1). Principles: Zakat is not obligatory on items of basic needs. Principles: First, after deducting debt from wealth, if the remaining wealth equals the nisab, then zakat is obligatory, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Kitab al-Zakat of al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi matn. It presents three connected rulings: (1) Regarding debt: If a person has a debt that completely covers his wealth, no zakat is due. If his wealth exceeds the debt, he must pay zakat on the surplus provided it reaches the nisab. This follows the Hanafi principle that debt is deducted from wealth before assessing zakat obligation. (2) Regarding exempt assets: No zakat is due on essential personal items such as houses for residence, clothing, household furniture, riding animals, domestic servants, and weapons for personal use. These are considered hawa'ij asliyyah (basic needs). (3) Regarding intention: Zakat payment requires an intention (niyyah) that is either simultaneous with the payment or with setting aside the zakat amount. If someone gives away all his wealth as general charity without specifically intending zakat, the zakat obligation is not fulfilled. The passage then provides hadith and athar proofs for these rulings: the statement of Uthman for the debt ruling, the hadith of Abu Hurayra about surplus wealth for exempt items, and the hadith of Umar about intentions for the requirement of niyyah. Additional proofs from Abu Hurayra (no zakat on slave or horse), Ali (no zakat on working cattle), and Amr ibn Shu'ayb (no zakat on working camels) support the exemption of essential assets. The Urdu usul notes reiterate the principles: zakat is not on basic needs, and debt is deducted before assessing nisab.

Key Terms
دَيْن (dayn): Debt owed by the zakat payer; it is deducted from total wealth before assessing zakat obligation.
نِصَاب (nisab): The minimum threshold of wealth that triggers zakat obligation; for gold it is 20 mithqal, for silver 200 dirhams, etc.
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intention; required for zakat payment to be valid; must be concurrent with payment or setting aside the amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi matn, when is a person exempt from zakat due to debt?
A) When the person has any debt at all, regardless of amount.
B) When the debt equals or exceeds the total wealth.
C) When the debt is more than the nisab but less than total wealth.
D) When the person has no intention to pay zakat.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat is due only on surplus wealth after deducting all debts, essential personal items are exempt, and a specific intention at the time of payment is required.

Zakat on Camels: Nisab, Schedule, and Conditions
Matn from al-Quduri detailing zakat schedule for camels with hadith proofs and condition of sa'imah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab thresholds for zakat on camels according to the Hanafi madhhab, identify the type of animal due at each bracket, and explain the condition of sa'imah.

Core Idea
Zakat on camels is wajib only on sa'imah (pasturing) camels when owning 5 or more and a full year passes.

Zakat on camels is a fixed obligation with a detailed schedule based on the number owned. This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents the nisab thresholds and the corresponding zakat animals, along with the key conditions of sa'imah and the passing of one lunar year (hawl). Understanding this schedule is essential for correctly fulfilling this pillar of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab and its conditions
The text begins by stating the minimum: no zakat below 5 camels. Conditions: camels must be sa'imah (pasturing) and a full lunar year must have passed. Focus on these three conditions as prerequisites.
The nisab for camels is 5; below that no zakat is due.
2
Memorize the zakat schedule bracket by bracket
The passage lists each range and the specific animal due. Break it down: 5-9 camels → 1 sheep; 10-14 → 2 sheep; 15-19 → 3 sheep; 20-24 → 4 sheep; 25-35 → bint makhad (1-year she-camel); 36-45 → bint labun (2-year); 46-60 → hiqqah (3-year); 61-75 → jadha'ah (4-year); 76-90 → two bint labun; 91-120 → two hiqqah. Beyond 120, for every 50 a hiqqah, for every 40 a bint labun.
Use this table to see the pattern clearly.
3
Understand the terminology of zakat animals
Each animal name corresponds to a specific age and type. Bint makhad = 1-year she-camel, bint labun = 2-year, hiqqah = 3-year, jadha'ah = 4-year. These are standard Hanafi terms.
The ages are approximate; the key is knowing the sequence.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs provided
Three hadith are cited: (1) Bahz ibn Hakim: 'For every forty pasturing camels, a bint labun'; (2) Abu Bakr's letter: details the thresholds including sheep and camels; (3) Salim's narration: the full schedule from the Prophet's document. Note the chains and authority.
These hadith establish the schedule and the sa'imah condition.
5
Apply the schedule to a hypothetical camel count
Given a number of camels, locate the bracket and find the due animal. For example, 30 camels: 25-35 bracket → bint makhad. 80 camels: 76-90 → two bint labun. 150 camels: beyond 120 → for every 50 a hiqqah (3 hiqqahs) and for every 40 a bint labun (3 bint labuns and remainder).
Practice with various numbers to internalize the schedule.

Source Text

بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْإِبِل
ل لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْس ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ خَمْسًا سَائِمَةً وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الحَوْلُ فَفِيهَا شَاةٌ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتُ فَخَاضٍ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِنَّا وَثَلَاثِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتُ لَبُونٍ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِرًّا وَأَرْبَعِينَ فَفِيهَا حِقَّةٌ إِلَى سِتِّينَ وَإِذَا كَانَتْ إِحْدَى وَسِتِّينَ فَفِيهَا جَذَعَةٌ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَسَبْعِينَ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِرًّا وَسَبْعِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتَا لَبُونٍ إِلَى تِسْعِينَ
لوجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ \ سَمِعْتُ بَهْزَ بْنَ حَكِيمٍ يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنْ جَدِهِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «فِي كُلِ إِبِلِ سَائِمَةٍ مِنْ كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ ابْنَةُ لَبُون سنن نسائی باببَابُ سُقُوطِ الزَّكَاةِ عَنِ الْإِبِلِ إِذَا كَانَتْ رُسُلًا لِأَهْلِهَا وَحِمُولَتِهِمْ نمبر 2449 /سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1557)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ \ «أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ ، كَتَبَ لَهُ هَذَا الْكِتَابَ لَمَّا وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْبَحْرَيْنِ : بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ هَذِهِ فَرِيضَةُ الصَّدَقَةِ، الَّتِي فَرَضَ رَسُولُ الله عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ ...... فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سَائِمَةُ الرَّجُلِ نَاقِصَةً مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً وَاحِدَةً، فَلَيْسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ رَبُّهَا (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ ، نمبر 1454 /سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1567)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ \ عَنْ سَالِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَتَبَ كِتَابَ الصَّدَقَةِ، فَلَمْ يُخْرِجْهُ إِلَى عُمَّالِهِ حَتَّى قُبِضَ ، فَقَرَنَهُ بِسَيْفِهِ، فَلَمَّا قُبِضَ عَمِلَ بِهِ أَبُو بَكْرٍ حَتَّى قُبِضَ، وَعُمَرُ حَتَّى قُبِضَ، وَكَانَ فِيهِ: فِي خَمْسِ مِنَ الإِبِلِ شَاةٌ ، وَفِي عَشْرِشَاتَانِ، وَفِي خَمْسَ عَشْرَةَ ثَلَاثُ شِيَاهِ، وَفِي عِشْرِينَ أَرْبَعُ شِيَاهِ، وَفِي خَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ بِنْتُ فَخَاضٍ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ ، فَإِذَازَادَتْ فَفِيهَا ابْنَةُ لَبُونِ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا حِقَّةٌ إِلَى سِيِّينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا جَذَعَةٌ إِلَى خَمْس وَسَبْعِينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا ابْنَتَالَبُونِ إِلَى تِسْعِينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا حِقَّتَانِ إِلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ فَفِي كُلِ خَمْسِينَ حِقَّةٌ، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ ابْنَةُ لَبُونٍ،
(سن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ الإِبِلِ وَالغَنَمِ 621 / ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، 1570) اصول: زکوۃ صرف ان جانوروں میں واجب ہو گی جو سال کا اکثر حصہ چرتے ہوں اور کچھ حصہ گھر پر بھی کھالیتے ہوں، پھر ان پر سال مکمل گذر جائے۔
Chapter of Zakat on Camels. There is no sadaqah in less than five camels. If they are five pasture camels (sa'imah) and a year has passed, then a sheep is due. When it reaches twenty-five, a bint makhad (one-year-old she-camel) is due. When it reaches thirty-six, a bint labun (two-year-old she-camel) is due up to forty-five. When it reaches forty-six, a hiqqah (three-year-old she-camel) is due up to sixty. When it becomes sixty-one, a jadha'ah (four-year-old she-camel) is due up to seventy-five. When it reaches seventy-six, two bint labun are due up to ninety. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no sadaqah in less than five camels.' I heard Bahz ibn Hakim narrating from his father from his grandfather: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'For every pasturing camel, from every forty, a bint labun.' (Sunan Nasa'i: Chapter on Dropping Zakat from Camels Used for Carrying, no. 2449 / Abu Dawood: Chapter on Zakat of Pasturing Animals, no. 1557) Proof (2): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no sadaqah in less than five camels.' That Abu Bakr wrote this document when he sent him to Bahrain: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. This is the obligatory sadaqah that the Messenger of Allah prescribed upon the Muslims... If a man's pasturing sheep is short by one from forty, then there is no sadaqah on them unless their owner wishes. (Bukhari: Chapter of Zakat on Sheep, no. 1454 / Abu Dawood: Chapter on Zakat of Pasturing Animals, no. 1567) Proof (3): Hadith for establishing: 'There is no sadaqah in less than five camels.' From Salim, from his father, that the Messenger of Allah wrote a document of sadaqah but did not send it to his agents until he passed away. He attached it to his sword. When he died, Abu Bakr acted upon it until he died, then Umar. It contained: For five camels, a sheep; for ten, two sheep; for fifteen, three sheep; for twenty, four sheep; for twenty-five, a bint makhad until thirty-five; when more, a bint labun up to forty-five; when more, a hiqqah up to sixty; when more, a jadha'ah up to seventy-five; when more, two bint labun up to ninety; when more, two hiqqah up to one hundred twenty; when more than one hundred twenty, for every fifty a hiqqah, and for every forty a bint labun. (Tirmidhi: Chapter on Zakat of Camels and Sheep, no. 621 / Abu Dawood: Chapter on Zakat of Pasturing Animals, no. 1570) Principle: Zakat will be obligatory only on those animals that graze for most of the year and also eat some portion at home, and then a full year passes over them.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from Bab Zakat al-Ibil of al-Quduri, detailing the zakat schedule for camels. The matn establishes the nisab thresholds and the specific animals due at each bracket. Key conditions: the camels must be sa'imah (pasturing animals that graze freely for most of the year) and a full lunar year must have passed (hawl). The schedule: 5-9 camels → 1 sheep; 10-14 → 2 sheep; 15-19 → 3 sheep; 20-24 → 4 sheep; 25-35 → bint makhad (1-year-old she-camel); 36-45 → bint labun (2-year-old); 46-60 → hiqqah (3-year-old); 61-75 → jadha'ah (4-year-old); 76-90 → two bint labun; 91-120 → two hiqqah; beyond 120, for every 50 a hiqqah, for every 40 a bint labun. The passage then provides three hadith proofs: (1) The hadith of Bahz ibn Hakim that zakat is on every 40 sa'imah camels, (2) the document of Abu Bakr on zakat thresholds including sheep and camels, (3) the detailed schedule from the Prophet's written document as transmitted by Salim. The Urdu usul note clarifies the condition of sa'imah: the animals must graze for most of the year (even if supplemented at home) for zakat to be wajib.

Key Terms
سَائِمَة (sa'imah): Pasturing livestock that graze freely for most of the year; zakat is only wajib on sa'imah animals.
بِنْتُ مَخَاض (bint makhad): A one-year-old she-camel; the zakat due for camels between 25-35.
بِنْتُ لَبُون (bint labun): A two-year-old she-camel; the zakat due for camels between 36-45 and also 76-90.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Zakat on camels is wajib on sa'imah camels at a nisab of 5, with a detailed schedule of animal dues that increases in age and number as the herd grows.

Zakat on Camels: Thresholds and Rates (5–120+)
Ruling on zakat of camels with thresholds and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the zakat thresholds for camels from 5 to 120 and beyond, and explain the Hadith proofs that establish them.

Core Idea
Zakat on camels begins at 5 and rises at specific thresholds, with a restart after 120.

This lesson walks through the classical Hanafi ruling on zakat of camels as presented in Al-Quduri. You will learn the exact animal due at each bracket (e.g., sheep, bint makhad, hiqqa) and the evidence from the Prophet's sunnah. Understanding these thresholds is foundational for calculating zakat on livestock today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab
The text states there is no zakat on less than five camels. Locate this statement and note the condition of sa'ima and hawl.
The nisab is 5 camels; below that no zakat.
2
List the thresholds from 5 to 120
Work through the text: at 5: one sheep; at 25: bint makhad; at 36: bint labun; at 46: hiqqa; at 61: jadha'a; at 76: two bint labun; at 91: two hiqqa up to 120.
Use the commentary to confirm the ages of the camels.
3
Understand the restart rule
After 120, the fard restarts: for every 40 a bint labun, for every 50 a hiqqa. See how the text handles numbers above 120.
This is a distinct Hanafi position.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
The text cites multiple hadith. Identify the key narrator and main content in the proof for each threshold.
The proofs include the letter of Abu Bakr and hadith of Bahz ibn Hakim.
5
Apply the ruling to Bukht and Irab camels
Note the equal treatment: both types (two-humped and one-humped) share the same zakat rates.
The text explicitly states 'al-bukht wa al-i'rab sawa'un'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْإِبِل
لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ خَمْسًا سَائِمَةً وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الحَوْلُ فَفِيهَا شَاةٌ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ خَمْسًا وَعِشْرِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتُ مَخَاضٍ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِتًّا وَثَلَاثِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتُ لَبُونٍ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِتًّا وَأَرْبَعِينَ فَفِيهَا حِقَّةٌ إِلَى سِتِّينَ وَإِذَا كَانَتْ إِحْدَى وَسِتِّينَ فَفِيهَا جَذَعَةٌ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَسَبْعِينَ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ سِتًّا وَسَبْعِينَ فَفِيهَا بِنْتَا لَبُونٍ إِلَى تِسْعِينَ فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ إِحْدَى وَتِسْعِينَ فَفِيهَا حِقَّتَانِ إِلَى مِائَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ ثُمَّ يَسْتَأْنِفُ الْفَرِيضَةَ : فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ وَالْبُخْتُ وَالْعِرَابُ سَوَاءٌ
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ سَمِعْتُ بَهْزَ بْنَ حَكِيمٍ يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «فِي كُلِّ إِبِلٍ سَائِمَةٍ مِنْ كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ ابْنَةُ لَبُونٍ» (سنن نسائي، بَابُ سُقُوطِ الزَّكَاةِ عَنِ الْإِبِلِ إِذَا كَانَتْ رُسُلًا لِأَهْلِهَا وَحِمُولَتِهِمْ، نمبر 2449 / سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1557)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ ، كَتَبَ لَهُ هَذَا الْكِتَابَ لَمَّا وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْبَحْرَيْنِ : بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ هَذِهِ فَرِيضَةُ الصَّدَقَةِ، الَّتِي فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللهِ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ ...... فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سَائِمَةُ الرَّجُلِ نَاقِصَةً مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً وَاحِدَةً، فَلَيْسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ رَبُّهَا (بخاري شريف، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ، نمبر 1454 / سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1567)
وجه : (٣) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ عَنْ سَالِمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَتَبَ كِتَابَ الصَّدَقَةِ، فَلَمْ يُخْرِجْهُ إِلَى عُمَّالِهِ حَتَّى قُبِضَ ، فَقَرَنَهُ بِسَيْفِهِ، فَلَمَّا قُبِضَ عَمِلَ بِهِ أَبُو بَكْرٍ حَتَّى قُبِضَ، وَعُمَرُ حَتَّى قُبِضَ، وَكَانَ فِيهِ: فِي خَمْسٍ مِنَ الإِبِلِ شَاةٌ ، وَفِي عَشْرٍ شَاتَانِ، وَفِي خَمْسَ عَشْرَةَ ثَلَاثُ شِيَاهٍ، وَفِي عِشْرِينَ أَرْبَعُ شِيَاهٍ، وَفِي خَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ بِنْتُ مَخَاضٍ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا ابْنَةُ لَبُونٍ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا حِقَّةٌ إِلَى سِتِّينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا جَذَعَةٌ إِلَى خَمْسٍ وَسَبْعِينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا ابْنَتَا لَبُونٍ إِلَى تِسْعِينَ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ فَفِيهَا حِقَّتَانِ إِلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ، فَإِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ فَفِي كُلِّ خَمْسِينَ حِقَّةٌ، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ ابْنَةُ لَبُونٍ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ الإِبِلِ وَالْغَنَمِ، نمبر 621 / سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1570)
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ فَفِي كُلِّ خَمْسِينَ حِقَّةٌ، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ ابْنَةُ لَبُونٍ (سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ الإِبِلِ وَالْغَنَمِ، نمبر 621 / سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1570)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ خَمْسِينَ وَمِائَةً، فَفِيهَا ثَلَاثُ حِقَاقٍ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ تِسْعًا وَخَمْسِينَ وَمِائَةً، فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سِتِّينَ وَمِائَةً، فَفِيهَا أَرْبَعُ بَنَاتِ لَبُونٍ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ تِسْعًا وَسِتِّينَ وَمِائَةً، فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سَبْعِينَ وَمِائَةً، فَفِيهَا ثَلَاثُ بَنَاتِ لَبُونٍ وَحِقَّةٌ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ تِسْعًا وَسَبْعِينَ وَمِائَةً) (سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1570)
وجه : (٣) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ أَعَنْ عَلِيٍّ، قَالَ: «إِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ يَسْتَقْبِلُ بِمَا الْفَرِيضَةَ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، مَنْ قَالَ: إِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ اسْتَقْبَلَ بِمَا الْفَرِيضَةَ، نمبر 9911)
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ حَدَّثَنَا حَمَّادٌ، قَالَ: أَخَذْتُ مِنْ ثُمَامَةَ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَنَسٍ كِتَابًا ، زَعَمَ أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ كَتَبَهُ لِأَنَسٍ، وَعَلَيْهِ خَاتِمُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم حِينَ بَعَثَهُ مُصَدِّقًا ...... فَإِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ، فَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ بِنْتُ لَبُونٍ، وَفِي كُلِّ خَمْسِينَ حِقَّةٌ (سنن أبي داود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1567 / بخاري شريف، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ، نمبر 1454)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَفِي الْخَمْسِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْعَشْرِ شَاتَانِ أَبِي بَكْرِ بْنِ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَمْرِو بْنِ حَزْمٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ .... تَبْلُغَ عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةً، فَإِذَا كَانَتْ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَعُدَّ فِي كُلِّ خَمْسِينَ حِقَّةً وَمَا فَضَلَ فَإِنَّهُ يُعَادُ إِلَى أَوَّلِ فَرِيضَةِ الْإِبِلِ، وَمَا كَانَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ فَفِيهِ الْغَنَمُ فِي كُلِّ خَمْسِ ذَوْدٍ شَاةٌ (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ ذِكْرِ رِوَايَةِ عَاصِمِ بْنِ ضَمْرَةَ عَنْ ...، نمبر 7268 / مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، مَنْ قَالَ: إِذَا زَادَتْ عَلَى عِشْرِينَ وَمِائَةٍ اسْتَقْبَلَ بِمَا الْفَرِيضَةَ، نمبر 9911)
اصول: زکوۃ صرف ان جانوروں میں واجب ہو گی جو سال کا اکثر حصہ چرتے ہوں اور کچھ حصہ گھر پر بھی کھالیتے ہوں، پھر ان پر سال مکمل گذر جائے۔ زکوۃ کا حکم، بختی اور عربی کے لیے یکساں ہے کیونکہ دونوں کو اونٹ ہی کہا جاتا ہے۔ (عرب میں اونٹ کی دو قسمیں ہوتی ہیں : بختی، جو کہ چھوٹا ہوتا ہے، اور دوسرا عربی، جو اونچے قد کا ہوتا ہے۔)
Chapter of Zakat of Camels. There is no sadaqah in less than five camels. If they are five, grazing (sa'ima), and a year has passed, then in them is one sheep. Then when they reach twenty-five, in them is a bint makhad (one-year-old she-camel). Then when they reach thirty-six, in them is a bint labun (two-year-old she-camel) up to forty-five. Then when they reach forty-six, in them is a hiqqa (three-year-old she-camel) up to sixty. Then when they become sixty-one, in them is a jadha'a (four-year-old she-camel) up to seventy-five. Then when they reach seventy-six, in them are two bint labun up to ninety. Then when they reach ninety-one, in them are two hiqqa up to one hundred twenty. Then the fard (obligation) recommences: in five is one sheep, in ten is two sheep, until the end. And the Bukht and Irab (crossbred and purebred) are equal. [Then hadith proofs and usul notes in Urdu.]
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is the ruling (hukm) on zakat of camels from the matn of Al-Quduri, followed by multiple hadith proofs and a brief usul explanation. The matn states the minimum nisab for camels is five; from 5 to 24 camels, the zakat is one sheep (or goat). The rates increase at specific thresholds: at 25 camels, a bint makhad (one-year-old she-camel); at 36, a bint labun (two-year-old); at 46, a hiqqa (three-year-old); at 61, a jadha'a (four-year-old); at 76, two bint labun; at 91, two hiqqa. This continues up to 120 camels. Beyond 120, the obligation 'restarts' (yasta'niful fariḍa), meaning that for every 40 camels a bint labun is due, and for every 50 a hiqqa, with the remainder following the lower thresholds. The author clarifies that both Bukht (two-humped, smaller) and Arab (one-humped, larger) camels are treated equally for zakat. The hadith proofs are cited from various sources, including the famous letter of Abu Bakr and the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ), confirming these thresholds. The usul note in Urdu adds conditions for zakat: the animals must be sa'ima (grazing for most of the year) and the full year (hawl) must pass. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the evidence, then the juristic principle.

Key Terms
سَائِمَة (sa'ima): Livestock that graze on natural pasture for most of the year, as opposed to being stall-fed.
بِنْتُ مَخَاض (bint makhad): A female camel that has entered its second year (one year old).
حِقَّة (hiqqa): A female camel that has entered its fourth year (three years old).
بُخْت (bukht): A type of camel with two humps, smaller in size, common in Central Asia.
عِرَاب (i'rab): Purebred Arab camels with one hump, larger in size.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At what number of camels does the zakat obligation begin according to the Hanafi school?
A) 1 camel
B) 5 camels
C) 10 camels
D) 25 camels

Key Takeaway
Zakat on camels is a graded obligation with specific thresholds from 5 to 120, after which the schedule restarts.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Basic Nisab and Obligation for Zakat on Cows
States the minimum nisab and obligatory zakat for 30 and 40 cows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for zakat on cows and identify the obligatory animal for 30 and 40 cows, citing the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Zakat on cows begins at 30; at 30 a one-year-old calf, at 40 a two-year-old calf.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule for zakat on cows from Imam al-Quduri's matn. You will learn the minimum number (nisab) that triggers the obligation, the specific animals due at 30 and 40 cows, and the conditions of pasture-feeding and passage of one year. The lesson also presents the prophetic evidence that establishes these rulings, anchoring the memorization of this important financial obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving zakat (sadaqah) from cows. The ruling is wajib when conditions are met.
Zakat is fard in general, but this specific obligation is wajib due to ahad hadith proof.
2
List the conditions for obligation
Three conditions: nisab of at least 30 cows, cows must be pasture-fed (sa'imah), and a full lunar year (hawl) must pass.
3
State the nisab thresholds and due animals
At 30 cows: one tabi' (1-year-old male or female calf). At 40 cows: one musinn (2-year-old male or female calf).
If the herd number is between 30 and 40, the ruling remains the same as for 30.
4
Recall the hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: one from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and one from Mu'adh ibn Jabal (via Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud). Both state the same obligations.
These are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut) but their meaning is clear (qati al-dalala), which in Hanafi usul establishes wujub.
5
Define key terms
Tabi'/tabi'ah: calf that has completed one year. Musinn/musinnah: calf that has completed two years. Sa'imah: cows that graze freely for most of the year.
These definitions are essential for correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَدَقَةِ الْبَقَرِ
لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ ثَلَاثِينَ مِنْ الْبَقَرِ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ ثَلَاثِينَ سَائِمَةً وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْحَوْلُ فَفِيهَا تَبِيعُ أَوْ تَبِيعَةٌ وَفِي أَرْبَعِينَ مُسِنٌ أَوْ مُسِنَّةٌ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ ثَلَاثِينَ مِنْ الْبَقَرِ صَدَقَةٌ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، قَالَ: «فِي ثَلَاثِينَ مِنَ البَقَرِ تَبِيعٌ أَوْ تَبِيعَةٌ، وَفِي كُلِ أَرْبَعِينَ مُسِنَّةٌ» (سن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ في زَكَاةِ البَقَرِ، نمبر (622)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ ثَلَاثِينَ مِنْ الْبَقَرِ صَدَقَةٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي وَائِلٍ، عَنْ مُعَادٍ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَمَّا وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَ مِنَ الْبَقَرِ مِنْ كُلِّ ثَلَاثِينَ تَبِيعًا، أَوْ تَبِيعَةً، وَمِنْ كُل أَرْبَعِينَ مُسِنَّةَ، وَمِنْ كُلِّ حَالِم يَعْنِي مُحْتَلِمًا دِينَارًا، أَوْ عَدْلَهُ مِنَ المَعَافِرِ ثِيَابٌ تَكُونُ بِالْيَمَنِ (سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1576/ سن ،ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ البَقَرِ، نمبر 623)
لغت : تبيع ، تبيعة : گائے کا بچہ جسکی عمر ایک سال سے متجاوز ہو، خواہ ایک دن ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
مُسِنٌ، مُسئَةٌ : گائے کا بچہ جسکی عمر دو سال سے متجاوز ہو ، خواہ ایک دن ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔
Chapter of Zakat on Cows. There is no sadaqah (zakat) on less than thirty cows. So when they are thirty, pasture-fed, and one year has passed over them, then in them is a tabi' or tabi'ah (one-year-old male or female). And in forty (cows) is a musinn or musinnah (two-year-old male or female). Evidence (1): Hadith for establishing 'There is no sadaqah on less than thirty cows' from Abdullah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'In thirty cows, a tabi' or tabi'ah; and in every forty, a musinnah.' Evidence (2): Hadith for establishing the same from Abu Wa'il from Mu'adh: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) when he sent him to Yemen commanded him to take from cows: from every thirty a tabi' or tabi'ah, and from every forty a musinnah, and from every adult (halim) a dinar or its equivalent in Ma'afir garments.' Lexicon: tabi', tabi'ah: a calf that has exceeded one year, even if only one day. Musinn, musinnah: a calf that has exceeded two years, even if only one day.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri is a ruling statement establishing the basic nisab and obligation for zakat on cows. The matn states: No zakat is due on fewer than 30 cows. When the herd reaches 30, provided the cows are pasture-fed (sa'imah) and a full lunar year has passed, one must give a tabi' (one-year-old calf) or tabi'ah. At 40, a musinn (two-year-old) or musinnah is due. The author then cites two hadith proofs from the Prophet (peace be upon him) via Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Mu'adh ibn Jabal, both confirming the same obligations. The linguistic note clarifies that tabi' means a calf that has completed one year (even if by one day), and musinn means a calf that has completed two years. This is standard Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
تَبِيع (tabi'): A calf of cow that has completed one year of age, even if by one day.
مُسِنّ (musinn): A calf of cow that has completed two years of age.
سَائِمَة (sa'imah): Cows that are pasture-fed, grazing freely for most of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the zakat due on exactly 30 pasture-fed cows that have been owned for one lunar year?
A) Nothing
B) One tabi' or tabi'ah
C) One musinn or musinnah
D) Two tabi's

Key Takeaway
The minimum nisab for cows is 30; for 30 cows one tabi' (one-year-old) is due; for 40 cows one musinn (two-year-old) is due, provided they are pasture-fed and one year has passed.
