Zakat Schedule for Cows (30-100) and Rule on Buffaloes
Specifies zakat schedule for cows and equates buffaloes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the zakat schedule for cows from 30 to 100 and explain the Hanafi position that buffaloes are equivalent to cows for zakat.

Core Idea
Buffaloes are treated exactly like cows in zakat — the same nisab and schedule apply.

This passage specifies the zakat obligations for cows from 30 to 100. It also establishes that buffaloes (jawamis) are considered the same as cows for zakat purposes, based on legal analogy (qiyas). Memorizing this schedule is essential for correctly calculating zakat on bovine animals.

Guided Path
1
Understand the alternating pattern
The obligation changes every ten cows: at 30 it is one tabi', at 40 one musinnah, then the pattern alternates every ten. Identify the sequence.
2
Memorize key numbers
Focus on the thresholds: 30, 40, 60, 70, 80, 90, 100. At each, note whether a tabi' or musinnah is added.
The schedule from 60 to 100 is explicitly given in the text.
3
Apply the equivalence of buffaloes
The text explicitly states 'buffaloes and cows are the same' for zakat. Therefore, buffaloes count towards the same nisab and follow the same schedule.
This is a unique Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي مِائَةٍ تَبِيعَانِ وَمُسِنَّةٌ وَعَلَى هَذَا يَتَغَيَّرُ الْفَرْضُ فِي كُلِ عَشْرٍ مِنْ تَبِيعِ إِلَى مُسِنَّةٍ وَالْجُوَامِيسُ وَالْبَقَرُ سَوَاءٌ
اصول: ہر تیس گائے میں ایک تبیعہ یعنی ایک سال کا بچھڑا اور چالیس میں ایک مسنہ تو ساٹھ گائے میں دو تبیعہ ، اور ستر گائے میں ایک مسنہ اور ایک تبیعہ، اسی میں دو مسنہ اور نوے میں تین تبیعہ اور سو میں ایک مسنہ اور دو تبیعہ وقس علی ہذا۔ اصول : گائی اور بھینس کی جنس الگ الگ ہے لیکن زکوۃ کے باب میں دونوں کا حکم اور حساب ایک ہی ہے ،لہذا جو گائے کا حکم بیان کیا گیا ہے اسی پر بھینس کو قیاس کر لیا جائے۔
And at one hundred (cows) are two tabi's and one musinnah. And upon this, the fard (zakat) changes every ten from tabi' to musinnah. And buffaloes and cows are the same. Principle: Every thirty cows, one tabi'ah (one-year-old calf); and at forty, one musinnah. So at sixty cows: two tabi'ah; at seventy: one musinnah and one tabi'ah; at eighty: two musinnah; at ninety: three tabi'ah; and at one hundred: one musinnah and two tabi'ah. And so on analogically. Principle: The cow and buffalo are different in species, but in the section of zakat, both have the same ruling and calculation. Therefore, the ruling mentioned for cows is analogically applied to buffaloes.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage continues the zakat schedule for cows from 60 to 100. It states that at 100 cows, the obligation is two tabi's and one musinnah. The ruling changes every ten cows: from a tabi' to a musinnah alternately. The Urdu commentary clarifies the pattern: 30: 1 tabi', 40: 1 musinn, 60: 2 tabi', 70: 1 musinn + 1 tabi', 80: 2 musinn, 90: 3 tabi', 100: 1 musinn + 2 tabi'. Then it states that buffaloes are treated the same as cows for zakat purposes, despite being a different species, by way of qiyas (analogy). This is the Hanafi position: buffaloes and cows are considered the same in zakat because they belong to the same general category of bovine animals. The calculation is identical.

Key Terms
تَبِيع (tabi'): A one-year-old calf (male or female) given as zakat.
مُسِنَّة (musinnah): A two-year-old cow (female) given as zakat.
جَوَامِيس (jawamis): Buffaloes, a type of bovine animal distinct from cows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One tabi'
B) Two tabi's
C) Three tabi's
D) One musinnah and two tabi's

Key Takeaway
The zakat schedule for cows from 30 to 100 alternates between tabi' and musinnah, and buffaloes are fully equivalent to cows.

Zakat of Sheep and Goats: Nisab and Proofs
Ruling on zakat of sheep and goats with multiple hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab and zakat rates for sheep and goats and explain the primary hadith proof from Abu Bakr's letter.

Core Idea
No zakat below 40; at 40, one sheep; rates increase at 120, 200, and every 100 thereafter.

Zakat on livestock is a pillar of wealth purification. For sheep and goats, the nisab is 40 head. This lesson establishes the exact thresholds and the prophetic ordinance that governs them, anchored in the famous letter of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ
لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ أَرْبَعِينَ سَائِمَةً وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْخَوْلُ فَفِيهَا شَاةٌ وَالضَّأْنُ وَالْمَعْرُ سَوَاءٌ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً صَدَقَةٌ \ أَنَّ أَنَسًا حَدَّثَهُ «أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ ، كَتَبَ لَهُ هَذَا الْكِتَابَ ، لَمَّا وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْبَحْرَيْنِ : بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ هَذِهِ فَرِيضَةُ الصَّدَقَةِ، الَّتي فَرَضَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ، ..... فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سَائِمَةُ الرَّجُلِ نَاقِصَةً مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً وَاحِدَةً، فَلَيْسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ رَبُّهَا (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ، نمبر 1454/سنن ابوداود ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1567)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَ مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً صَدَقَةٌ \ قَالَ: ابْنُ أَخِي، وَأَيَّ نَحْوِ تَأْخُذُونَ؟ قُلْتُ: تَخَتَارُ، حَتَّى إِنَّا نَتَبَيَّنَ ضُرُوعَ الْغَنَمِ، قَالَ : " ابْنُ أَخِي فَإِنِّي أُحَدِثُكَ أَتِي كُنتُ فِي شِعْبِ مِنْ هَذِهِ الشَّعَابِ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي غَنَمِ لِي، . وَقَدْ نَهَانَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنْ نَأْخُذَ شَافِعًا، قُلْتُ: فَأَيَّ شَيْءٍ تَأْخُذَانِ؟ قَالَا: عَنَاقًا جَذَعَةً، أَوْ ثَنِيَّةً(سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1581)

وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً صَدَقَةٌ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ. قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ (لَا تَذْبَحُوا إِلَّا مُسِنَّةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْسُرَ عَلَيْكُمْ، فَتَذْبَحُوا جَذَعَةً مِنَ الضَّأْنِ (مسلم شريف، باب: ن الْأُضْحِيَّةِ، نمبر 1963/ سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ السِّنَّ فِي الصَّحَايَا، نمبر 2799) قَالَا : عَنَاقًا جَذَعَةً، أَوْ ثَنِيَّةً (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1581) اصول: چالیس بکریوں سے کم میں کوئی زکوۃ نہیں ہے البتہ 40 سے 120 تک ایک بکری، اور 120 سے 200
تک دو بکری، پھر 201 سے 300 تک تین بکری، پھر ہر 100 میں ایک ایک بکری واجب ہوتی چلی جائے گی۔
Chapter on Zakat of Sheep. There is no zakat on less than forty sheep. So when there are forty grazing sheep and a year has passed, then one sheep is due. And sheep (ḍa'n) and goats (ma'z) are the same. Wajh (1) for establishing the hadith: 'There is no zakat on less than forty sheep' - that Anas narrated to him: 'Abu Bakr wrote this document when he sent him to Bahrain: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. This is the obligatory charity that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) enjoined upon the Muslims... So if a man's grazing sheep are less than forty by one, there is no zakat on them unless the owner wishes.' (Bukhari, Sunan Abi Dawud) Wajh (2): ... 'He said: Nephew, what kind do you take? I said: We choose until we even examine the udders of the sheep. He said: Nephew, I will tell you that I was in one of these valleys during the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with my sheep, and the Messenger of Allah prohibited us from taking shāfi'. I said: What do you take? They said: A young weaned goat (jadh'ah) or a thinniyyah.' (Sunan Abi Dawud) ... Wajh (3): ... 'We were with a man from the companions of the Prophet called Mujāshi' from Banu Sulaym. Sheep became scarce, so he ordered a caller to announce that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The jadh' suffices from what the thinniy suffices.' ... Wajh (4): From Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not sacrifice except a musinnah unless it is difficult for you, then sacrifice a jadh'ah of sheep.' (Muslim, Sunan Abi Dawud) They said: A young weaned goat (jadh'ah) or a thinniyyah. Principle: There is no zakat on less than forty goats. However, from 40 to 120, one goat; from 120 to 200, two goats; then from 201 to 300, three goats; then for every 100, one goat becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on zakat of sheep (ghanam, including both sheep and goats). It is a ruling_with_proof. The base ruling: no zakat is due on fewer than forty head. When the flock reaches forty (grazing and owned for a full lunar year), one sheep is due. The text equates sheep (ḍa'n) and goats (ma'z) in this ruling. The author provides multiple hadith proofs. The primary proof is the famous letter of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) which records the prophetic ordinance on zakat, explicitly stating that below forty sheep there is no zakat. Additional proofs address the quality of the animal taken (not the best or poorest) and the permissibility of taking a jadh'ah (a young goat) when the proper age animal is unavailable. The Urdu commentary clarifies the progressive rates: 40-119: 1 sheep; 120-199: 2 sheep; 200-299: 3 sheep; then 1 sheep for every additional 100. The lesson reinforces that the nisab for small livestock is 40.

Key Terms
شاة (shāh): A head of sheep or goat (generic term for small livestock).
سائمة (sā'imah): Livestock that graze freely for the majority of the year without being fed by the owner.
جذعة (jadh'ah): A young goat or sheep that has reached a certain age (usually around one year for goats, but varies).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One sheep
B) Two sheep
C) Three sheep
D) Four sheep

Key Takeaway
Zakat on sheep and goats is wajib at 40 head, with progressive rates up to 300, then 1 per 100.

Zakat on Pastured Horses: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Rulings on zakat of sā'ima horses, mules, donkeys, and young animals with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on zakat of sā'ima horses, identify his proof, and explain the Sahibayn's opposing view and the practical consequence.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa requires zakat on pastured horses; the Sahibayn exempt them — an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with tangible financial impact.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a notable intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat of horses. While Abu Hanifa holds zakat wajib on sā'ima horses, his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree. The passage also covers related rulings on mules, donkeys, and young livestock, each supported by hadith. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh proofs within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the Hanafi position
The act is owning sā'ima (pastured) horses for a full lunar year. Abu Hanifa's ruling: zakat is wajib with an option — either pay one dinar per horse or 2.5% of the value.
Sā'ima means the horses graze freely for most of the year.
2
Locate the dalil for Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Jabir: 'In pastured horses, for every horse a dinar is given.' The imperative 'tū'addīhi' indicates obligation.
This is a hadith ahad, so its thubut is zanni, but in Hanafi usul, ahad hadith can impose a wajib obligation.
3
Identify the opposing view and its dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say no zakat on horses. Their proof is the hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave.'
The Sahibayn's hadith is more general and is found in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa reconciles by considering the Jabir hadith as specific to horses, while the Abu Hurairah hadith is general. In usul, a specific text (khass) overrides a general one (amm) when conflict arises.
The Sahibayn likely give precedence to the general hadith or interpret it as abrogating.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to Abu Hanifa, horse owners must pay zakat; according to the Sahibayn, they do not. Later Hanafi fatwa often follows the Sahibayn.
The ruling also affects how to treat young animals and other livestock.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الخَيْلِ

إِذَا كَانَتْ الْخَيْلُ سَائِمَةً ذُكُورًا وَإِنَاثًا وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الحَوْلُ فَصَاحِبُهَا بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَعْطَى عَنْ كُلِ فَرَسٍ دِينَارًا وَإِنْ شَاءَ قَوَّمَهَا وَأَعْطَى عَنْ كُلِ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا زَكَاةَ فِي الخَيْلِ. وَلَا شَيْءٍ فِي الْبِغَالِ وَالْحَمِيرِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَكُونَ لِلتِّجَارَةِ. وَلَيْسَ فِي الْفُصْلَانِ وَالْعَجَاجِيلِ وَالحَمْلَانِ صَدَقَةٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٍ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيهَا كِبَارٌ.

وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت إذا كانت الخيل سائمة ... عن جابر، قال: قال رسول الله : «في الخيل السائمة في كل فرس دينار تؤديه» (سنن دارقطني، باب زكاة مال التجارة وسقوطها عن الخيل والرقيق، رقم 2019/ سنن بيهقي، باب من رأى في الخيل صدقة، رقم 7419/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخيل، رقم 6889)

وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد لا زكاة في الخيل ... عن أبي هريرة قال: قال النبي : «ليس على المسلم في فرسه وغلامه صدقة.» (بخاري شريف، باب: ليس على المسلم في فرسه صدقة، رقم 1463/ سنن أبي داود، باب صدقة الرقيق، رقم 1595)

وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت ولا شيء في البغال والحمير ... أنه سمع أبا هريرة يقول: قال رسول الله . قيل: يا رسول الله فالحمر؟ قال: "ما أنزل علي في الحمر شيء إلا هذه الآية الفاذة الجامعة: {فمن يعمل مثقال ذرة خيرا يره. ومن يعمل مثقال ذرة شرا يره}" (مسلم شريف، باب إثم مانع الزكاة، رقم 987/ بخاري شريف باب: الخيل لثلاثة، رقم 2860/)

وجه:(2) قول الصحابي لثبوت ولا شيء في البغال والحمير ... قال سفيان: "ونحن نقول: إلا أن تكون لتجارة" (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الحمر، رقم 6871)

وجه:(1) قول التابعي لثبوت وليس في الفصلان والعجاجيل ... عن الحسن، قالا: «لا يعتد بالسخلة، ولا تؤخذ في الصدقة» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، السخلة تحسب على صاحب الغنم، رقم 9982)

وقال أبو يوسف فيها واحدة منها. وجه:(1) قول التابعي لثبوت وقال أبو يوسف فيها واحدة منها ... عن عطاء، قال: قلت له: أيعتد بالصغار أولاد الشاة؟ قال: «نعم» (مصنف ابن شيبه، السخلة تحسب على صاحب الغنم، 9983)

اصول: اصل مال کو اختیار ہو گا کہ ہر گھوڑے کے بدلہ ایک دینار دیدے، یا پھر قیمت کے حساب سے ہر دوسو در ہم میں پانچ در ہم دیدے۔
Chapter of zakat of horses. If horses are pasturing, male and female, and a year passes, then their owner has the choice: if he wishes, he gives for every horse a dinar; and if he wishes, he values them and gives for every two hundred dirhams five dirhams. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: No zakat on horses. And nothing on mules and donkeys unless they are for trade. And there is no sadaqah on foals, calves, and lambs according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad unless there are adults among them. (Proofs follow). And Abu Yusuf said concerning them (young animals): one from them. (Proof). Principle: The owner of the property will have the choice to give for each horse one dinar, or according to value, for every two hundred dirhams give five dirhams.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on zakat of horses in al-Quduri. It presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa that on pastured horses (sā'ima) that have been in one's possession for a full year, zakat is obligatory. The owner has an option: either give one dinar per horse directly, or assess the value and pay 2.5% (5 dirhams per 200). This is based on a hadith from Jabir. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that there is no zakat on horses, citing the hadith of Abu Hurairah that there is no sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave. This is a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The text then states that there is no zakat on mules and donkeys unless they are trade goods, supported by a hadith that only the general verse on good deeds applies to donkeys. Finally, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, young animals (foals, calves, lambs) are not subject to zakat unless there are adult animals among them; but Abu Yusuf held that one young animal counts. The principle is that the owner has the choice of payment method.

Key Terms
سَائِمَة (sā'ima): Livestock that graze freely in pastures for most of the year, as opposed to being stall-fed.
زَكَاة الخَيْل (zakāt al-khayl): Zakat on horses, which Abu Hanifa considers obligatory on pastured horses; Sahibayn disagree.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad use to argue that no zakat is due on horses?
A) The hadith of Jabir: 'In pastured horses, for every horse a dinar is given.'
B) The hadith of Abu Hurairah: 'There is no sadaqah on a Muslim's horse or slave.'
C) The Qur'anic verse on charity.
D) Consensus of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa made zakat on sā'ima horses wajib with an option, but his two students exempted all horses, and their view became the relied-upon position in the late Hanafi school.

Substitution When Exact Due Animal is Missing and Paying Value
Ruling with proofs on substitution and value payment in zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for substituting a missing zakat animal and explain the permissibility of paying value in zakat based on istihsan.

Core Idea
If the exact zakat animal is absent, the collector substitutes a higher/lower animal with compensation; paying value is allowed by istihsan.

This lesson addresses a practical challenge in zakat collection: when the specific age of livestock due is not available. The Hanafi school, drawing on the practice of the early caliphs, provides a flexible solution: the collector may take a better or worse animal and adjust the difference. Additionally, paying monetary value is permitted based on istihsan (juristic preference) and the precedent of Mu'adh ibn Jabal. We will examine the proofs and the cross-madhhab difference on value payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its objective
Read the first sentence: when the exact due animal is missing, the collector takes a higher or lower animal and adjusts. This ensures collection continues without hardship.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the practice of Abu Bakr as recorded in Bukhari: 'An Abi Bakr kataba lahu...'. This hadith instructs taking a higher animal and giving compensation.
This is the key dalil for substitution.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly mentions taking a better animal and paying twenty dirhams or two sheep. This directly shows that substitution with value adjustment is valid.
4
Examine the ruling on paying value
The text states 'وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الْقِيمَةِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ' and provides the proof from Mu'adh: people brought clothes instead of grain. This qawl al-sahabi supports paying value in kind by monetary equivalent.
5
Identify the ikhtilaf and the Hanafi tarjih
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) do not permit paying value in zakat. The Hanafi position is based on istihsan and the practice of the companions. The mufta bihi is permissibility.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سِنٌ فَلَمْ يُوجَدْ مَعَهُ أَخَذَ الْمُصَدِّقُ أَعْلَى مِنْهَا وَرَدَّ الْفَضْلَ أَوْ أَخَذَ دُونَهَا وَأَخَذَ الْفَضْلَ - وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الْقِيمَةِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ. وَلَيْسَ فِي الْعَوَامِلِ وَالْحَوَامِلِ وَالْمَعْلُوفَةِ صَدَقَةٌ. وَلَا يَأْخُذُ الْمُصَدِّقُ خِيَارَ الْمَالِ وَلَا رَذَالَتَهُ وَيَأْخُذُ الْوَسَطَ مِنْهُ.

وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت ومن وجب عليه سن فلم يوجد معه ... أن أبا بكر كتب له التي أمر الله رسوله : ومن بلغت صدقته بنت مخاض وليست عنده، وعنده بنت لبون، فإنها تقبل منه، ويعطيه المصدق عشرين درهما أو شاتين، فإن لم تكن عنده بنت مخاض على وجهها، وعنده ابن لبون، فإنه يقبل منه، وليس معه شيء (بخاري شريف، باب العرض في الزكاة، 1448)

وجه:(2) قول الصحابي لثبوت ومن وجب عليه سن فلم يوجد معه ... قال معاذ الله لأهل اليمن: ائتوني بعرض ثياب خميص أو لبيس في الصدقة مكان الشعير والدرة أهون عليكم وخير لأصحاب النبي بالمدينة (بخاري شريف، باب العرض في الزكاة، رقم 1448)

د وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت وليس في العوامل والحوامل والمعلوفة صدقة ... عن علي ، قال زهير: أحسبه عن النبي ... وليس على العوامل شيء (سنن أبي داود، باب في زكاة السائمة، رقم 1572/ سنن دارقطني باب ليس في العوامل صدقة، رقم 1938)

وجه:(2) قول التابعي لثبوت وليس في العوامل والحوامل والمعلوفة صدقة ... عن إبراهيم، قال: «ليس في غنم الربائب صدقة» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبه، في الرجل تكون له الغنم في المصر يحتلبها، رقم 9981)

ووجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت ولا يأخذ المصدق خيار المال ... أن أبا بكر في كتب له التي أمر الله رسوله : ولا يخرج في الصدقة هرمة، ولا ذات عوار، ولا تيس، إلا ما شاء

اصول: اگر زکوۃ میں کوئی چھوٹا جانور واجب ہوا ہے اور مالک کے پاس سب بڑے جانور ہیں یا بڑا واجب ہوا لیکن مالک کے پاس سب چھوٹے ہیں تو قیمت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔
And whoever owes a certain age (of animal) and does not have it with him, the collector takes a higher one and refunds the excess, or takes a lower one and takes the surplus. And it is permissible to pay value in zakat. And there is no sadaqah on working animals, pack animals, and fed animals. And the collector does not take the best of the wealth nor the worst, but takes the middle from it. (Proofs follow). Principle: If in zakat a small animal is due and the owner has only large animals, or a large animal is due and he has only small, then value is considered.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on zakat of horses but applies generally to livestock zakat. It provides rules for the collector when the exact due animal (e.g., a one-year-old sheep) is not available. The collector may take a better animal and refund the difference, or take an inferior one and collect the shortfall in cash or kind. Paying value (qi mah) in zakat is explicitly allowed, supported by the practice of Abu Bakr and Mu'adh. Then the text exempts working animals (used for ploughing), pack animals (for carrying loads), and animals that are stall-fed (ma'lūfah) from zakat, citing hadith. Finally, the collector is instructed to take neither the best nor the worst animals, but the medium quality, based on Abu Bakr's instructions. The Urdu principle clarifies that if the due animal is of one age and the owner possesses animals of different ages, the value is considered instead.

Key Terms
الْقِيمَة (al-qīmah): Monetary value paid in lieu of the exact zakat item; permissible in Hanafi school.
الْمُصَدِّق (al-muṣaddiq): Zakat collector authorized by the state or community to collect and distribute zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the text say about paying value (qīmah) in zakat?
A) It is not allowed under any circumstances.
B) It is allowed only when the due animal is missing.
C) It is allowed generally (يجوز دفع القيمة في الزكاة).
D) It is allowed but only with the collector's permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits substituting a missing zakat animal with a higher/lower one with compensation and also allows paying value, based on istihsan and the practice of the early caliphs.

Exemptions for Working, Pack, and Fed Animals; Collector Must Take Medium Quality
Rulings with proofs on exemptions and medium quality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which animals are exempt from zakat (al-'awāmil, al-ḥawāmil, al-ma'lūfah) and state the rule that the collector must take the average quality.

Core Idea
Working, pack, and stall-fed animals are exempt from zakat; the collector must avoid the best and worst and take the middle.

This lesson covers two practical rules in zakat collection: exemptions for certain categories of animals and the quality standard for collection. The first rule excludes animals used for labour or not pastured freely, based on hadith. The second rule instructs collectors to avoid extreme quality and take the average, as per the guidance of Abu Bakr. These rules ensure fairness and prevent hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
The text mentions three: al-‘awāmil (working animals like ploughing oxen), al-ḥawāmil (pack animals like camels used for carrying loads), and al-ma'lūfah (stall-fed animals that are not free-grazing).
These categories are in the second sentence.
2
Locate the proof for exemption
The author cites a hadith from Ali (ra): 'ليس على العوامل شيء' (there is nothing on working animals). Also a qawl of the tabi'i Ibrahim: 'ليس في غنم الربائب صدقة'.
These proofs establish the exemption.
3
Understand the ruling on medium quality
The collector must not take the best or worst, but the average (al-wasaṭ). This is based on the letter of Abu Bakr: 'ولا يخرج في الصدقة هرمة، ولا ذات عوار، ولا تيس'.
4
Apply the quality rule
When assessing zakat animals, avoid choosing the very best (khiyār al-māl) or the very worst (radhālatuhu). Select medium quality to avoid injustice.
5
Recognize the wisdom behind these rules
Exemptions protect farmers' livelihood; the medium quality rule balances the rights of the poor and the owner.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Zakat of Horses and General Zakat Rules
Chapter on zakat of horses with rulings and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on zakat of horses, identify the conditions for livestock zakat, and explain the proofs for key rules.

Core Idea
Zakat on horses is wajib according to Abu Yusuf; no zakat on working or fodder-fed animals.

This chapter from al-Quduri sets out the rulings on zakat of horses, a topic of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. You will learn the conditions for livestock zakat, how to handle missing age animals, and the collector's obligations. The text also provides hadith evidence for each rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on horses and the intra-Hanafi dispute
The matn states Abu Yusuf's view: one unit per sa'imah horse. Abu Hanifa holds no zakat on horses. Recognize which view is presented as the operative rule.
The text focuses on Abu Yusuf's position, implying it is the relied-upon view in later Hanafi works.
2
Understand the rule for missing age animals and value payment
When the exact age required is unavailable, the collector may take a higher or lower age and compensate with cash or kind. This shows the permissibility of paying value (qima) in zakat.
This rule is derived from the letter of Abu Bakr and the practice of Mu'adh.
3
List exemptions from zakat on animals
Three categories are exempt: draft animals (al-'awamil), pregnant animals (al-hawamil), and fodder-fed animals (al-ma'lufah). These are not zakatable even if they reach nisab.
The hadith of Ali confirms 'no zakat on working animals'.
4
Grasp the definition of sa'imah and the nisab-only zakat rule
Sa'imah means animals that graze on natural pasture for most of the year. If fed for half the year or more, no zakat. Also, zakat is due only on the nisab amount, not on surplus (al-'afw).
This distinction from the Shafi'i school is highlighted.
5
Trace the proofs: which hadith supports each rule
Each ruling in the matn is footnoted with hadith or athar. For example, the hadith of Abu Bakr supports the age substitution rule; the hadith of Mu'adh supports value payment; the hadith of Ali supports exemption of working animals.
The text uses 'wajh' to indicate the evidential basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْخَيْلِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِيهَا وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْهَا. وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سِنٌ فَلَمْ يُوجَدْ مَعَهُ أَخَذَ الْمُصَدِّقُ أَعْلَى مِنْهَا وَرَدَّ الْفَضْلَ أَوْ أَخَذَ دُونَهَا وَأَخَذَ الْفَضْلَ - وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الْقِيمَةِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ. وَلَيْسَ فِي الْعَوَامِلِ وَالْحَوَامِلِ وَالْمَعْلُوفَةِ صَدَقَةٌ. وَلَا يَأْخُذُ الْمُصَدِّقُ خِيَارَ الْمَالِ وَلَا رَذَالَتَهُ وَيَأْخُذُ الْوَسَطَ مِنْهُ. وَمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ نِصَابٌ فَاسْتَفَادَ فِي أَثْنَاءِ الْحَوْلِ مَالًا مِنْ جِنْسِهِ ضَمَّهُ إِلَى مَالِهِ وَزَكَّاهُ. وَالسَّائِمَةُ هِيَ الَّتِي تَكْتَفِي بِالرَّعْيِ فِي أَكْثَرِ حَوْلِهَا فَإِنْ عَلَفَهَا نِصْفَ الْحَوْلِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ فِيهَا. وَالزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي النِّصَابِ دُونَ الْعَفْوِ.

وَجْهٌ (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِيهَا وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْهَا: عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لَهُ: أَيُعْتَدُّ بِالصَّغَارِ أَوْلَادِ الشَّاةِ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ. (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، 9983)
وَجْهٌ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سِنٌ فَلَمْ يُوجَدْ مَعَهُ: أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ كَتَبَ لَهُ الَّتِي أَمَرَ اللَّهُ رَسُولَهُ: وَمَنْ بَلَغَتْ صَدَقَتُهُ بِنْتَ مَخَاضٍ وَلَيْسَتْ عِنْدَهُ وَعِنْدَهُ بِنْتُ لَبُونٍ فَإِنَّهَا تُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ وَيُعْطِيهِ الْمُصَدِّقُ عِشْرِينَ دِرْهَمًا أَوْ شَاتَيْنِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عِنْدَهُ بِنْتُ مَخَاضٍ عَلَى وَجْهِهَا وَعِنْدَهُ ابْنُ لَبُونٍ فَإِنَّهُ يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ وَلَيْسَ مَعَهُ شَيْءٌ. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ الْعَرْضِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ، 1448)
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ سِنٌ فَلَمْ يُوجَدْ مَعَهُ: قَالَ مُعَاذٌ لِأَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ: ائْتُونِي بِعَرْضِ ثِيَابٍ خَمِيصٍ أَوْ لَبِيسٍ فِي الصَّدَقَةِ مَكَانَ الشَّعِيرِ وَالدُّرَّةِ أَهْوَنُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَخَيْرٌ لِأَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ بِالْمَدِينَةِ. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ الْعَرْضِ فِي الزَّكَاةِ، 1448)
وَجْهٌ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَيْسَ فِي الْعَوَامِلِ وَالْخَوَامِلِ وَالْمَعْلُوفَةِ صَدَقَةٌ: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ أَحْسَبُهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَلَيْسَ عَلَى الْعَوَامِلِ شَيْءٌ. (سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، 1572 / سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، بَابٌ لَيْسَ فِي الْعَوَامِلِ صَدَقَةٌ، 1938)
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: لَيْسَ فِي غَنَمِ الرَّبَائِبِ صَدَقَةٌ. (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، 9981)
وَجْهٌ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَأْخُذُ الْمُصَدِّقُ خِيَارَ الْمَالِ: أَنَّ أَبَا بَكْرٍ فِي كِتَابِهِ الَّذِي أَمَرَ اللَّهُ رَسُولَهُ: وَلَا يُخْرَجُ فِي الصَّدَقَةِ هَرِمَةٌ وَلَا ذَاتُ عَوَارٍ وَلَا تَيْسٌ إِلَّا مَا شَاءَ الْمُصَدِّقُ. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابٌ لَا تُؤْخَذُ فِي الصَّدَقَةِ هَرِمَةٌ وَلَا ذَاتُ عَوَارٍ، 1455)
وَجْهٌ (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ لَمَّا بَعَثَ مُعَاذًا عَلَى الْيَمَنِ ... وَتَوَقَّ كَرَائِمَ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابٌ لَا تُؤْخَذُ كَرَائِمُ أَمْوَالِ النَّاسِ فِي الصَّدَقَةِ، 1458)
وَجْهٌ (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ نِصَابٌ فَاسْتَفَادَ فِي أَثْنَاءِ الْحَوْلِ: عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقُولُ: إِذَا اسْتَفَادَ الرَّجُلُ مَالًا فَأَرَادَ أَنْ يُنْفِقَهُ قَبْلَ فَجِيءٍ شَهْرٍ زَكَاتِهِ فَلْيُزَكِّهِ ثُمَّ لْيُنْفِقْهُ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُرِيدُ أَنْ يُنْفِقَ فَلْيُزَكِّهِ مَعَ مَالِهِ. (مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، 10227 / مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، 6872)
وَجْهٌ (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: مَنِ اسْتَفَادَ مَالًا فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ حَتَّى يَحُولَ عَلَيْهِ الْحَوْلُ. (سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، 631 / سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، 1887)
وَجْهٌ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالسَّائِمَةُ هِيَ الَّتِي تَكْتَفِي بِالرَّعْيِ: حَدَّثَنِي ثُمَامَةُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَنَسٍ أَنَّ أَنَسًا حَدَّثَهُ ... فَإِذَا كَانَتْ سَائِمَةُ الرَّجُلِ نَاقِصَةً مِنْ أَرْبَعِينَ شَاةً وَاحِدَةً فَلَيْسَ فِيهَا صَدَقَةٌ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشَاءَ رَبُّهَا. (صَحِيحُ الْبُخَارِيِّ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْغَنَمِ، 1454 / سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، 1570)
وَجْهٌ (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَاجِبَةٌ: عَنْ مُعَاذٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَمَرَهُ حِينَ وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ: أَنْ لَا تَأْخُذَ مِنَ الْكَسْرِ شَيْئًا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَرِقُ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ فَخُذْ مِنْهَا خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ وَلَا تَأْخُذْ مِمَّا زَادَ شَيْئًا حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمًا. (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، 1903)
أُصُولٌ: إِذَا زَكَاةٍ فِي كَوْيَ چھوٹا جانور واجب ہوا ہے اور مالک کے پاس سب بڑے جانور ہیں یا بڑا واجب ہوا لیکن مالک کے پاس سب چھوٹے ہیں تو قیمت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔
أُصُولٌ: إِذَا نِصَابٌ کے بقدر جانور ہوں اور کچھ ان کے بچے بھی ہوں تو بچے بھی زکاۃ میں شمار ہوں گے۔
Chapter of Zakat of Horses. Abu Yusuf said: On them, one from each. Whoever is obligated with an age [of animal] but it is not found with him, the collector takes a higher [value] and returns the excess, or takes a lower [value] and takes the excess. And it is permissible to pay the value in zakat. There is no sadaqah on draft animals, pregnant animals, and fodder-fed animals. The collector does not take the best of the wealth nor its worst, and takes the middle from it. Whoever possesses a nisab and acquires wealth of the same type during the year, he adds it to his wealth and pays zakat on it. The grazing animal (sa'imah) is one that subsists on pasture for most of the year; if it is fed for half the year or more, then there is no zakat on it for him. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, zakat is obligatory on the nisab, not on the surplus. Evidence (1) Statement of the follower for establishing that Abu Yusuf said: On them, one from each: from 'Ata', he said: I asked him: Are the young of sheep counted? He said: Yes. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 9983) ... [continues with all proofs] Principles: If in zakat a small animal is due but the owner has only large ones, or a large one is due but the owner has only small ones, then the value is considered. Principles: If there are animals equal to the nisab and also some of their young, the young are also counted in the zakat.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is the complete chapter on zakat of horses from al-Quduri with hadith proofs. The matn begins by stating the ruling of Abu Yusuf on horses (implicitly differing from Abu Hanifa who holds no zakat on horses). Then it covers several general zakah rules: when the required animal age is missing, the collector may take a higher or lower value and compensate; paying value in kind is allowed; draft, pregnant, and stall-fed animals have no zakat; the collector must take middle quality, not the best or worst. On page 197, the matn adds: newly acquired wealth of the same type is added to the nisab and zakat is due; definition of sa'imah (grazing livestock) and the ruling that if fed half the year or more, no zakat; and finally that zakat is on the nisab only, not on surplus (highlighting the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i view on surplus). The margin provides hadith and athar proofs for each ruling. The Urdu notes summarize two principles: when there is a size mismatch, value is considered; and young animals are included in the nisab count.

Key Terms
السائِمَةُ (al-sā'imah): Livestock that graze on natural pasture for most of the year, as opposed to being stall-fed.
الْعَوَامِلُ (al-'awāmil): Draft animals used for work (plowing, carrying).
الْعَفْوُ (al-'afw): The surplus amount of wealth beyond the nisab that is less than a full nisab increment (e.g., excess dirhams beyond 200).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on zakat for horses according to Abu Yusuf?
A) No zakat on horses at all.
B) Zakat is due on grazing horses, one unit per horse.
C) Zakat is due on all horses regardless of use.
D) Zakat is due only on working horses.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on horses is specific to sa'imah (grazing) animals and is wajib per Abu Yusuf; working and fed horses are exempt.

Ruling on Adding Newly Acquired Wealth to Zakatable Wealth
States ruling on adding newly acquired wealth of same type during zakat year

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding newly acquired wealth to an existing nisab and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
New wealth of the same type is added to existing nisab; zakat is due on the total at the end of the original year.

This lesson covers a concise ruling from Al-Quduri's matn on zakat. The rule is simple but often misunderstood: when you already own the minimum zakatable amount (nisab) and acquire more of the same type during the year, you do not start a new year for the new wealth. Instead, you add it to your existing total and pay zakat on everything together at the end of the original year. This reflects the Hanafi principle that the zakat year is tied to the nisab, not to each individual unit of wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of acquiring additional wealth of the same type during the zakat year. The ruling is wajib: it must be added to the existing nisab and zakat paid on the combined total.
2
Identify the conditions for the ruling
The ruling only applies if: (1) the person already has a complete nisab, (2) the newly acquired wealth is of the same genus (jins) as the existing nisab, (3) the acquisition occurs during the current zakat year.
If the genus is different, the new wealth may start its own year.
3
Understand the evidence
The Hanafi school relies on the hadith: 'Whoever acquires wealth, there is no zakat on it until a year passes over it.' The key point is that the 'year' refers to the existing nisab's year, not a new year for each addition.
The hadith is cited in the commentary as support for adding.
4
Contrast with other schools
Note that the Maliki and Shafi'i schools treat new acquisitions as starting a separate year. This difference affects how zakat is calculated in practice.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْخَيْلَ وَمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ نِصَابٌ فَاسْتَفَادَ فِي أَثْنَاءِ الْحَوْلِ مَالًا مِنْ جِنْسِهِ ضَمَّهُ إِلَى مَالِهِ وَزَكَّاهُ
Chapter of Zakat of Horses: And whoever has a nisab and acquires during the year wealth of its same type, he adds it to his wealth and gives zakat on it.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri. It states that if a person already owns a nisab (minimum threshold) of zakatable wealth and during the zakat year acquires additional wealth of the same category (e.g., more cash of the same currency, or more livestock of the same type), then this newly acquired wealth is added to the existing nisab, and zakat is paid on the total at the end of the year, provided the original nisab was held at the beginning and end of the year. This follows the Hanafi principle that zakat is based on the complete lunar year (hawl) for the nisab, and new acquisitions of the same genus are treated as part of the original pile, not as a separate new wealth starting a new year. The Hadith proofs for this are given in the commentary, including statements from Al-Zuhri and Ibn Umar.

Key Terms
اسْتَفَادَ (istafāda): To acquire new wealth during the zakat year.
نِصَاب (niṣāb): The minimum threshold of wealth that obligates zakat.
ضَمَّهُ (ḍammahu): To add the new wealth to the existing wealth for zakat calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone has 200 dirhams (nisab) and during the year acquires another 100 dirhams, how is zakat calculated?
A) The new 100 dirhams starts its own year, so zakat is due separately after a year.
B) The new 100 dirhams is added to the 200, and zakat on 300 is given at the end of the original year.
C) No zakat is due on the new 100 until it completes a year alone.
D) Zakat is given immediately on the new 100 as soon as acquired.

Key Takeaway
New wealth of the same genus is added to the existing nisab; zakat on the total is due at the end of the original year.

Definition of Sa'imah and Effect of Feeding on Zakat
Defines sa'imah and states ruling when fed half the year or more.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sa'imah and apply the Hanafi rule that zakat is not due on livestock fed for half the year or more.

Core Idea
Zakat on livestock is only obligatory if they are sa'imah — grazing naturally for most of the year.

This lesson examines the definition of sa'imah (pastured livestock) and the crucial effect of feeding (al-‘alaf) on the obligation of zakat. Understanding this distinction is vital for correctly determining zakat liability on camels, cattle, and goats. The Hanafi school uniquely restricts zakat on livestock to those that are sa'imah, unlike other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses the act of owning livestock and the ruling of zakat. First, identify that zakat is wajib on sa'imah livestock meeting nisab. Then note the exception: if fed half the year or more, zakat drops.
The ruling is based on the definition of sa'imah.
2
Define sa'imah precisely
Sa'imah is defined as livestock that suffice with grazing (al-ra'iy) for most of their year. 'Most' means more than half the year. The animals must depend on natural pasture, not on fodder provided by the owner.
If they are stall-fed, they are ma'lufah, not sa'imah.
3
Determine the feeding threshold
If the owner feeds the animals (al-‘alaf) for half the year or more, they are no longer considered sa'imah, and zakat is not wajib. Feeding for exactly half counts as 'half the year or more'.
Feeding for less than half the year does not affect the obligation.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school does not distinguish between sa'imah and ma'lufah; they require zakat on all livestock reaching nisab, regardless of feeding. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is based on hadiths that specify 'sa'imah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالسَّائِمَةُ هِيَ الَّتِي تَكْتَفِي بِالرَّعْيِ فِي أَكْثَرِ حَوْلِهَا فَإِنْ عَلَفَهَا نِصْفَ الْحَوْلِ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فَلَا زَكَاةَ عَلَيْهِ فِيهَا
And sa'imah is that which suffices with grazing for most of its year. Then if he feeds it half the year or more, there is no zakat on him concerning them.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'sa'imah' (pastured livestock) as animals that depend primarily on natural grazing for the majority of the year. If the owner feeds them (with stored fodder) for half the year or more, they are no longer considered sa'imah, and zakat is not obligatory on them. This ruling applies to camels, cattle, and goats. The condition is that the animals must be grazing on natural pasture (not cultivated land) for more than half the year. If they are stall-fed or fed by the owner for half the year or more, they are ma'lufah (fed livestock), and no zakat on them. The proof cited in the commentary is the hadith of Anas regarding sa'imah sheep below 40.

Key Terms
السَّائِمَة (al-sā'imah): Livestock that graze on natural pasture for most of the year.
الْعَلَف (al-‘alaf): Fodder provided by the owner; if given for half the year or more, zakat drops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has 40 sheep that are fed stored grain for 7 months of the year. According to Hanafi fiqh, is zakat obligatory on these sheep?
A) Yes, because they reached nisab.
B) No, because they are not sa'imah (pastured) for most of the year.
C) Yes, but only if they are pastured for the entire year.
D) No, because feeding for 7 months is less than half the year.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the obligation of zakat on livestock depends on them being sa'imah; feeding for half the year or more removes the obligation.

Zakat on Nisab vs. Afw: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat scope

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat on nisab vs. afw, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Zakat is only on the first nisab; surplus (afw) is exempt until it reaches another nisab.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between the early masters. While Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is due only on the nisab amount itself, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar extend it to the entire wealth including surplus. Understanding this difference is crucial for correct zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold versus what Muhammad and Zufar hold. Note that the dispute is about whether zakat applies only to the minimum nisab or also to the surplus (afw) that is less than a full nisab.
2
Understand the hadith proof
The hadith of Mu'adh ( narrated by Abu Dawud) instructs: 'Take from the kasr (breakage, i.e., surplus less than nisab) nothing, and when silver reaches 200 dirhams, take 5 dirhams...' This is the dalil for Abu Hanifa's position that amounts below a new nisab are exempt.
The hadith is explicit (nas) and restricts the general command to pay zakat on wealth.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Work through an example: 250 dirhams. Under Abu Hanifa, zakat is on the first 200 (5 dirhams) and 50 is exempt. Under Muhammad, zakat is on the whole 250 (6.25 dirhams). The practical difference is the amount payable.
The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالزَّكَاةُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي النِّصَابِ دُونَ الْعَفْوِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ وَزُفَرُ تَتَعَلَّقُ بِالنِّصَابِ وَالْعَفْوِ
And zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is obligatory on the nisab, not on the surplus. And Muhammad and Zufar said it is attached to both the nisab and the surplus.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the early masters. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that zakat is due only on the nisab amount itself; any excess wealth (afw) above the nisab is not subject to zakat until it itself reaches a new nisab (i.e., each 200 dirhams or part thereof). In contrast, Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar hold that zakat is due on the entire amount, including the surplus, even if the surplus is less than the nisab. For example, if someone has 250 dirhams, Abu Hanifa says zakat is only on the first 200 (5 dirhams) and the 50 is afw (exempt), while Muhammad says zakat is on the whole 250 (6.25 dirhams). The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is more cautious and in line with the Sunnah. The hadith proofs cited in the commentary include the instruction to Mu'adh: 'Take from the kasr (breakage, i.e., surplus less than nisab) nothing, and when silver reaches 200 dirhams, take 5 dirhams...' This hadith supports Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
الْعَفْو (al-‘afw): The surplus wealth above the nisab that is less than a full nisab.
النِّصَاب (al-niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if someone has 300 dirhams (nisab for silver is 200), how much zakat is due?
A) 7.5 dirhams (on 300)
B) 5 dirhams (on 200, 100 exempt)
C) 2.5 dirhams (on 100 only)
D) 10 dirhams (on 400?)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that zakat is only on the nisab, and surplus (afw) is exempt from zakat until it forms a full new nisab.

Destruction of Zakatable Wealth After Obligation
States the ruling on destruction dropping zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zakat obligation drops when the wealth is destroyed after the year completes, and explain the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Zakat is a right in the wealth, not a personal debt; loss of wealth extinguishes the right.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a critical question: What happens to the obligation of zakat if the zakatable wealth is destroyed after the year ends but before payment? The Hanafi school holds that the obligation drops entirely, while the Shafi'i school treats it as a debt in the dhimmah. Understanding the underlying principle — that zakat is attached to the specific wealth — resolves this.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario is: wealth is destroyed ('halka al-mal') after zakat has become obligatory (i.e., after the lunar year has completed).
The obligation arises at the end of the year, not before.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The text says 'saqatat anhu' — it drops from him. The obligation is completely lifted.
No requirement to pay in the future.
3
Understand the legal basis
Zakat is a right (haqq) tied to the specific wealth ('ayn), not a personal liability (dayn). When that wealth perishes, the right no longer exists.
This contrasts with debts, which persist in the dhimmah.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i
The Shafi'i school treats zakat as a debt in the dhimmah, so destruction does not drop the obligation; one must pay when able.
The practical difference: Hanafi says no payment; Shafi'i says it remains.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is clear: in a fatwa, the Hanafi mufti will not require payment, while the Shafi'i mufti will.
Both positions are based on valid usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا هَلَكَ الْمَالُ بَعْدَ وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ سَقَطَتْ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الزَّكَاةَ عَلَى الْحَوْلِ وَهُوَ مَالِكٌ لِلنِّصَابِ جَازَ
And when the wealth is destroyed after the obligation of zakat, it is dropped from him. Then if he advances zakat before the year while he is owner of the nisab, it is permissible.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from Al-Quduri. First: If the zakatable wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory (i.e., after the completion of the year), the obligation of zakat is dropped (saqatat) because the wealth is no longer in his possession; zakat is a right attached to the wealth itself, not a personal debt irrevocable. The commentary cites proofs from Ata and Mughirah. Second: A person may give zakat before the completion of the year (ta'jil al-zakat) provided he owns the nisab at the time of advancing. This is permissible because zakat can be accelerated. The proof cited is the hadith of Abbas who asked the Prophet to give his zakat early and was permitted. However, if the wealth is destroyed after advancing, the payment is valid; if the wealth increases, he may need to pay more. The detailed conditions are in the commentaries.

Key Terms
هَلَكَ الْمَال (halaka al-māl): Destruction of wealth before zakat payment.
سَقَطَتْ (saqatat): It drops; the obligation is lifted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, if a person's zakatable wealth is destroyed after the completion of the lunar year but before payment, what is the ruling?
A) He must still pay zakat from other sources.
B) The obligation drops and no payment is required.
C) He must make up the zakat when he acquires new wealth.
D) He must pay half of the zakat.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, zakat obligation is extinguished when the zakatable wealth is destroyed after the obligation becomes due, because the right is attached to the wealth itself.

Advancing Zakat Before the Year End
States the ruling on advancing zakat before the year.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that advancing zakat before the year end is permissible if one owns the nisab, and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Zakat may be paid early if you already own the minimum threshold, but the obligation is not yet due.

The second ruling in this passage addresses a practical question: Can a person pay zakat before the completion of the lunar year? Al-Quduri states that it is permissible (ja'iz) provided the person owns the nisab at the time of payment. This is based on the hadith of Abbas, who sought and received the Prophet's permission to pay his zakat early. We will examine the condition, the proof, and the Shafi'i perspective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and ruling
The action is advancing zakat (taqdīm al-zakāt) before the year (hawl) completes. The ruling is 'jāza' (permissible).
It is not obligatory to advance; it is a voluntary option.
2
Note the condition
The text explicitly states the condition: 'wa huwa mālikun li al-nisāb' — he must be the owner of the nisab at the time of advancing.
If he does not own the nisab at the time, the payment is not considered valid zakat for the current year.
3
Locate the dalil
The Hadith of Abbas: the Prophet (ﷺ) permitted Abbas to give his zakat early. This is a proof that advancing is allowed.
The hadith is cited in Sunan Abi Dawud and al-Tirmidhi.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
The permissibility is based on the principle that zakat can be accelerated because the right becomes due at the end of the year, but payment can be made earlier as a form of ihsan.
There is no harm in paying early as long as the nisab condition is met.
5
Contrast with Shafi'i
The Shafi'i school also permits it but considers it makruh (disliked) if done without necessity, because it is preferable to pay after the year.
Hanafi: ja'iz (permissible) without dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا هَلَكَ الْمَالُ بَعْدَ وُجُوبِ الزَّكَاةِ سَقَطَتْ عَنْهُ فَإِنْ قَدَّمَ الزَّكَاةَ عَلَى الْحَوْلِ وَهُوَ مَالِكٌ لِلنِّصَابِ جَازَ

Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from Al-Quduri. First: If the zakatable wealth is destroyed after zakat becomes obligatory (i.e., after the completion of the year), the obligation of zakat is dropped (saqatat) because the wealth is no longer in his possession; zakat is a right attached to the wealth itself, not a personal debt irrevocable. The commentary cites proofs from Ata and Mughirah. Second: A person may give zakat before the completion of the year (ta'jil al-zakat) provided he owns the nisab at the time of advancing. This is permissible because zakat can be accelerated. The proof cited is the hadith of Abbas who asked the Prophet to give his zakat early and was permitted. However, if the wealth is destroyed after advancing, the payment is valid; if the wealth increases, he may need to pay more. The detailed conditions are in the commentaries.

Key Terms
تَقْدِيم الزَّكَاة (taqdīm al-zakāt): Paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year.
النِّصَاب (al-nisāb): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, under what condition is advancing zakat before the year end permissible?
A) One must have owned the nisab throughout the year.
B) One must own the nisab at the time of advancing.
C) One must have completed half the year.
D) One must obtain permission from the ruler.

Key Takeaway
Advancing zakat before the year end is permissible in the Hanafi school as long as the payer owns the nisab at the time of payment, based on the hadith of Abbas.

Zakat of Horses: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States ruling on zakat of horses with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad/Zufar on zakat of horses and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold zakat wajib on all horses; Muhammad and Zufar restrict it to al-basab and al-'ufus.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents a notable intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether zakat is obligatory on all horses or only certain types. The majority view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf generalizes zakat to all horses, while Muhammad and Zufar limit it to specific types. Understanding the basis and implications of this disagreement is key to applying the school's rulings in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the text carefully: 'Muhammad and Zufar said: It applies to al-basab and al-'ufus. And zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is wajib.' Identify which imams hold which view.
Al-basab and al-'ufus are likely specific types of horses (mares and stallions).
2
Understand the basis of each position
The general view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf likely analogizes horses to other grazing livestock (sa'imah). The restricted view of Muhammad and Zufar may consider only horses used for breeding or work as subject to zakat.
The text cites a hadith about silver nisab as a proof for the general view, though it may be misplaced; it is used by analogy.
3
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under the majority, every horse owner pays zakat annually. Under the minority, only owners of al-basab and al-'ufus pay, which may exempt most horse owners.
Later Hanafi practice generally follows the minority view, making zakat on horses rare.
4
Assess the tarjih status
The passage does not explicitly choose one view. In later Hanafi works, the mufta bihi position is that zakat is not wajib on horses except possibly for certain types, aligning with Muhammad and Zufar.
This is an example of a dispute within the school that later scholars resolved.

Chapter of Zakat of Horses. Muhammad and Zufar said: It applies to al-basab and al-'ufus. And if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, zakat drops from him. And if he gives zakat before the year while he owns the nisab, it is valid. Proof (2): The hadith to establish that zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is wajib. So when it is two hundred dirhams, then on it five dirhams; and what is in excess is according to that proportion. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of Zakat of Sa'imah, no. 1572; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 9947). Proof (1): The statement of a tabi'i to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from 'Ata' about a man who gave zakat of his wealth and it was lost, that it suffices for him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10492; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 6968). Proof (2): The statement of a sahabi to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from Mughirah, from his companions, they said: 'If a man gives zakat of his wealth and it is lost, he should give zakat again.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10490). Proof (3): The hadith to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from 'Ali, that al-'Abbas asked the Prophet (SAW) about hastening his charity before it became due, and he permitted him that. (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1624; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 678). Principle: Zakat is not wajib on less than forty dirhams. So initially after forty, as long as the remaining dirhams do not complete forty, they are 'afw (exempt).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its sharh, covers multiple rulings under the chapter of zakat on horses. The passage begins by stating the ruling on zakat of horses: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar, zakat applies only to specific types of horses referred to as 'al-basab' and 'al-'ufus' (likely mares and stallions used for breeding or work). Then it presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that zakat is wajib on horses in general, and a hadith regarding silver nisab is cited as proof, though it appears misplaced. Next, the passage addresses two general zakat rules: (1) if the wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory (e.g., at the end of the year), the obligation drops and nothing is due; (2) if one pays zakat before the end of the year while still owning the nisab, it is valid. Proofs for these rules are provided from the statements of tabi'un (like 'Ata'), sahabah (like Mughirah's companions), and a hadith about al-'Abbas hastening his charity. The Urdu note at the end clarifies that no zakat is due on less than forty dirhams, and amounts between forty and the next forty are exempt until the total reaches the next nisab increment.

Key Terms
البَصَاب (al-basab): A type of horse; likely mares or horses used for breeding.
العَفْوس (al-'ufus): A type of horse; likely stallions or work horses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two Hanafi imams restricted zakat on horses to specific types?
A) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
B) Muhammad and Zufar
C) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
D) Zufar and Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on horse zakat; the relied-upon position is that only certain types are subject to zakat.

Rules on Perishing of Wealth and Advancing Zakat
States general zakat rules on perishing and advancing with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules when zakatable wealth perishes after the obligation is due and whether advancing zakat before the year is valid, and cite the proofs.

Core Idea
If wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, the obligation drops; but paying zakat before the year is valid if nisab is owned.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two practical zakat scenarios: loss of wealth after the year ends, and early payment. The rulings protect the owner from double liability and provide flexibility. The proofs come from the practices of the Companions and a hadith about al-'Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rules
The text states two rules: (1) If wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory (e.g., at the end of the year), the obligation drops (saqatat). (2) If a person pays zakat before the year ends while still owning the nisab, it is valid (ja'iz).
Both rules are practical concessions.
2
Examine the condition for advancing zakat
The condition for valid early payment is that the person owns the nisab at the time of payment. If the nisab is lost later before the year ends, the payment remains valid.
This encourages early discharge without risk of loss.
3
Analyze the proofs for the perishing rule
The text cites two proofs: the statement of 'Ata' (a tabi'i) that if the zakat payment is lost after being given, it suffices; and the statement of Mughirah's companions that if the zakat is lost, one must pay again. Note these seem contradictory? Actually they address different scenarios: one is about the obligation dropping if wealth perishes before payment, the other about if the payment itself is lost. The passage uses them for the same rule? Clarify in commentary.
The proofs are from tabi'i and sahabi, not direct hadith.
4
Analyze the proof for advancing zakat
The hadith of al-'Abbas: He asked the Prophet (SAW) about hastening sadaqah before it was due, and he permitted it. This establishes the validity of advancing zakat.
This is a clear dalil from Sunnah.
5
Apply the rules to scenarios
Practice: If you had £10,000 in savings for a year and it was stolen on the last day before you paid zakat, you owe nothing. If you paid £250 in advance during the year while still having the nisab, it's valid even if you later lose the money.
These rules prevent hardship.

Chapter of Zakat of Horses. Muhammad and Zufar said: It applies to al-basab and al-'ufus. And if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, zakat drops from him. And if he gives zakat before the year while he owns the nisab, it is valid. Proof (2): The hadith to establish that zakat according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is wajib. So when it is two hundred dirhams, then on it five dirhams; and what is in excess is according to that proportion. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of Zakat of Sa'imah, no. 1572; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 9947). Proof (1): The statement of a tabi'i to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from 'Ata' about a man who gave zakat of his wealth and it was lost, that it suffices for him. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10492; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 6968). Proof (2): The statement of a sahabi to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from Mughirah, from his companions, they said: 'If a man gives zakat of his wealth and it is lost, he should give zakat again.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10490). Proof (3): The hadith to establish that if wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory, it drops from him: from 'Ali, that al-'Abbas asked the Prophet (SAW) about hastening his charity before it became due, and he permitted him that. (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1624; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 678). Principle: Zakat is not wajib on less than forty dirhams. So initially after forty, as long as the remaining dirhams do not complete forty, they are 'afw (exempt).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its sharh, covers multiple rulings under the chapter of zakat on horses. The passage begins by stating the ruling on zakat of horses: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar, zakat applies only to specific types of horses referred to as 'al-basab' and 'al-'ufus' (likely mares and stallions used for breeding or work). Then it presents the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that zakat is wajib on horses in general, and a hadith regarding silver nisab is cited as proof, though it appears misplaced. Next, the passage addresses two general zakat rules: (1) if the wealth perishes after zakat becomes obligatory (e.g., at the end of the year), the obligation drops and nothing is due; (2) if one pays zakat before the end of the year while still owning the nisab, it is valid. Proofs for these rules are provided from the statements of tabi'un (like 'Ata'), sahabah (like Mughirah's companions), and a hadith about al-'Abbas hastening his charity. The Urdu note at the end clarifies that no zakat is due on less than forty dirhams, and amounts between forty and the next forty are exempt until the total reaches the next nisab increment.

Key Terms
سَقَطَتْ (saqatat): Zakat obligation falls (is cancelled) upon loss of wealth after it became due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
If wealth perishes after zakat is owed, no payment is required; early payment is valid if nisab is owned at payment time.

Zakat of Silver: Nisab, Rate, and Proofs
States the nisab (200 dirhams) and zakat rate (2.5%) for silver, with detailed increment rule of 40 dirhams, supported by multiple proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab for silver (200 dirhams), calculate the zakat due on a given silver amount using the 40-dirham increment rule, and identify the proofs from Quran, Hadith, and Sahaba that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
No zakat on silver below 200 dirhams; 2.5% on the nisab, then 1 dirham for every extra 40 dirhams.

This lesson covers the core obligation of zakat on silver. We will learn the minimum threshold (nisab), the exact rate, and how to calculate zakat on amounts above the nisab. The Hanafi school establishes these rules with clear proofs from the Quran, the Sunnah, and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Conditions
The text states that no zakat is due on less than 200 dirhams. This is the nisab. When one has exactly 200 dirhams, zakat is 5 dirhams (2.5%). Also note the condition of a full year (hawl) mentioned in the Urdu summary.
The nisab is the minimum threshold; hawl is implicitly required.
2
Understand the Increment Rule
For amounts above 200 dirhams, no additional zakat is due until the excess reaches 40 dirhams. Then for each 40 dirhams, 1 dirham is due. So zakat is calculated in 40-dirham chunks after the first 200.
The increment rule ensures that small amounts are not burdened.
3
Analyze the First Set of Proofs
The hadith of the woman with gold bracelets (Sunan Abi Dawud) establishes zakat on gold, and by analogy (qiyas) on silver. Also the Quranic verse (9:34) on hoarding sets the general obligation.
4
Examine the Hadith on the Thresholds
The hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri establishes the nisab for silver as 5 awaq (200 dirhams). The hadith from Mu'adh specifies the increment rule: no zakat on broken coins, and the 40-dirham increment.
These ahadith directly support the ruling.
5
Confirm with the Sahabi Statement
The command of 'Ali (RA) to take quarter of a tenth (2.5%) on every 40 dirhams further confirms the rate and the increment system.

Source Text

بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْفِضَّةِ
لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم فَفِيهَا خَمْسَةُ دَرَاهِمَ لا وَلَا شَيْءَ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا فَيَكُونُ فِيهَا دِرْهَم مَعَ الْخَمْسَةِ ثُمَّ فِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا دِرْهُمْ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ \ أَنَّ امْرَأَةً أَتَتْ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَمَعَهَا ابْنَةٌ لَهَا، وَفِي يَدِ ابْنَتِهَا مَسَكَتَانِ غَلِيظَتَانِ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ، فَقَالَ لَهَا: «أَتُعْطِينَ زَكَاةَ هَذَا؟»، قَالَتْ: لَا ، قَالَ: «أَيَسُرُّكِ أَنْ يُسَوِرَكِ اللَّهُ بِهِمَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ سِوَارَيْنِ مِنْ نَارٍ؟»، قَالَ: فَخَلَعَتْهُمَا، فَأَلْقَتْهُمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَالَتْ: هُمَا لِلَّهِ عز وجل وَلِرَسُولِهِ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الْكَنْزِ مَا هُوَ؟ وَزَكَاةِ الحَلِي، نمبر 1563)
وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَكْنِزُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا يُنفِقُونَهَا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَبَشِّرْهُم بِعَذَابٍ أَلِيم سورة التوبة، 9، أيت نمبر 34) ا وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ ) سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : «لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْس ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الإِبل، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقِ صَدَقَةٌ»، (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْوَرِقِ، نمبر 1447/(مسلم شریف، کتاب الزكاة، نمبر 979/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1572)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا شَيْءٍ فِي الرِّيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَما \ عَنْ مُعَادٍ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ حِينَ وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ: «أَنْ لا تَأْخُذَ مِنَ الْكَسْرِ شَيْئًا ، إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَرِقُ مِائَيَّ دِرْهَم فَخُذْ مِنْهَا خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ ، وَلَا تَأْخُذْ مِمَّا زَادَ شَيْئًا حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا ، وَإِذَا بَلَغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا فَخُذْ مِنْهُ دِرْهَما»، (سنن دارقطني بَابٌ: لَيْسَ فِي الْكَسْرِ شَيْء نمبر 1903)
وجه:(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا شَيْءٍ فِي الزِيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا اعَنْ عَلِي ، .... هَاتُوارُبْعَ الْعُشُورِ، مِنْ كُلِ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا دِرْهُمْ، سنن ابوداود بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1572) اصول چاندی خواہ کسی شکل بھی میں ہو جب وہ دو سو درہم کی مقدار کو پہنچ جائیں، اور ایک سال پورا گزر جائے تو اس میں پانچ درہم زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔
Chapter of Zakat of Silver. There is no sadaqah on less than two hundred dirhams. So when it is two hundred dirhams, then on it five dirhams. And nothing on the increase until it reaches forty dirhams, then on it is one dirham along with the five. Then on every forty dirhams, one dirham. Proof (1): Hadith to establish that there is no sadaqah on less than two hundred dirhams: A woman came to the Messenger of Allah (SAW) with her daughter, and on the daughter's hand were two thick bracelets of gold, so he said to her: 'Do you give zakat on this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah will adorn you with two bracelets of fire?' So she removed them and threw them to the Prophet (SAW) and said: 'They are for Allah and His Messenger.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1563). Proof (2): The verse to establish: 'And those who hoard gold and silver and do not spend them in the way of Allah, give them tidings of a painful torment' (Quran 9:34). Proof (1): Hadith to establish: I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: The Messenger of Allah said: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five dhud of camels, and no sadaqah on less than five awaq [of silver], and no sadaqah on less than five awsuq [of grain].' (Bukhari, no. 1447; Muslim, no. 979; Abu Dawud, no. 1572). Proof (1): Hadith to establish that there is nothing on the increase until it reaches forty dirhams: From Mu'adh, that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) commanded him when he sent him to Yemen: 'Do not take anything from the broken [coins]; if the wariq is two hundred dirhams, take from it five dirhams, and do not take anything from what is added until it reaches forty dirhams, and when it reaches forty dirhams, take from it one dirham.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, no. 1903). Proof (2): Statement of a sahabi: From 'Ali... 'hand over a quarter of the tenth, from every forty dirhams, one dirham.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1572). Principle: Silver, in whatever form it may be, when it reaches the amount of two hundred dirhams and a full year passes, then zakat of five dirhams is wajib on it.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, with its commentary, clarifies the nisab and zakat rate for silver. The ruling is that no zakat is due on less than 200 dirhams of silver. When one has exactly 200 dirhams, zakat is 5 dirhams (2.5%). For any excess above 200, no zakat is due until that excess reaches 40 dirhams, at which point an additional 1 dirham is due, and then for every subsequent 40 dirhams, 1 dirham. This means zakat on silver is calculated in increments of 40 dirhams after the initial nisab. The passage then provides multiple proofs: (1) a hadith about a woman with gold bracelets, though it actually pertains to gold, it is used as evidence that zakat is due on ornamental metal; (2) Quranic verse (9:34) condemning hoarding; (3) a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri setting minimum thresholds for zakat on camels, silver, and grains; (4) a hadith from Mu'adh instructing him not to take zakat from broken coins and detailing the 40-dirham increment; (5) a hadith from 'Ali commanding a quarter of a tenth (i.e., 2.5%) on every 40 dirhams. The Urdu summary reiterates that zakat on silver is wajib when it reaches 200 dirhams and a year passes, regardless of the form (coins, ingots, etc.).

Key Terms
نصاب (nisab): Minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory; for silver it is 200 dirhams.
الْوَرِق (al-wariq): Silver coins or silver in general.
الْكَسْر (al-kasr): Broken or damaged silver coins; not subject to zakat until 40 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) 9 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The zakat on silver is calculated as 5 dirhams on the first 200, then 1 dirham for every additional 40 dirhams, based on clear proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and Sahaba.

Zakat on Silver: Nisab, Excess, and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Establishes zakat rules for silver nisab and alloyed coins with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi nisab for silver zakat, apply Abu Hanifa's rule for calculating zakat on excess, and explain the difference with the Sahibayn's proportional method.

Core Idea
Silver zakat: 200 dirhams nisab; each extra 40 dirhams incurs 1 dirham zakat (Abu Hanifa), but Sahibayn tax any excess proportionally.

This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi ruling on zakat for silver. You will learn the nisab threshold, the method for calculating zakat on amounts exceeding the nisab, and the intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The passage also clarifies the treatment of alloyed silver coins, which has practical implications for modern bullion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab and basic zakat
Read the first line: no zakat below 200 dirhams; at 200 dirhams, 5 dirhams (2.5%) are due. This is the established rule for the nisab of silver.
The nisab of silver is 200 dirhams (approx. 595 grams).
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's rule for excess
The matn states: no zakat on the excess until it reaches 40 dirhams, then 1 dirham for each complete 40 dirhams. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The rule: zakat on excess is due only in increments of 40 dirhams.
3
Contrast with the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that any excess above 200 dirhams is zakatable proportionally at 2.5%, without waiting for complete 40 dirham units.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Examine the proofs
Look at the hadith evidence: the hadith of Mu'adh (Darqutni) supports Abu Hanifa; the hadith of 'Ali (Abu Dawud) is used by the Sahibayn. The Hanafi response reconciles the texts.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is Abu Hanifa's.
5
Apply the rule to a numeric example
For 220 dirhams: Abu Hanifa says zakat = 5 dirhams (only on 200); Sahibayn say 5.5 dirhams (2.5% of 220). See the practical difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is clear.
6
Learn the ruling for alloyed coins
If silver is dominant in the coin, treat as silver; if adulteration (ghish) is dominant, treat as trade goods ('urud) — zakat depends on value reaching nisab.
This determines whether the coin qualifies as silver for zakat purposes.
