بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْفِضَّةِ
لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ فَفِيهَا خَمْسَةُ دَرَاهِمَ وَلَا شَيْءَ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمًا فَيَكُونُ فِيهَا دِرْهَمٌ مَعَ الْخَمْسَةِ ثُمَّ فِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمًا دِرْهَمٌ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ : أَنَّ امْرَأَةً أَتَتْ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَمَعَهَا ابْنَةٌ لَهَا، وَفِي يَدِ ابْنَتِهَا مَسَكَتَانِ غَلِيظَتَانِ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ، فَقَالَ لَهَا: «أَتُعْطِينَ زَكَاةَ هَذَا؟»، قَالَتْ: لَا ، قَالَ: «أَيَسُرُّكِ أَنْ يُسَوِرَكِ اللَّهُ بِهِمَا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ سِوَارَيْنِ مِنْ نَارٍ؟»، قَالَ: فَخَلَعَتْهُمَا، فَأَلْقَتْهُمَا إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَقَالَتْ: هُمَا لِلَّهِ عز وجل وَلِرَسُولِهِ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الْكَنْزِ مَا هُوَ؟ وَزَكَاةِ الحَلِي، نمبر 1563)
وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يَكْنِزُونَ الذَّهَبَ وَالْفِضَّةَ وَلَا يُنفِقُونَهَا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَبَشِّرْهُم بِعَذَابٍ أَلِيم﴾ سورة التوبة، 9، أيت نمبر 34
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت لَيْسَ فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَم صَدَقَةٌ : سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ : «لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْس ذَوْدٍ صَدَقَةٌ مِنَ الإِبل، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقِ صَدَقَةٌ»، (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْوَرِقِ، نمبر 1447/مسلم شریف، کتاب الزكاة، نمبر 979/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1572)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا شَيْءٍ فِي الرِّيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَما : عَنْ مُعَادٍ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَهُ حِينَ وَجَّهَهُ إِلَى الْيَمَنِ: «أَنْ لا تَأْخُذَ مِنَ الْكَسْرِ شَيْئًا ، إِذَا كَانَتِ الْوَرِقُ مِائَيَّ دِرْهَم فَخُذْ مِنْهَا خَمْسَةَ دَرَاهِمَ ، وَلَا تَأْخُذْ مِمَّا زَادَ شَيْئًا حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا ، وَإِذَا بَلَغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا فَخُذْ مِنْهُ دِرْهَما»، (سنن دارقطني بَابٌ: لَيْسَ فِي الْكَسْرِ شَيْء نمبر 1903)
وجه:(۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا شَيْءٍ فِي الزِيَادَةِ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا : عَنْ عَلِي ، .... هَاتُوارُبْعَ الْعُشُورِ، مِنْ كُلِ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا دِرْهُمْ، سنن ابوداود بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ، نمبر 1572)
اصول: چاندی خواہ کسی شکل بھی میں ہو جب وہ دو سو درہم کی مقدار کو پہنچ جائیں، اور ایک سال پورا گزر جائے تو اس میں پانچ درہم زکوۃ واجب ہو گی۔
وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ مَا زَادَ عَلَى الْمِائَتَيْنِ فَزَكَاتُهُ بِحِسَابِهِ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الْوَرِقِ الْفِضَّةُ فَهِيَ فِي حُكْمِ الْفِضَّةِ وَإِذَا كَانَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَيْهَا الْغِشُ فَهِيَ فِي حُكْمِ الْعُرُوضِ وَيُعْتَبَرُ أَنْ تَبْلُغَ قِيمَتَهَا نِصَابًا
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ مَا زَادَ عَلَى الْمِائَتَيْنِ : عَنْ عَلِي ، - قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ : أَحْسَبُهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ لا أَنَّه قَالَ: «هَاتُوا رُبِّعَ الْعُشُورِ، مِنْ كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ دِرْهَمَا دِرْهُمْ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ شَيْءٌ حَتَّى تَتِمَّ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ، فَإِذَا كَانَتْ مِائَتَيْ دِرْهَمٍ، فَفِيهَا خَمْسَةٌ دَرَاهِمَ، فَمَا زَادَ فَعَلَى حِسَابِ ذَلِكَ ، سنن ابوداود بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ ، نمبر 1572/سنن بيهقي، بَابُ وُجُوبِ ربعِ الْعُشْرِ فِي نِصَابِهَا وَفِيمَا زَادَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ قَلَّتِ الرِّيَادَةُ، نمبر 7521)
اصول: چاندی کے سکوں میں چاندی غالب ہے تو چاندی کے حکم میں ہے اور چاندی مغلوب ہے تو سامان کے حکم میں ہے۔
Chapter of Zakat of Silver. There is no charity in less than two hundred dirhams. When there are two hundred dirhams, then in it five dirhams. There is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty dirhams, then in it one dirham along with the five. Then in every forty dirhams, one dirham. Evidence (1) the hadith to establish 'There is no charity in less than two hundred dirhams': A woman came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with her daughter, and on the daughter's hand were two thick bracelets of gold. He said to her: 'Do you give zakat for this?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'Would it please you that Allah should adorn you with two bracelets of fire on the Day of Resurrection?' He said: So she removed them and threw them to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: 'They are for Allah Almighty and His Messenger.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, Bab al-Kanz, Hadith 1563). Evidence (2) the verse to establish 'There is no charity in less than two hundred dirhams': 'And those who hoard gold and silver and spend them not in the way of Allah, give them tidings of a painful punishment' (Surah at-Tawbah, 9:34). Evidence (1) the hadith to establish 'There is no charity in less than two hundred dirhams': I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no charity in less than five camels, and no charity in less than five awāq [of silver], and no charity in less than five wasqs.' (Bukhari, Bab Zakat al-Wariq, Hadith 1447; Muslim, Kitab al-Zakat, Hadith 979; Abu Dawud, Bab fi Zakat al-Sa'imah, Hadith 1572). Evidence (1) the hadith to establish 'There is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty dirhams': From Mu'adh, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded him when he sent him to Yemen: 'Do not take anything from the broken (coins). When the silver is two hundred dirhams, take from it five dirhams; and do not take anything from what is added until it reaches forty dirhams; and when it reaches forty dirhams, take from it one dirham.' (Sunan al-Darqutni, Bab: laysa fi al-kasr shay', Hadith 1903). Evidence (2) the saying of the Companion to establish 'There is nothing in the excess until it reaches forty dirhams': From Ali... 'Give a quarter of the tenth (2.5%), from every forty dirhams one dirham.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, Bab fi Zakat al-Sa'imah, Hadith 1572). Principle: Silver, whatever form it is in, when it reaches the amount of two hundred dirhams, and a full year passes, then five dirhams of zakat become obligatory. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Whatever exceeds two hundred, its zakat is in proportion to it. And when the predominant (metal) in the silver coins is silver, then it is considered as silver; and when the predominant (metal) in them is adulteration, then it is considered as trade goods, and it is required that its value reaches the nisab. Evidence (1) the hadith to establish 'And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Whatever exceeds two hundred...' From Ali... (Zuheyr said: I think it is from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said): 'Give a quarter of the tenth, from every forty dirhams one dirham, and nothing is due from you until it reaches two hundred dirhams. When it reaches two hundred dirhams, then in it five dirhams, and whatever exceeds, then in proportion to that.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, Bab fi Zakat al-Sa'imah, Hadith 1572; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab wujub rub' al-'ushr fi nisabiha wa fima zada 'alayhi wa in qallat al-ziyada, Hadith 7521). Principle: If silver dominates in the silver coins, then it is in the ruling of silver; and if silver is dominated, then it is in the ruling of trade goods.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn, expanded with hadith evidence and usul (principles), addresses zakat on silver. It first states the basic ruling: no zakat on silver below 200 dirhams. At the nisab of 200 dirhams, zakat is 5 dirhams (2.5%). For any excess above 200, according to the matn (Imam Abu Hanifa's view), no zakat is due until the excess reaches 40 dirhams; then 1 dirham is due for that 40, and so on. This means each additional 40 dirhams, once complete, incur 1 dirham zakat. Evidence is provided from hadith: the narration of Mu'adh instructing not to take anything from the surplus until 40 dirhams, and the saying of 'Ali. Then the text presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that any excess over the nisab is zakatable proportionally at the same rate (2.5%), without waiting for complete 40 dirhams. Their evidence is the hadith of 'Ali: 'whatever exceeds, then in proportion to that.' The text also provides a usul (principle) on alloyed silver coins: if the coin is predominantly silver (al-ghalib 'ala al-wariq al-fiddah), it is treated as silver for zakat purposes; if the adulteration (ghish) is predominant, it is treated as trade goods ('urud) and its value must reach the nisab for zakat to be due. The commentary (usul) adds that silver in any form, whether coins or bullion, if it reaches 200 dirhams and a year passes, zakat is due. The madhhab dispute on the method of calculating zakat on excess and the ruling on alloyed coins are important practical differences within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
وَرِق (wariq): Silver coins (dirhams) used as currency.
غِش (ghish): Adulteration or base metal mixed with silver in coins.
عُرُوض (urud): Trade goods or commodities other than gold and silver used for business.
نِصَاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn (Abu Hanifa's position), what zakat is due on 230 dirhams of silver held for one year?
A) 5 dirhams
B) 5.75 dirhams
C) 6 dirhams
D) 0 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's: zakat on silver is calculated on complete units of 40 dirhams beyond the nisab of 200 dirhams.

Zakat of Gold: Nisab and Rate
Ruling on nisab and rate for gold zakat with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab (20 mithqals) and rate (2.5%) for gold zakat according to the Hanafi school, and identify the hadith from Ali that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Gold zakat is wajib on 20 mithqals after one year at half a mithqal.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling on zakat for gold as presented in Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. You will learn the precise nisab threshold, the rate due, and the key prophetic tradition that establishes this obligation. The passage also clarifies that zakat applies to all forms of gold, including jewelry and ingots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on zakat for gold. Determine the hukm level and the conditions that trigger it.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the dalil is zanni al-thubut (single-transmission hadith).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ali (RA) to prove the nisab and rate. Find the specific wording.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Identify how the hadith explicitly fixes the nisab at 20 dinars and the zakat at half a dinar.
The imperative form indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools exempt jewelry from zakat. See how the Hanafi school responds.
The text affirms zakat on all forms, including huli (jewelry).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative). No intra-Hanafi dispute is noted here.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

بَابُ زَكَاةِ الذَّهَبِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ الذَّهَبِ صَدَقَةٌ فَإِذَا كَانَتْ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْخَوْلُ فَفِيهَا نِصْفُ مِثْقَالِ ٣ـ وَفِي تِبْر الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَحُلِيهِمَا وَالْآنِيَةِ مِنْهُمَا الزَّكَاةُ
ل وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ الذَّهَبِ صَدَقَةٌ \ عَنْ عَلِيَّ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِبَعْضِ أَوَّلِ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ، قَالَ: «فَإِذَا كَانَتْ لَكَ مِائَتَا دِرْهَمٍ، وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْخَوْلُ، فَفِيهَا خَمْسَةُ دَرَاهِمَ، وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكَ شَيْءٌ - يَعْنِي – فِي الذَّهَبِ حَتَّى يَكُونَ لَكَ عِشْرُونَ دِينَارًا، فَإِذَا كَانَ لَكَ عِشْرُونَ دِينَارًا، وَحَالَ عَلَيْهَا الْخَوْلُ، فَفِيهَا نِصْفُ دِينَارٍ، فَمَا زَادَ، فَبِحِسَابِ ذَلِكَ»، قَالَ: فَلَا أَدْرِي أَعَلِيٌّ يَقُولُ : فَبِحِسَابِ ذَلِكَ،(سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي زَكَاةِ السَّائِمَةِ نمبر 1573/سنن ابن ماجه ، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْوَرِقِ وَالذَّهَبِ، نمبر 1791)
وجه: (ا) قول التابعي لثبوت قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ عِشْرِينَ مِثْقَالًا مِنْ الذَّهَبِ صَدَقَةٌ قَالَ عَطَاءُ: «لَا يَكُونُ فِي مَالٍ صَدَقَةٌ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ عِشْرِينَ دِينَارًا، فَإِذَا بَلَغَتْ عِشْرِينَ دِينَارًا فَفِيهَا دِينَارٌ، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعَةِ دَنَانِيرَ يَزِيدُهَا مِنَ الْمَالِ دِرْهَمْ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ أَرْبَعِينَ دِينَارًا، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعِينَ دِينَارًا دِينَارٌ، وَفِي كُلِّ أَرْبَعَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ دِينَارًا نِصْفُ دِينَارٍ وَدِرْهَمْ»» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الدَّنَانِيرِ مَا يُؤْخَذُ مِنْهَا فِي الزَّكَاةِ، نمبر 9883
وجه:(1) الحديث لثبوت وَفِي تِبْرِ الذَّهَبِ وَالْفِضَّةِ وَحُلِيِّهِمَا \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَتْ تَلِي بَنَاتِ أَخِيهَا يَتَامَى فِي حِجْرِهَا فَهُنَّ الخَلِيُّ فَلَا تُخْرِجُ مِنْهُ الزَّكَاةَ ""(سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ لَا زَكَاةَ فِي الخَلِي، نمبر 7535)
اصول ہیں مثقال سے کم میں کوئی زکوۃ نہیں ہے اور بیس مثقال میں نصف مثقال واجب ہو گا، پھر ہر ہیں
میں نصف مثقال واجب ہو تا چلا جائے گا، اور جو نہیں سے کم ہے اس میں کوئی زکوۃ لازم نہیں ہو گی۔ اصول : سونا اور چاندی خواہ کسی شکل میں ہوں اور چاہے استعمالی ہوں یا غیر استعمالی، جب وہ نصاب کو پہنچ جائیں تو ان کا چالیسواں حصہ زکوۃ میں دینا واجب ہے کیوں کہ قرآن مجید میں مطلق سونے اور چاندی کی زکوۃ کا حکم دیا گیا ہے۔
Chapter of Zakat of Gold. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: There is no charity in less than twenty mithqals of gold. When it reaches twenty mithqals and a year passes, then half a mithqal is due. And in gold and silver ingots, their jewelry, and vessels made of them, zakat is obligatory. Proof (1): Hadith for establishing the author's statement: from Ali from the Prophet, part of this hadith: 'When you have two hundred dirhams and a year passes, five dirhams are due; you owe nothing on gold until you have twenty dinars; when you have twenty dinars and a year passes, half a dinar is due; for any increase, calculate accordingly.' He said: I do not know if Ali said 'calculate accordingly.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab Zakat al-Sa'imah, no. 1573/Sunan Ibn Majah, Bab Zakat al-Wariq wa al-Dhahab, no. 1791). Proof (a): Statement of a Tabi'i: Ata said: 'There is no zakat on wealth until it reaches twenty dinars; when it reaches twenty dinars, one dinar is due; for every four dinars increase, one dirham until it reaches forty dinars; for each forty dinars, one dinar; for each twenty-four dinars, half a dinar and one dirham.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 9883). Proof (1): Hadith for establishing the ruling on ingots and jewelry: from Aisha, wife of the Prophet, that she was raising orphaned nieces, and they had jewelry from which she did not pay zakat. (Sunan Bayhaqi, Bab Man Qala La Zakata fi al-Huli, no. 7535). Principles: There is no zakat in less than twenty mithqals; at twenty mithqals, half a mithqal is obligatory, and then for each additional [twenty] mithqals, half a mithqal is obligatory. Whatever is less than that does not require zakat. Principle: Gold and silver, regardless of form, whether used or unused, when they reach the nisab, one-fortieth is wajib as zakat, because the Quran commands zakat on gold and silver absolutely.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states the ruling on zakat of gold. It first establishes the nisab: no zakat on gold less than 20 mithqals. Once gold reaches 20 mithqals and a lunar year passes, the zakat due is half a mithqal (2.5%). The author then clarifies that zakat is obligatory on gold and silver in all forms: ingots (tibr), jewelry (huli), and vessels (aniya). This is supported by hadith from Ali ibn Abi Talib and the practice of Ata' ibn Abi Rabah. The Urdu commentary reinforces that the nisab applies regardless of whether the gold is in use or not, based on the general command in the Quran.

Key Terms
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight for gold, approximately 4.25 grams. Used to define the nisab for gold.
تبر (tibr): Gold or silver in its raw form, such as ingots or nuggets, as opposed to coins or jewelry.
حلية (huliya (pl. huli)): Jewelry made of gold or silver, including items worn for adornment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Quduri, what is the minimum amount of gold (in mithqals) that triggers zakat after one year?
A) 10 mithqals
B) 20 mithqals
C) 40 mithqals
D) 1 mithqal

Key Takeaway
The nisab for gold zakat is 20 mithqals (approx. 85g), and the rate is 2.5% (half a mithqal per 20 mithqals) after one lunar year, applicable to all forms of gold including jewelry.

Zakat on Trade Goods and Mixing Gold and Silver
Ruling on zakat on trade goods and intra-Hanafi dispute on mixing gold and silver for nisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of zakat on trade goods in the Hanafi school and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on mixing gold and silver by value vs. weight, including the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Zakat on trade goods is wajib; gold and silver may be mixed by value to complete nisab according to Abu Hanifa.

This passage from Al-Quduri establishes the obligation of zakat on trade goods and addresses how to combine gold and silver when each individually falls short of the nisab. The Hanafi school is unanimous on the obligation, but a significant intra-madhhab disagreement exists between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, on the method of mixing. Understanding this dispute and its practical consequences is essential for correct zakat calculation in mixed assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on trade goods
State that zakat is wajib on goods intended for sale, based on hadith evidence. The passage explicitly says 'al-zakatu wajibatun fi urud al-tijarah.'
This is the established Hanafi position, supported by the hadith from Samurah ibn Jundab.
2
Recognize the nisab condition
The nisab must be complete at the beginning and end of the lunar year; temporary decrease in between does not break the obligation. The value of trade goods is added to gold and silver to determine nisab.
This is the general rule for zakat on trade goods.
3
State the dispute on mixing gold and silver
Abu Hanifa holds that gold and silver are mixed by value (bi al-qimah) to complete the nisab. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that mixing is by weight (bi al-ajza').
This is the core intra-madhhab difference.
4
Examine the proofs
The hadith evidence for the obligation is provided. For the mixing method, the debate is based on analogy: Abu Hanifa considers both as mediums of exchange, so value equivalence suffices; Sahibayn argue for weight precision as the nisab texts specify weight.
The passage explicitly cites two hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud and Sunan Darqutni for the obligation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical effect
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view (mixing by value), as recorded in major works like Al-Hidayah. This means that if the total value of gold and silver together reaches the nisab of either, zakat is due on the combined value.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Sahibayn, mixing only occurs if the combined weight reaches the nisab of one type; under Abu Hanifa, value mixing allows reaching nisab more easily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْعُرُوضِ
الزَّكَاةَ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي عُرُوض التِّجَارَةِ كَائِنَةً مَا كَانَتْ يُقَوَمُهَا بِمَا هُوَ أَنْفَعُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ وَإِذَا كَانَ النِّصَابُ كَامِلًا فِي طَرَفَيْ الْحَوْلِ فَنُقْصَانُهُ فِيمَا بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ لَا يُسْقِطُ الزَّكَاةَ وَتُضَمُّ قِيمَةُ الْعُرُوض إلَى الذَّهَب وَالْفِضَّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ يُضَمُّ الذَّهَبُ إلَى الْفِضَّةِ بِالْقِيمَةِ حَتَّى يَتِمَّ النِّصَابُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لا يُضَمُ الذَّهَبُ إلَى الْفِضَّةِ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَيُضَمُّ بِالْأَجْزَاءِ وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت الزَّكَاة وَاجِبَةٌ فِي عُرُوضِ التَّجَارَةِ كَائِنَةَ \ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ، حَدَّثَنِي خُبَيْبُ بْنُ سُلَيْمَانَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ سُلَيْمَانَ، عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ ، قَالَ: «أَمَّا بَعْدُ، فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يَأْمُرُنَا أَنْ تُخْرِجَ الصَّدَقَةَ مِنَ الَّذِي نُعِدُّ لِلْبَيْعِ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الْعُرُوضِ إِذَا كَانَتْ لِلتِّجَارَةِ، هَلْ فِيهَا مِنْ زَكَاةٍ، نمبر 1562)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت الزَّكاةُ وَاجِبَةٌ فِي عُرُوضِ التِّجَارَةِ كَائِنَةَ \ عَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ ، قَالَ : " بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ} [الفاتحة: 1] مِنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدَبٍ إِلَى بَنِيهِ سَلَامٌ عَلَيْكُمْ ، أَمَّا بَعْدُ فَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ يَأْمُرُنَا بِرَقِيقِ الرَّجُلِ أَوِ الْمَرْأَةِ الَّذِينَ هُمْ تِلَادٌ لَهُ وَهُمْ عُمْلَةٌ لَا يُرِيدُ بَيْعَهُمْ ، فَكَانَ يَأْمُرُنَا أَنْ لَا تُخْرِجَ عَنْهُمْ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ شَيْئًا وَكَانَ يَأْمُرُنَا أَنْ تُخْرِجَ مِنَ الرَّقِيقِ الَّذِي يُعَدُّ لِلْبَيْعِ
سنن دارقطني، بَابُ زَكَاةِ مَالِ التِّجَارَةِ وَسُقُوطِهَا عَنِ الْخَيْلِ وَالرَّقِيقِ، نمبر 2027)
اصول: سونا اور چاندی کے علاوہ سامان میں بھی زکوۃ واجب ہو گی جبکہ وہ حوائج اصلیہ سے زائد ہو، سال گزر جائے اور سونے یا چاندی کے نصاب کو پہنچ جائے تو چالیسواں حصہ واجب ہو گا۔ اصول : جب سونا یا چاندی، دونوں میں سے کسی کا نصاب مکمل نہ ہو رہا ہو تو ایک دوسرے میں ضم کیا جائے گا اور ملانے کے بعد دونوں کی قیمت، سونا یا چاندی میں سے جس کے نصاب کو بھی پہنچ جائے اس کے اعتبار سے زکوۃ دیدی جائے گی۔
Chapter of Zakat of Trade Goods. Zakat is obligatory on trade goods, whatever they may be. They are valued by what is most beneficial for the poor and needy. If the nisab is complete at both ends of the year, its decrease in between does not drop the zakat. The value of trade goods is added to gold and silver, and similarly gold is added to silver by value until the nisab is completed, according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: Gold is not added to silver by value; rather it is added by parts (weight). Proof (1): Hadith for establishing that zakat is obligatory on trade goods: from Samurah ibn Jundab, who said: 'To proceed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us to give charity from what we prepared for sale.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Bab al-Urud idha Kanat lil-Tijarah, Hal Fiha min Zakah, no. 1562). Proof (2): Hadith for establishing that zakat is obligatory on trade goods: from Samurah ibn Jundab, who said in a letter: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. From Samurah ibn Jundab to his sons: Peace be upon you. To proceed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to command us regarding a man's or woman's slaves who were hereditary and were workers not intended for sale, that we should not give charity from them; and he used to command us to give charity from slaves who were prepared for sale.' (Sunan Darqutni, Bab Zakat Mal al-Tijarah wa Suqutiha an al-Khayl wa al-Raqiq, no. 2027). Principles: Zakat is obligatory on goods other than gold and silver when they exceed essential needs, a year passes, and they reach the nisab of gold or silver; then one-fortieth is wajib. Principle: When neither gold nor silver alone reaches the nisab, they are added together, and after addition, if the value reaches the nisab of either, zakat is given according to that.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri deals with zakat on trade goods ('urud al-tijara). The ruling: zakat is wajib on merchandise intended for sale. The valuation is done in a way beneficial to the poor (i.e., the higher value to give more, but the Hanafi position is to value at the end of the year at current market price). The passage also states that if the nisab is complete at the beginning and end of the year, a temporary decrease in between does not nullify zakat. Then there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows mixing gold and silver by value to complete the nisab for zakat on trade goods, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that mixing should be by weight (parts), not value. This difference has practical implications: e.g., if someone has 10 mithqals of gold and 100 dirhams of silver, under Abu Hanifa the total value might reach nisab of either, while under Sahibayn one must consider the actual weight of each. The hadith evidence from Samurah ibn Jundab supports the obligation of zakat on goods prepared for sale and exempts slaves not intended for sale. The Urdu commentary summarizes that zakat applies to goods beyond essential needs, and mixing is done by value to reach nisab.

Key Terms
عروض التجارة (urud al-tijarah): Trade goods; merchandise intended for sale, excluding items for personal use or essential needs.
ضم (damm): Adding or combining different types of wealth (e.g., gold and silver) to complete the nisab for zakat.
بالقيمة (bi al-qimah): By value; assessing the monetary worth of an asset (e.g., gold) to combine with another asset (e.g., silver) for nisab.
بالأجزاء (bi al-ajza'): By weight or parts; adding gold and silver by their actual weight, not by value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, how are gold and silver mixed to complete the nisab for zakat on trade goods?
A) By weight only
B) By value
C) They cannot be mixed
D) By number of coins

Key Takeaway
Zakat on trade goods is wajib, and the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that gold and silver are combined by value to complete the nisab.

Zakat on Crops: The Nisab Dispute
Ruling on 'ushr for all produce according to Abu Hanifa and the nisab requirement by the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on 'ushr for crops and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the nisab requirement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: 'Ushr on all produce, no minimum; Sahibayn: only on 5 awsuq or more.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, we encounter a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Is 'ushr (the tithe) due on all agricultural produce regardless of quantity, or only when it reaches a minimum threshold? This question has practical implications for small farmers and gardeners. We will examine the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, along with their hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and identify the scholars
Read the matn carefully. Note that Abu Hanifa's ruling is presented first, followed by the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn).
Abu Hanifa: 'ushr on all produce except firewood, bamboo, grass. Sahibayn: only on produce with lasting benefit, min. 5 awsuq.
2
Locate the proofs for each side
The passage cites two hadith for Abu Hanifa (Bukhari hadith on 'ushr for rain-fed crops; practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz) and two for the Sahibayn (hadith of Mu'adh on no zakat on vegetables; hadith on nisab of 5 awsuq).
Identify the specific hadith references and their implications.
3
Compare the dalil (wajh al-dalalah)
Analyze how each side extracts its ruling from the texts. Abu Hanifa emphasizes the absence of a minimum in the hadith; the Sahibayn rely on the explicit nisab hadith and the exception for vegetables.
Consider the strength (thubut and dalala) of each hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: For a small crop (e.g., 3 awsuq of barley), Abu Hanifa requires 'ushr, the Sahibayn do not.
This affects whether a Muslim must pay zakat on a small garden harvest.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Al-Quduri presents Abu Hanifa's view as the matn, indicating it is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi; no nisab for 'ushr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الرُّرُوعِ وَالحِمَارِ
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الرُّرُوعِ وَالثَّمَارِ
لا قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيلِ مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ وَكَثِيرِهِ الْعُشْرُ سَوَاءٌ مُسْقَى سَيْحًا أَوْ سَقَتْهُ السَّمَاءُ إِلَّا الْخَطَبُ وَالْقَصَبُ وَالْخَشِيشُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَرَةٌ بَاقِيَةٌ إِذَا بَلَغَ خَمْسَةَ أَوْسُقِ ٣ وَالْوِسْقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا بِصَاعِ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ - وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيلِ مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ \ عَنْ سَالِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «فِيمَا سَقَتِ السَّمَاءُ وَالْعُيُونُ، أَوْ كَانَ عَثَرِيَّا، الْعُشْرُ، وَمَا سُقِيَ بِالنَّصْح نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ » » (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الْعُشْرِ فِيمَا يُسْقَى مِنْ مَاءِ السَّمَاءِ، نمبر 1483) وجه (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيل مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ \ كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ: «أَنْ يُؤْخَذَ لِمَا أَنْبَتَتِ الْأَرْضُ مِنْ قَلِيلٍ، أَوْ كَثِيرِ الْعُشْرُ» ""(مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ
الخُضَرِ ، غبر 7196 /مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في كُلِّ شَيْءٍ أَخْرَجَتِ الْأَرْضُ زَكَاةً ، غمبر 10028) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَرَةٌ \ عَنْ مُعَادٍ، أَنَّهُ كَتَبَ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَسْأَلُهُ عَنِ الخَضْرَاوَاتِ وَهِيَ البُقُولُ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ» ،"(سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ الخَضْرَاوَاتِ ، نمبر 638/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ فِيمَا يَزْرَعُهُ الْآدَمِيُّونَ وَيَيْبَسُ وَيُدَّخَرُ وَيُقْتَاتُ دُونَ مَا تُنْبِتُهُ الْأَرْضُ مِنَ الْخُضَرِ ، نمبر 7474)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَمَرَةٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدِ الْخُدْرِيِّ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِيمَا أَقَلُّ مِنْ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَا فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسَةٍ مِنَ الإِبِلِ الدَّوْدِ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَا فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ مِنَ الْوَرِقِ صَدَقَةٌ» (صحيح البخاري، باب : لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُق صَدَقَةٌ، غمبر 1484/مسلم شریف، کتاب الزكاة ، نمبر 976/ سنن ابو داود بَابُ مَا تَجبُ فِيهِ الزَّكَاةُ ، غمبر 1558) وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَالْوِسْقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا بِصَاعِ النَّبِيِّ اعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، قَالَ: «الْوَسْقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا» ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه ، فِي الْوَسْقِ كُمْ هُوَ ، نمبر 10011)
اصول : زمین کی پیداوار ، خواہ کم ہو یا زیادہ پانی سے سیراب کی ہو یا بارش سے اس میں عشر واجب ہے۔ لغت سبح: پانی کا بہنا، سَقَتْ : آب رسائی کرنا، الخَطَبُ : لکڑی ۔ وَالْقَصَبُ : بانسِ وَالخَشِيسُ: گھاس۔
Chapter of Zakat on Crops and Fruits: Abu Hanifa said: On the little of what the earth produces and its much, the 'ushr (tithe) is due, whether irrigated by flowing water or watered by the sky, except firewood, bamboo, and grass. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The 'ushr is not obligatory except on that which has a remaining fruit/benefit when it reaches five awsuq; and the wasq is sixty sa' by the sa' of the Prophet (SAW). Evidence (1) Hadith for establishing that Abu Hanifa said on the little of what the earth produces: from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father from the Prophet (SAW) who said: 'On what is watered by the sky and springs, or is 'athariyy (rain-fed), the 'ushr, and what is watered by irrigation, half of the 'ushr.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 1483). Evidence (2) Saying of a Tabi'i for establishing that Abu Hanifa said on the little of what the earth produces: 'Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote: 'The 'ushr is to be taken from what the earth grows, little or much.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 7196; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10028). Evidence (1) Hadith for establishing that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The 'ushr is not obligatory except on that which has a fruit/benefit: from Mu'adh that he wrote to the Prophet (SAW) asking about vegetables (al-khadrawat, i.e., greens), and he said: 'There is nothing on them.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 638; Sunan al-Kubra al-Bayhaqi, no. 7474). Evidence (2) Hadith for establishing that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The 'ushr is not obligatory except on that which has fruit: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri from the Prophet (SAW) who said: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awsuq, nor on less than five head of camels, nor on less than five uqiyyah of silver.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 1484; Muslim, no. 976; Sunan Abi Dawood, no. 1558). Evidence (1) Hadith for establishing that the wasq is sixty sa' by the sa' of the Prophet: from Abu Sa'id who said: 'The wasq is sixty sa'.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10011). Principle: On the produce of the land, whether little or much, irrigated by water or rain, 'ushr is wajib. Explanation of words: 'sabh': flowing of water; 'saqat': irrigation; 'al-khatab': firewood; 'al-qasab': bamboo; 'al-khashish': grass.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on zakat (ushr) for agricultural produce, with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states Abu Hanifa's position: 'ushr is due on all produce from land, whether little or much, regardless of irrigation method, except for three items: firewood, bamboo, and grass. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that 'ushr is only due on produce that has a lasting fruit or benefit (i.e., grains and fruits that can be stored) and reaches a minimum quantity of 5 awsuq (with 1 wasq = 60 sa'). The hadith proofs are then provided. For Abu Hanifa, the hadith from Bukhari mentions 'ushr on what is watered naturally, but does not mention a minimum quantity, supporting his view. Also the practice of Caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz is cited. For the Sahibayn, the hadith of Mu'adh indicates no zakat on vegetables (which lack lasting fruit), and the well-known hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri sets a minimum nisab of 5 awsuq for zakat on crops. The Urdu summary confirms Abu Hanifa's view as the principle, and explains the exceptions. The passage closes with definitions of key terms.

Key Terms
العشر (al-‘ushr): The tithe or one-tenth of agricultural produce due as zakat.
وسق (wasaq (plural: awsuq)): A measure of volume equal to 60 sa', used as a nisab for agricultural produce.
صاع (ṣā‘): A unit of volume; the Prophet's sa' is used as the standard measure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, 'ushr is due on all produce except which of the following?
A) Wheat and barley
B) Dates and grapes
C) Firewood, bamboo, and grass
D) Vegetables and fruits

Key Takeaway
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether 'ushr requires a nisab; the relied-upon Hanafi position is that all produce (with few exceptions) is subject to 'ushr regardless of quantity.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Zakat of Crops: Nisab and Durability
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs on 'ushr conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on the conditions for 'ushr and evaluate which position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa obligates 'ushr on all produce; the Sahibayn require nisab and durability — and the mufta bihi is Sahibayn.

Zakat on agricultural produce ('ushr) is a wajib act, but its scope is debated within the Hanafi school itself. Imam Abu Hanifa holds a broad view that any yield from the earth — except wild growth — is subject to 'ushr, regardless of quantity or type. His disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), restrict the obligation to staple crops that reach a minimum nisab of five awsuq and are durable enough to be stored. This lesson dissects their proofs and shows how the later school settled on the Sahibayn's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Extract exactly what Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn rule regarding 'ushr from the passage.
Abu Hanifa: 'ushr on all produce except firewood, bamboo, grass. Sahibayn: only on durable crops reaching 5 awsuq.
2
Understand the reasoning
Note that Abu Hanifa relies on general hadith and practice of Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, while Sahibayn rely on specific hadith setting thresholds.
Think about whether general or specific proofs take precedence in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyse the proofs
Compare the hadith of Ibn Umar (general: no minimum) vs. hadith of Mu'adh (no zakat on vegetables) and Abu Sa'id (nisab of 5 awsuq).
Each side has support; weigh the strength of dalala.
4
Explore the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does the disagreement make for a farmer owning a small vegetable plot vs. a wheat field?
Small quantities of non-staple crops may be exempt under Sahibayn but subject under Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi jurists favoured Sahibayn; why? Because specific hadith override general (takhsis) and the nisab hadith is clear.
The operative ruling for fatwa today is that 'ushr requires nisab and durability.

بَابُ زَكَاةِ الرُّرُوعِ وَالثَّمَارِ
قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيلِ مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ وَكَثِيرِهِ الْعُشْرُ سَوَاءٌ مُسْقَى سَيْحًا أَوْ سَقَتْهُ السَّمَاءُ إِلَّا الْخَطَبُ وَالْقَصَبُ وَالْخَشِيشُ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَمَرَةٌ بَاقِيَةٌ إِذَا بَلَغَ خَمْسَةَ أَوْسُقٍ وَالْوِسْقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا بِصَاعِ النَّبِيِّ - صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ -
وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيلِ مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ عَنْ سَالِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «فِيمَا سَقَتِ السَّمَاءُ وَالْعُيُونُ، أَوْ كَانَ عَثَرِيَّا، الْعُشْرُ، وَمَا سُقِيَ بِالنَّضْحِ نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الْعُشْرِ فِيمَا يُسْقَى مِنْ مَاءِ السَّمَاءِ، نمبر 1483)
وجه (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت قَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ فِي قَلِيل مَا أَخْرَجَتْهُ الْأَرْضُ كَتَبَ عُمَرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ: «أَنْ يُؤْخَذَ لِمَا أَنْبَتَتِ الْأَرْضُ مِنْ قَلِيلٍ، أَوْ كَثِيرِ الْعُشْرُ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْخُضَرِ ، غبر 7196 /مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في كُلِّ شَيْءٍ أَخْرَجَتِ الْأَرْضُ زَكَاةً ، غمبر 10028)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَمَرَةٌ عَنْ مُعَاذٍ، أَنَّهُ كَتَبَ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَسْأَلُهُ عَنِ الْخَضْرَاوَاتِ وَهِيَ البُقُولُ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ الْخَضْرَاوَاتِ ، نمبر 638/ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ فِيمَا يَزْرَعُهُ الْآدَمِيُّونَ وَيَيْبَسُ وَيُدَّخَرُ وَيُقْتَاتُ دُونَ مَا تُنْبِتُهُ الْأَرْضُ مِنَ الْخُضَرِ ، نمبر 7474)
وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِلَّا فِيمَا لَهُ ثَمَرَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدِ الْخُدْرِيِّ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِيمَا أَقَلُّ مِنْ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُقٍ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَا فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسَةٍ مِنَ الإِبِلِ الدَّوْدِ صَدَقَةٌ، وَلَا فِي أَقَلَّ مِنْ خَمْسٍ أَوَاقٍ مِنَ الْوَرِقِ صَدَقَةٌ» (صحيح البخاري، باب : لَيْسَ فِيمَا دُونَ خَمْسَةِ أَوْسُق صَدَقَةٌ، غمبر 1484/مسلم شریف، کتاب الزكاة ، نمبر 976/ سنن ابو داود بَابُ مَا تَجبُ فِيهِ الزَّكَاةُ ، غمبر 1558)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَالْوِسْقُ سِتُّونَ صَاعًا بِصَاعِ النَّبِيِّ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، قَالَ: «الْوَسْقُ سِتُونَ صَاعًا» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه ، فِي الْوَسْقِ كُمْ هُوَ ، نمبر 10011)
اصول : زمین کی پیداوار ، خواہ کم ہو یا زیادہ پانی سے سیراب کی ہو یا بارش سے اس میں عشر واجب ہے۔ لغت سبح: پانی کا بہنا، سَقَتْ : آب رسائی کرنا، الخَطَبُ : لکڑی ۔ وَالْقَصَبُ : بانسِ وَالْخَشِيسُ: گھاس۔
Chapter of Zakat of Crops and Fruits. Abu Hanifa said: In the small and large of what the earth produces, the tithe (ʻushr) is due, whether irrigated by flowing water or by rain, except firewood, bamboo, and grass. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The tithe is not obligatory except on what has a lasting fruit, when it reaches five awsuq, and the wasq is sixty saʻ by the saʻ of the Prophet (peace be upon him). Proof (1): The hadith to establish Abu Hanifa's saying in the small of what the earth produces: from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: "In what is irrigated by the sky and springs, or is athari (i.e., naturally watered), the tithe; and what is irrigated by a waterwheel, half the tithe." (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of tithe on what is irrigated by rain water, no. 1483). Proof (2): Statement of the tabi'i to establish Abu Hanifa's saying in the small of what the earth produces: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz wrote: "Let the tithe be taken for what the earth grows, small or large." (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter of vegetables, no. 7196; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, on everything the earth produces as zakat, no. 10028). Proof (1): The hadith to establish Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's statement that the tithe is only obligatory on what has a fruit: from Muʻadh that he wrote to the Prophet (peace be upon him) asking about greens (i.e., vegetables), and he said: "There is nothing (zakat) in them." (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on zakat of greens, no. 638; Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, chapter on sadaqah on what humans plant and dries and is stored and is staple, no. 7474). Proof (2): The hadith to establish Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's statement that the tithe is only obligatory on what has a fruit: from Abu Saʻid al-Khudri from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: "There is no sadaqah in less than five awsuq, nor in less than five (heads) of camels, nor in less than five awaq of silver." (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: there is no sadaqah in less than five awsuq, no. 1484; Muslim, book of zakat, no. 976; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on what requires zakat, no. 1558). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that the wasq is sixty saʻ by the saʻ of the Prophet: from Abu Saʻid, he said: "The wasq is sixty saʻ." (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, on the wasq how much it is, no. 10011). Principles: In the produce of the land, whether small or large, whether irrigated by water or rain, the tithe is wajib. Lexicon: sabih: flowing of water; saqat: irrigation; al-khatab: firewood; al-qasab: bamboo; al-khashish: grass.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on zakat of crops and fruits. Imam Abu Hanifa (RA) states a general rule that the tithe (ʻushr) is due on all produce from the earth, regardless of quantity, and whether the land is irrigated naturally (by rain or flowing water) or artificially. He explicitly excludes three types of produce: firewood, bamboo, and grass, meaning uncultivated wild growth. His position is based on the general import of the Quranic verse (2:267) and the hadith that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) did not set a minimum threshold for crop zakat. The author then presents the view of the two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), who restrict the obligation of ʻushr to crops that have a 'lasting fruit' (thamara baqiya) – i.e., they are staple foods that can be stored – and that reach the nisab of five awsuq (approximately 653 kg or 130 kg? Actually 5 awsuq = 300 saʻ, roughly 653 kg). They also define the wasq as sixty saʻ by the Prophet's saʻ. The text then provides hadith proofs for both positions. For Abu Hanifa, the general hadith from Ibn Umar (RA) about irrigation methods does not mention a minimum, and the practice of Caliph Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz supports it. For the Sahibayn, they cite the hadith about Muʻadh that vegetables (greens) have no zakat, implying that only durable crops are subject, and the hadith of Abu Saʻid that no sadaqah is due on less than five awsuq. This is a classic intra-Hanafi dispute where the Sahibayn introduce the condition of nisab and durability, relying on a specific hadith, while Abu Hanifa relies on general proofs and the principle of istihsan. The usul note summarizes that according to Sahibayn, two conditions are required for zakat on crops: (1) the crop must be lasting and storable, (2) it must reach five awsuq. The lexicon explains terms: sabah (flowing water), saqat (irrigation), khatab (firewood), qasab (bamboo), khashish (grass).

Key Terms
الْعُشْرُ (al-ʻushr): The tithe, a 10% zakat on land produce irrigated naturally (rain, rivers) or artificially (5% if irrigated by effort).
الْوِسْقُ (al-wisq (pl. awsuq)): A unit of measure equal to 60 saʻ by the Prophet's saʻ, used as the nisab for crops.
سَيْحًا (sayhan): Flowing water used for irrigation (e.g., from a canal or stream).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of crop for which 'ushr becomes wajib?
A) Any amount, as per Abu Hanifa
B) Five awsuq, as per the Sahibayn
C) Ten awsuq
D) One wasq

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position for zakat on crops is the view of the Sahibayn: only durable staple crops reaching 5 awsuq are subject to 'ushr.

Specific Rulings on Vegetables, Irrigation, and Special Crops
Zakat rulings for vegetables, irrigation, and special crops with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on zakat for vegetables, irrigation methods, and special crops (cotton, saffron, honey) and explain the intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Vegetables have no zakat; manual irrigation gives half rate; honey and cash crops have divergent rulings.

This lesson dives into specific zakat rules that apply to different types of crops. You'll learn that not all produce is treated equally: vegetables are exempt from zakat, the method of irrigation changes the rate, and special crops like cotton and honey have their own thresholds. We'll also explore the internal differences between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on these issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on vegetables
Note that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule no tithe on vegetables, while Abu Hanifa disagrees. The proof is the statement of Ali (RA).
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
2
Understand the irrigation ruling
When irrigation is by manual means (bucket, pulley, waterwheel), the tithe is half (5%). This is based on the hadith from Bukhari.
Both Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn agree on this.
3
Analyze special crops (cotton, saffron)
For items not measured by wasq, Abu Yusuf says no zakat; Muhammad imposes zakat with specific nisab: 5 loads for cotton, 5 mann for saffron.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view.
4
Examine honey rulings
Three views: general obligation without nisab; Abu Yusuf requires 10 containers; Muhammad requires 5 afraq (each 36 ratls). Proofs from hadiths of Umar and Ibn Umar.
The general view (without nisab) is mufta bihi for tithe land.
5
Apply the condition of land type
All these rulings apply only to produce from tithe land (ʻushr land). No zakat on produce from kharaj land.
This is a fundamental condition.

وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي الْخَضْرَاوَاتِ عِنْدَهُمَا عُشْرًا عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ فِي الْخُضَرِ صَدَقَةٌ الْبَقْلِ، وَالتَّفَاحِ، وَالْقِتَاءِ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ الْخُضَرِ ،نمبر 7188)
وجه:(۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَا سُقِيَ بِغَرْبٍ أَوْ دَالِيَةٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «فِيمَا سَقَتِ السَّمَاءُ وَالْعُيُونُ، أَوْ كَانَ عَثَرِيَّا الْعُشْرُ، وَمَا سُقِيَ بِالنَّضْحِ نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الْعُشْرِ فِيمَا يُسْقَى مِنْ مَاءِ السَّمَاءِ، نمبر 1483)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَفِي الْعَسَلِ الْعُشْرُ قَلَّ أَوْ كَثُرَ إِذَا أُخِذَ مِنْ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِ قَالَ: جَاءَ هِلَالٌ أَحَدُ بَنِي مُنْعَانَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ بِعُشُورِ نَحْلٍ لَهُ، وَكَانَ سَأَلَهُ أَنْ يَحْمِيَ لَهُ وَادِيًا، يُقَالُ لَهُ: سَلَبَةُ، فَحَمَى لَهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم ذَلِكَ الْوَادِي، فَلَمَّا وَلِيَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ كَتَبَ سُفْيَانُ بْنُ وَهْبٍ إِلَى عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ يَسْأَلُهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَكَتَبَ عُمَرُ الله : «إِنْ أَدَّى إِلَيْكَ مَا كَانَ يُؤَدِّي إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنْ عُشُورِ نَحْلِهِ، فَاحْمِ لَهُ سَلَبَةَ، وَإِلَّا ، فَإِنَّمَا هُوَ ذُبَابُ غَيْثٍ يَأْكُلُهُ مَنْ يَشَاءُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ زَكَاةِ الْعَسَلِ، نمبر 1600)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا شَيْءَ فِيهِ عَنْ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ فِي العَسَلِ: «فِي كُلِّ عَشَرَةِ أَزُقٍّ زِقٌّ» (سنن الترمذي بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي زَكَاةِ العَسَلِ، 629)
اصول : صاحبین کے یہاں پھل اور سبزیوں میں زکوۃ کے وجوب کے لیے دو شرطیں ہیں: (1) دیر تک باقی رہنے والی ہوں۔ (2) کم از کم پانچ وسق ہوں۔ اصول : جب کھیتی کو بارش اور ڈول، دونوں سے سیراب کیا گیا ہو تو یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ سال کا اکثر حصہ بارش سے سیراب کیا گیا ہے یا ڈول سے، اگر اکثر بارش سے سیراب کیا تو عشر واجب ہو گا ورنہ نصف عشر واجب ہو گا۔
Chapter of Zakat of Crops and Fruits. And there is no tithe on vegetables according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And what is irrigated by a bucket, a pulley, or a waterwheel, then half the tithe is due on it according to the two views. Abu Yusuf said regarding what cannot be measured by wasq: and Muhammad said: the tithe is obligatory when the output reaches five equivalents of the highest measure by which its type is estimated. So for cotton, five loads are considered; for saffron, five mann; and for honey, the tithe (is due), little or much, when taken from land of tithe. Abu Yusuf said: there is nothing in it until it reaches ten containers (ziqaq); Muhammad said: five afraq, and the farq is thirty-six ratls. And there is no tithe on the produce from kharaj land. Proof (1): Statement of the Companion to establish that there is no tithe on vegetables according to the two: from Ali (RA) who said: "There is no sadaqah in greens: vegetables, apples, and cucumbers." (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, chapter of vegetables, no. 7188). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that what is irrigated by a bucket or pulley: from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: "In what is irrigated by the sky and springs, or is athari, the tithe; and what is irrigated by a waterwheel, half the tithe." (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter of tithe on what is irrigated by rain water, no. 1483). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that for honey, the tithe is due small or large when taken from land of tithe: He said: Hilal, one of the Banu Mun'an, came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with the tithes of his bees, and he asked him to declare a valley called Salaba as a sanctuary, so the Messenger of Allah declared that valley as a sanctuary for him. When Umar ibn al-Khattab became caliph, Sufyan ibn Wahb wrote to Umar asking about that, and Umar wrote: "If he pays you what he used to pay to the Messenger of Allah from the tithes of his bees, then declare Salaba a sanctuary for him; otherwise, it is only a fly of rain that whoever wishes may eat from it." (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter of zakat of honey, no. 1600). Proof (1): The hadith to establish that Abu Yusuf said there is nothing in it: from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah said concerning honey: "For every ten skins (of honey), one skin (as zakat)." (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on zakat of honey, no. 629). Principles: According to the Sahibayn, there are two conditions for the obligation of zakat on fruits and vegetables: (1) they must be lasting and storable, (2) they must be at least five awsuq. Principles: When a crop is irrigated by both rain and bucket, it is considered: whichever method irrigated the majority of the year. If mostly rain, full tithe is wajib; otherwise, half tithe is wajib.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on zakat of crops and fruits, detailing specific rulings. First, it states that according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), vegetables (khudrawat) are not subject to ʻushr. This is because vegetables do not have lasting value (they spoil quickly) and thus do not meet their condition of 'lasting fruit'. A hadith from Imam Ali (RA) supports this. Second, the text discusses irrigation method: if the crop is irrigated by manual effort (using a bucket, pulley, or waterwheel), then half the ʻushr (5%) is due, according to both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. The hadith on irrigation is used as proof. Third, there is a dispute on items that cannot be measured by wasq (like cotton, saffron). Abu Yusuf says they are not zakatable; Muhammad says they are, but with their own nisab equivalents: for cotton, five loads (ahmal); for saffron, five mann. For honey, the text gives three opinions: According to the first opinion (attributed to the general view), honey is subject to ʻushr regardless of quantity when taken from land of tithe (i.e., non-kharaj land). Abu Yusuf requires a nisab of ten containers (aziqqa) and Muhammad requires five afraq (one farq = 36 ratls). A hadith from Umar's letter about Hilal's beehives is cited for the general view, and another hadith for Abu Yusuf's position. Finally, the text states that there is no ʻushr on produce from kharaj land (land conquered by force and subject to land tax). The usul notes summarize the conditions of Sahibayn and the rule for mixed irrigation. This passage demonstrates the intra-Hanafi differences on specific items and the use of athar (sayings of companions) and hadith.

Key Terms
الْخُضْرَاوَاتُ (al-khudrawat): Vegetables and greens that are perishable; according to Sahibayn, not subject to zakat.
غَرْبٍ (gharb): A bucket used for drawing water; irrigation by manual effort triggers half ʻushr.
أَزْقَاقٌ (aziqqa (sing. ziq)): A container or skin for honey; used as a measure for nisab of honey (10 ziq).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Half ʻushr is wajib
C) No ʻushr is wajib
D) ʻUshr is wajib only if they reach 5 awsuq

Key Takeaway
Vegetables are not subject to zakat; irrigation method affects the rate; cotton, saffron, and honey have unique nisab rules within the Hanafi school.

Zakat on Vegetables and Manually-Irrigated Crops
Rulings on vegetables and manual irrigation with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on zakat of vegetables and manually-irrigated crops and cite the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
Vegetables are exempt from zakat; manual irrigation reduces the rate to half-ushr.

This lesson extracts the first set of rulings from the chapter on zakat of crops and fruits. The matn declares that vegetables are not subject to 'ushr according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and that crops irrigated by manual means (bucket, noria, water-wheel) incur only half the standard rate. The evidence quoted includes a saying of Ali (RA) on vegetables and the well-known hadith on irrigation methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
First ruling: no 'ushr on vegetables according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Second ruling: half-'ushr on crops irrigated by manual means (gharb, daliyah, saniyah).
The text uses 'indahuma to indicate the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Abu Hanifa reportedly differed on vegetables.
2
Locate the evidence for each
For vegetables: a saying of Ali (RA) stating 'there is no sadaqah on vegetables'. For irrigation: the hadith 'in what is watered by sky... full 'ushr; what is watered by bucket, half-'ushr'.
Both evidences are cited in the source text.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah of the irrigation hadith
The imperative 'al-'ushr' indicates obligation. The explicit distinction between natural and artificial irrigation defines the rate: full for natural, half for manual.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalalah qati'ah).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on vegetables
Abu Hanifa's position is not given; the matn only transmits the view of the two. Later Hanafi works attribute to Abu Hanifa the opinion that vegetables are subject to 'ushr if they reach nisab.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two (no 'ushr on vegetables).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a farmer growing vegetables pays no zakat, unlike grains/fruits that are naturally irrigated. For manually-watered crops, the rate is 5% instead of 10%.
This is a significant practical difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الزُّرُوعِ وَالثَّمَارِ وَلَيْسَ فِي الْخُضْرَاوَاتِ عِنْدَهُمَا عُشْرًه، وَمَا سُقِيَ بِغَرْب أَوْ دَالِيَةٍ أَوْ سَانِيَةٍ فَفِيهِ نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ لا وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِيمَا لَا يُوَسَّقُ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِذَا بَلَغَ الْخَارِجُ خَمْسَةَ أَمْثَالٍ مِنْ أَعْلَى مَا يُقَدَّرُ بِهِ نَوْعُهُ فَاعْتُبِرَ فِي الْقُطْنِ خَمْسَةُ أَحْمَالٍ وَفِي الزَّعْفَرَانِ خَمْسَةُ أَمْنَانٍ ك وَفِي الْعَسَلِ الْعُشْرُ قَلَّ أَوْ كَثُرَ إِذَا أُخِذَ مِنْ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا شَيْءٍ فِيهِ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ عَشَرَةَ أَزْقَاقٍ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ خَمْسَةُ أَفْرَاقِ وَالْفَرَقُ سِتَّةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ رِضْلًا وَلَيْسَ فِي الخارج مِنْ أَرْضِ الْحَرَاج عُشْرٌ. توجه: (۱) قول الصحابي: عن علي قال: «ليس في الخضر صدقة: البقل، والتفاح، والقتاء» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخضر، رقم 7188). وجه: (۱) الحديث: عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «فيما سقت السماء والعيون أو كان عثريا العشر، وما سقي بالنضح نصف العشر» (صحيح البخاري، باب العشر فيما يسقى من ماء السماء، رقم 1483). وجه: (۱) الحديث: قال: جاء هلال أحد بني منعان إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعشور نحل له... (سنن أبي داود، باب زكاة العسل، رقم 1600). وجه: (۱) الحديث: عن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في العسل: «في كل عشرة أزقة زق» (سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في زكاة العسل، رقم 629).
Chapter on Zakat of Crops and Fruits. There is no tithe on vegetables according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). What is irrigated by bucket, noria, or water-wheel, there is half-tithe in it according to the two views. Abu Yusuf said: Regarding what is not measured in wasq... and Muhammad said: The tithe is obligatory when the produce reaches five likenesses (amsal) from the highest by which its type is measured. So for cotton, five loads are considered; for saffron, five mans; and for honey, the tithe (is obligatory) whether little or much when taken from tithe-land. Abu Yusuf said: Nothing (is due) in it until it reaches ten waterskins. Muhammad said: Five faraq; the faraq is thirty-six ratls. And there is no tithe on produce from kharaj land. Evidence: (1) Saying of the Companion: From Ali, he said: 'There is no charity on vegetables: greens, apples, and cucumbers' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). (2) Hadith: From his father from the Prophet (SAW) said: 'In what is watered by sky and springs or is watered by roots, the tithe; and what is watered by bucket, half-tithe.' (Sahih al-Bukhari). (3) Hadith: 'Hilal, one of Banu Min'an came to the Messenger of Allah with tithes of his bees...' (Sunan Abi Dawud). (4) Hadith: From Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah said regarding honey: 'In every ten waterskins, a waterskin.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from al-Quduri's matn on zakat of agricultural produce, followed by hadith evidence. The author states that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is no 'ushr (tithe) on vegetables. This is a ruling with proof from a Companion saying. Then, for crops irrigated by manual means (bucket, noria, animal-driven wheel), half-tithe is due. This is supported by the well-known hadith differentiating between naturally-watered and manually-watered crops. The text then records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says there is no threshold before the produce is measurable in wasq, while Muhammad says the tithe applies when the produce reaches five amthal (standard measures of volume for that crop). Practical examples: for cotton, five loads; for saffron, five mans. The next ruling: honey always incurs 'ushr when taken from 'ushr land, regardless of quantity, but Abu Yusuf requires a minimum of ten waterskins, and Muhammad requires five faraq (each faraq = 36 ratls). The final ruling: no 'ushr on produce from kharaj (taxed) land. The hadith proofs are then cited: the first (from Ali) supports the exemption of vegetables; the second (the famous 'ushr hadith) supports the half-tithe for manual irrigation; the third and fourth (from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi) support the obligation on honey and specify the nisab according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad respectively.

Key Terms
الْخُضْرَاوَات (al-khudrawat): Vegetables and greens that do not last long in storage.
غَرْب (gharb): A large bucket used for manual irrigation.
دَالِيَة (daliyah): Noria; a water-lifting device.
سَانِيَة (saniyah): Water-wheel driven by an animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, what is the ruling on zakat of vegetables?
A) They are subject to full 'ushr
B) They are subject to half-'ushr
C) There is no 'ushr on them
D) They are subject to 'ushr only if they reach five wasq

Key Takeaway
Vegetables are exempt from zakat in the Hanafi school; manually-irrigated crops are subject to half-ushr.

Zakat on Honey and Non-Standard Crops: Intra-Hanafi Disputes
Rulings on nisab for honey and non-standard crops, with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the different Hanafi views on the nisab for honey and non-standard crops (cotton, saffron) and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Honey and non-standard crops have specific nisab thresholds; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, and the kharaj land exemption is absolute.

This lesson covers the second part of the chapter, where the matn addresses crops that are not measured by wasq (like cotton and saffron) and honey. The text records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf requires a nisab of 10 waterskins for honey, while Muhammad requires 5 faraq. For other crops, each has its own standard measure. The final ruling states that produce from kharaj land is not subject to 'ushr.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context: non-wasq crops
The matn introduces a ruling for crops not measured by volume (wasq), such as cotton and saffron. Instead, they are measured by weight or load.
Muhammad's view: 'ushr is due when the produce reaches five of the highest standard unit for that type.
2
Identify the dispute on honey nisab
Abu Yusuf: nisab is 10 waterskins (azqaq). Muhammad: nisab is 5 faraq (each faraq = 36 ratls). The text implies Abu Hanifa held that 'ushr is due regardless of quantity.
The hadith from Ibn Umar supports the 10-waterskin view; the hadith from Hilal supports general obligation.
3
Locate the evidence for honey
Two hadiths are cited: (1) The story of Hilal bringing tithe of his bees (Sunan Abi Dawud). (2) Ibn Umar report: 'In every ten waterskins, a waterskin' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi).
These are used to support both the obligation and the nisab.
4
Apply the ruling on kharaj land
No 'ushr is due on produce from kharaj (taxed) land. This is a clear rule with no dispute in the text.
Kharaj land is land conquered by force and left to its owners, subject to kharaj tax.
5
Determine the tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars adopt Muhammad's view of 5 faraq (180 ratls) as the mufta bihi for honey. The nisab for other non-standard crops follows their respective standard measures.
The tarjih is not explicit in the matn but is established in later works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ زَكَاةِ الزُّرُوعِ وَالثَّمَارِ وَلَيْسَ فِي الْخُضْرَاوَاتِ عِنْدَهُمَا عُشْرًه، وَمَا سُقِيَ بِغَرْب أَوْ دَالِيَةٍ أَوْ سَانِيَةٍ فَفِيهِ نِصْفُ الْعُشْرِ عَلَى الْقَوْلَيْنِ لا وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ فِيمَا لَا يُوَسَّقُ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجِبُ الْعُشْرُ إِذَا بَلَغَ الْخَارِجُ خَمْسَةَ أَمْثَالٍ مِنْ أَعْلَى مَا يُقَدَّرُ بِهِ نَوْعُهُ فَاعْتُبِرَ فِي الْقُطْنِ خَمْسَةُ أَحْمَالٍ وَفِي الزَّعْفَرَانِ خَمْسَةُ أَمْنَانٍ ك وَفِي الْعَسَلِ الْعُشْرُ قَلَّ أَوْ كَثُرَ إِذَا أُخِذَ مِنْ أَرْضِ الْعُشْرِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا شَيْءٍ فِيهِ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ عَشَرَةَ أَزْقَاقٍ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ خَمْسَةُ أَفْرَاقِ وَالْفَرَقُ سِتَّةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ رِضْلًا وَلَيْسَ فِي الخارج مِنْ أَرْضِ الْحَرَاج عُشْرٌ. توجه: (۱) قول الصحابي: عن علي قال: «ليس في الخضر صدقة: البقل، والتفاح، والقتاء» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الخضر، رقم 7188). وجه: (۱) الحديث: عن أبيه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «فيما سقت السماء والعيون أو كان عثريا العشر، وما سقي بالنضح نصف العشر» (صحيح البخاري، باب العشر فيما يسقى من ماء السماء، رقم 1483). وجه: (۱) الحديث: قال: جاء هلال أحد بني منعان إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعشور نحل له... (سنن أبي داود، باب زكاة العسل، رقم 1600). وجه: (۱) الحديث: عن ابن عمر قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في العسل: «في كل عشرة أزقة زق» (سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في زكاة العسل، رقم 629).
Chapter on Zakat of Crops and Fruits. There is no tithe on vegetables according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). What is irrigated by bucket, noria, or water-wheel, there is half-tithe in it according to the two views. Abu Yusuf said: Regarding what is not measured in wasq... and Muhammad said: The tithe is obligatory when the produce reaches five likenesses (amsal) from the highest by which its type is measured. So for cotton, five loads are considered; for saffron, five mans; and for honey, the tithe (is obligatory) whether little or much when taken from tithe-land. Abu Yusuf said: Nothing (is due) in it until it reaches ten waterskins. Muhammad said: Five faraq; the faraq is thirty-six ratls. And there is no tithe on produce from kharaj land. Evidence: (1) Saying of the Companion: From Ali, he said: 'There is no charity on vegetables: greens, apples, and cucumbers' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). (2) Hadith: From his father from the Prophet (SAW) said: 'In what is watered by sky and springs or is watered by roots, the tithe; and what is watered by bucket, half-tithe.' (Sahih al-Bukhari). (3) Hadith: 'Hilal, one of Banu Min'an came to the Messenger of Allah with tithes of his bees...' (Sunan Abi Dawud). (4) Hadith: From Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah said regarding honey: 'In every ten waterskins, a waterskin.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from al-Quduri's matn on zakat of agricultural produce, followed by hadith evidence. The author states that according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) there is no 'ushr (tithe) on vegetables. This is a ruling with proof from a Companion saying. Then, for crops irrigated by manual means (bucket, noria, animal-driven wheel), half-tithe is due. This is supported by the well-known hadith differentiating between naturally-watered and manually-watered crops. The text then records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says there is no threshold before the produce is measurable in wasq, while Muhammad says the tithe applies when the produce reaches five amthal (standard measures of volume for that crop). Practical examples: for cotton, five loads; for saffron, five mans. The next ruling: honey always incurs 'ushr when taken from 'ushr land, regardless of quantity, but Abu Yusuf requires a minimum of ten waterskins, and Muhammad requires five faraq (each faraq = 36 ratls). The final ruling: no 'ushr on produce from kharaj (taxed) land. The hadith proofs are then cited: the first (from Ali) supports the exemption of vegetables; the second (the famous 'ushr hadith) supports the half-tithe for manual irrigation; the third and fourth (from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi) support the obligation on honey and specify the nisab according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad respectively.

Key Terms
أَزْقَاق (azqaq): Waterskins; a unit of volume for honey or liquids.
فَرَق (faraq): A large measure equal to 36 ratls (approx. 16.4 kg).
خَرَاج (kharaj): Tax on land conquered by force; such land is not subject to 'ushr.
أَمْثَال (amsal): Plural of mithl; standard measures of the same type.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (preferred opinion) in the Hanafi school, what is the nisab for zakat on honey?
A) 10 waterskins (azqaq)
B) 5 faraq (180 ratls)
C) 5 wasq
D) No nisab; any quantity triggers zakat

Key Takeaway
For honey, the mufta bihi nisab is 5 faraq (180 ratls); produce from kharaj land is exempt from 'ushr.

The Eight Categories of Zakat Recipients (Masarif al-Zakah)
Lists eight zakat categories and defines faqir/miskin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight categories of zakat recipients, define faqir and miskin according to the Hanafi school, and explain why the category of muallafatu qulubuhum has fallen away.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given only to eight specific groups; the muallafah category is no longer valid.

The Quran specifies eight categories for zakat expenditure, making them the exclusive recipients. This lesson examines each category, clarifies the Hanafi definitions of faqir and miskin, and explains why one category—muallafatu qulubuhum—is no longer applicable after the time of the Prophet (SAW). Understanding these categories is essential for valid zakat distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic basis
Read the opening of Surah At-Tawbah (9:60) which lists the eight categories. Note that the verse uses 'innama' (only), indicating exclusivity.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah.
2
List the eight categories
From the verse, enumerate: fuqara (poor), masakin (needy), amilin (collectors), muallafatu qulubuhum (those whose hearts are reconciled), riqab (slaves), gharimin (debtors), fi sabil Allah (in the cause of Allah), ibn al-sabil (wayfarer).
The passage confirms these eight.
3
Understand the Hanafi definitions of faqir and miskin
According to the passage, faqir is one who possesses the least thing (adna shay'), while miskin is one who has nothing. This is the Hanafi position, opposite to the Shafi'i view.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists, but the text's definition is relied upon.
4
Recognize that muallafah has lapsed
The text states 'qad saqata minha al-muallafah'—the category has fallen away. The evidence is a report that Abu Bakr (RA) discontinued it, implying consensus.
This is a point of dispute with the Shafi'i school.
5
Review the supporting hadith evidence
Two hadith are cited: one shows the Prophet distinguished between charity and gifts, the other confirms that charity is not permissible for the Prophet's household and their freed clients.
These hadith reinforce the rules about who may receive zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ مَصَارِفِ الزَّكَاةِ بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الصَّدَقَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَمَنْ لَا يَجُوزُ قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى {إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ} [التوبة: 60] الْآيَةُ فَهَذِهِ ثَمَانِيَةُ أَصْنَافِ لَ قَدْ سَقَطَ مِنْهَا الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ فَالْفَقِيرُ مَنْ لَهُ أَدْنَ شَيْءٍ لِّ وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ إِنْ عَمِلَ بِقَدْرِ عَمَلِهِ. توجه: (۱) الآية لثبوت... (۱) الحديث لثبوت قَدْ سَقَطَ مِنْهَا الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا كَانَتِ الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ قُلُوبُهُمْ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَلَمَّا وَلِيَ أَبُو بَكْرِ انْقَطَعَتْ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة). (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لا شَيْءَ لَهُ وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ عَنْ بَهْرِ بْنِ حَكِيمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أُتِيَ بِشَيْءٍ سَأَلَ: «أَصَدَقَةٌ هِيَ، أَمْ هَدِيَّةٌ؟»، فَإِنْ قَالُوا : صَدَقَةٌ لَم يَأْكُلْ، وَإنْ قَالُوا هَدِيَّةٌ أَكَلَ (سنن ترمذي، 656/أبو داود، 1652). (۲) الحديث: عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعَثَ رَجُلًا مِنْ بَنِي مَخْزُومٍ عَلَى الصَّدَقَةِ، فَقَالَ لِأَبِي رَافِعِ: اصْحَبْنِي كَيْمَا تُصِيبَ مِنْهَا، فَقَالَ: لا، حَتَّى آتِي رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَسْأَلَهُ، فَانْطَلَقَ إِلَى النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلَهُ فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ لَا تَحِلُّ لَنَا، وَإِنَّ مَوَالِيَ القَوْمِ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ» (سنن ترمذي، 657/أبو داود، 1650).
Chapter on Expenditures of Zakat. Chapter on to whom it is permissible to give charity and to whom it is not. Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' (At-Tawbah 60). The verse (continues). So these are eight categories. The category of those whose hearts are to be reconciled has fallen away. The poor (faqir) is one who possesses the least thing. The needy (miskin) is one who has nothing. The worker (amil) is paid by the Imam if he works, according to his work. Evidence: (1) The verse for proof... (1) Hadith for proof that the Muallafah has fallen: From Amir, he said: 'Indeed the Muallafatu Qulubuhum were only in the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and when Abu Bakr took over, it ceased.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba). (1) Hadith for proof that the miskin is one who has nothing and the worker is paid by the Imam: From Bahz bin Hakim, from his father, from his grandfather, he said: When something was brought to the Messenger of Allah, he would ask: 'Is it charity or a gift?' If they said charity, he did not eat; if they said gift, he ate. (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, 656/Abu Dawud, 1652). (2) Hadith: From Abu Rafi', that the Prophet sent a man from Banu Makhzum in charge of charity, and he said to Abu Rafi': 'Accompany me so you may get some of it.' He said: 'No, until I ask the Messenger of Allah.' So he went to the Prophet and asked, and he said: 'Charity is not permissible for us, and the freed clients of a people are part of them.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, 657/Abu Dawud, 1650).
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on the categories (masarif) of zakat. The matn quotes Quran 9:60 which lists eight categories: the poor, the needy, the workers (collectors), those whose hearts are to be reconciled (muallafatu qulubuhum), slaves, debtors, in the cause of Allah, and the wayfarer. The text then states that the category of muallafah has fallen away (sagata) after the time of the Prophet (SAW); this is supported by a report from Amir that Abu Bakr discontinued it. Then the matn gives definitions: faqir (poor) is one who has the least something (less than nisab? According to Hanafi, faqir has some property but less than nisab; miskin has nothing. But here the matn defines faqir as having the least thing and miskin as having nothing. This matches the Hanafi view. The third category is the 'amil (zakat collector), who receives payment from the Imam in proportion to his work. The hadith evidence cited includes: (1) the story of Bahz bin Hakim showing the Prophet's distinction between charity and gifts; (2) the hadith of Abu Rafi' that charity is not permissible for the Prophet and his household, and that the freed slaves of a tribe are considered part of them in this prohibition. These hadith support the rules about who may receive zakat and who may not (e.g., Banu Hashim and their freed slaves).

Key Terms
الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ (al-muallafah): Those whose hearts are to be reconciled, i.e., new Muslims or potential allies given zakat to strengthen faith or avoid harm.
الْفَقِيرُ (al-faqir): One who possesses the least something (some property but less than nisab, or he has some income but insufficient).
الْعَامِلُ (al-amil): The zakat collector appointed by the Imam; he is paid from zakat funds for his work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of the category 'muallafatu qulubuhum' (those whose hearts are to be reconciled) in current zakat distribution?
A) It is still applicable and must be given priority
B) It has fallen away after the Prophet's time
C) It applies only to non-Muslims
D) It is only for the family of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given exclusively to the eight Quranic categories; the category of muallafah is no longer operative in the Hanafi school.

Zakat — Almsgiving
