6 min
The Eight Categories of Zakat Recipients
Lists and defines the eight eligible recipients of zakat with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight categories of zakat recipients as per the Hanafi school, distinguish between faqir and miskin according to Hanafi definitions, and identify which categories are currently operative and which are abrogated.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given to the eight Quranic categories, but the mu'allaf category is abrogated; the owner may give to one category or distribute.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn lays out the recipients of zakat based on the Quranic verse. It not only lists the eight categories but also clarifies key definitions, such as the difference between faqir (one who has a little) and miskin (one who has nothing). Understanding these categories is essential for proper zakat distribution. The text also addresses practical issues such as whether zakat can be given to a dhimmi or used for building mosques.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic basis
Read Surah At-Tawbah 9:60, which lists the eight categories. Note the particle 'innama' indicating restriction.
The verse is the core dalil.
2
Understand the Hanafi definitions of faqir and miskin
The faqir is one who has a little something; the miskin is one who has nothing. This reverses the common understanding.
This is a distinct Hanafi position.
3
Recognize the abrogation of mu'allaf
The text states that the mu'allaf category has fallen. It was only for the time of the Prophet, as Islam grew strong.
Supported by the hadith of 'Amir.
4
Note the permissible distribution flexibility
The owner may give zakat to all categories or confine it to one. The Quranic enumeration is not a mandatory equal distribution.
Based on the saying of Hudhayfah.
5
Learn the impermissible uses
Zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi, used to build a mosque, shroud a deceased, or purchase a slave to free.
Supported by multiple hadith and the saying of al-Thawri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ مَصَارِفِ الزَّكَاةِ
بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الصَّدَقَةِ إِلَيْهِ وَمَنْ لَا يَجُوزُ قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى {إِنَّمَا الصَّدَقَاتُ لِلْفُقَرَاءِ وَالْمَسَاكِينِ} [التوبة: 60] الْآيَةُ فَهَذِهِ ثَمَانِيَةُ أَصْنَافٍ قَدْ سَقَطَ مِنْهَا الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ فَالْفَقِيرُ مَنْ لَهُ أَدْنَى شَيْءٍ وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ إِنْ عَمِلَ بِقَدْرِ عَمَلِهِ
وَفِي الرّقَابِ يُعَانُ الْمُكَاتَبُونَ فِي فَكِ رِقَاهِمْ وَالْغَارِمُ مَنْ لَزِمَهُ دَيْنٌ لَا وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ فِي وَطَنِهِ وَهُوَ فِي مَكَان آخَرَ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ فِيهِ وَلِلْمَالِكِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَقْتَصِرَ عَلَى صِنْفٍ وَاحِدٍ
وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمِّي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ وَلَا يُكَفَّنُ بِمَا مَيِّتٌ وَلَا يَشْتَرِي بِمَا رَقَبَةً تَعْتِقُ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت مَنْ لَهُ أَدْنَى شَيْءٍ عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا كَانَتِ الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ قُلُوبُهُمْ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَلَمَّا وَلِيَ أَبُو بَكْرِ انْقَطَعَتْ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه في الْمُؤَلَّفَةِ قُلُوبُهُمْ يُوجَدُونَ الْيَوْمَ أَوْ ذَهَبُوا، غبر (10759)
وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ حَدَّثَنَا بَهْرُ بْنُ حَكِيمٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم إِذَا أُتِيَ بِشَيْءٍ سَأَلَ: «أَصَدَقَةٌ هِيَ، أَمْ هَدِيَّةٌ؟»، فَإِنْ قَالُوا: صَدَقَةٌ لَم يَأْكُلْ، وَإنْ قَالُوا هَدِيَّةٌ أَكَلَ (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الصَّدَقَةِ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَهْلِ بَيْتِهِ وَمَوَالِيهِ، 656/سنن ابوداود بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ عَلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ،1652)
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَالْمِسْكِينُ مَنْ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ وَالْعَامِلُ يَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ الْإِمَامُ عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعَثَ رَجُلًا مِنْ بَنِي مَخْزُومٍ عَلَى الصَّدَقَةِ، فَقَالَ لِأَبِي رَافِعِ: اصْحَبْنِي كَيْمَا تُصِيبَ مِنْهَا، فَقَالَ: لَا، حَتَّى آتِي رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَسْأَلَهُ، فَانْطَلَقَ إِلَى النَّبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فَسَأَلَهُ فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ لَا تَحِلُّ لَنَا، وَإِنَّ مَوَالِيَ القَوْمِ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ» (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الصَّدَقَةِ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَهْلِ بَيْتِهِ وَمَوَالِيهِ، نمبر 657/سنن ابوداود بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ عَلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ، نمبر 1650)
وجه: (4) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلِلْمَالِكِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ عَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أَعْطَاهَا فِي صِنْفِ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَصْنَافِ الثَّمَانِيَةِ الَّتِي سَمَّى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَجْزَأَهُ» (مصنف ابن شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ إِذَا وَضَعَ الصَّدَقَةَ فِي صِنْفِ وَاحِدٍ، نمبر 10445)
وجه: (5) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمِّي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِهَا مَسْجِدٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ عنهما قَالَ: «قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِمُعَاذِ بْنِ جَبَلٍ، أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ خَمْسَ صَلَوَاتٍ فِي كُلّ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ، فَإِنْ هُمْ أَطَاعُوا لَكَ بِذَلِكَ، فَأَخْبِرْهُمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُؤْخَذُ مِنْ أَغْنِيَائِهِمْ فَتُرَدُّ عَلَى فُقَرَائِهِمْ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ أَخْذِ الصَّدَقَةِ مِنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ وَتُرَدَّ فِي الْفُقَرَاءِ حَيْثُ كَانُوا، 1496/مسلم شریف، باب الدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الشَّهَادَتَيْنِ وَشَرَائِعِ الإِسْلَامِ، نمبر 19)
وجه: (6) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إلَى ذِمّي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «الرَّجُلُ لَا يُعْطِي زَكَاةَ مَالِهُ مَنْ يُحْبَسُ عَلَى النَّفَقَةِ مِنْ ذَوِي أَرْحَامِهِ، وَلَا يُعْطِيهَا فِي كَفَنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا دَيْنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا بِنَاءِ مَسْجِدٍ، وَلَا شِرَاءِ مُصْحَفِ، وَلَا يَحُجُّ بِهَا، وَلَا تُعْطِيهَا مُكَاتِبَكَ، وَلَا تَبْتَاعُ بِمَا نَسَمَةً تُحَرِّرُهَا، وَلَا تُعْطِيهَا فِي الْيَهُودِ، وَلَا النَّصَارَى، وَلَا تَسْتَأْجِرُ عَلَيْهَا مِنْهَا مَنْ يَحْمِلُهَا لِيَحْمِلَهَا مِنْ مَكَانٍ إِلَى مَكَانٍ» (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ لِمَنِ الزَّكَاةُ، نمبر 1770)
وجه: (7) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمَيَ وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ، قَالَتْ: قَدِمَتْ عَلَيَّ أُمِّي رَاغِبَةً فِي عَهْدِ قُرَيْشٍ وَهِيَ رَاغِمَةٌ مُشْرِكَةً، فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّ أُمِّي قَدِمَتْ عَلَيَّ، وَهِيَ رَاغِمَةٌ مُشْرِكَةٌ، أَفَأَصِلُهَا؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ، فَصِلِي أُمَّكِ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ، نمبر 1668)
اصول: تالیف قلب کے لئے لوگوں کو زکوۃ دینا حضور صلی صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانے میں جائز تھا، پھر بعد میں جب اللہ تعالیٰ نے اسلام کو قوت عطا فرمائی تو یہ حکم منقطع کر دیا گیا۔
اصول: حاکم وقت، زکوۃ وصول کرنے والوں کو اس کی محنت کے بقدر، زکوہ کی رقم میں سے دے سکتا ہے۔
Chapter on the recipients of zakat. Chapter on to whom it is permissible to give charity and to whom it is not. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' [At-Tawbah 9:60] the verse. So these are eight categories, from which the mu'allafatu qulubuhum have fallen. So the faqir is one who has a little something, and the miskin is one who has nothing. And the worker: the Imam pays him if he works according to the extent of his work. And in the slaves: the mukatabs are assisted in freeing their necks. And the gharim is one to whom a debt is due (he is in debt) without (sufficient) means. And in the path of Allah: the stranded warrior. And the ibn al-sabil: one who has wealth in his homeland but is in another place where he has nothing. And the owner (of wealth) may pay to each one of them, and he may limit himself to one category. And it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi, nor may a mosque be built with it, nor may a deceased be shrouded with it, nor may a slave be purchased with it (such that the slave) becomes free. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish that [the faqir] has a little something: from 'Amir who said: 'Indeed the mu'allafatu qulubuhum (those whose hearts are to be reconciled) existed in the time of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, then when Abu Bakr took charge, it ceased.' (Mussannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on mu'allafatu qulubuhum: 'Are they found today or have they gone?', no. 10759). Evidence: (2) The hadith to establish that the miskin is he who has nothing, and the worker: the Imam pays him: From Bahz ibn Hakim, from his father, from his grandfather who said: 'Whenever something was brought to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, he asked: 'Is it charity or a gift?' If they said charity, he would not eat; if they said gift, he would eat.' (Sunan Tirmidhi, chapter on dislike of charity for the Prophet and his family and their clients, 656; Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on charity to Banu Hashim, 1652). Evidence: (3) The hadith to establish that the miskin is he who has nothing, and the worker: the Imam pays him: From Abu Rafi', that the Prophet, peace be upon him, sent a man from Banu Makhzum to collect charity, and he said to Abu Rafi': 'Accompany me so you may get some of it.' He said: 'No, until I go to the Messenger of Allah and ask him.' So he went to the Prophet and asked him, and he said: 'Charity is not lawful for us, and the clients of a tribe are from among them.' (Sunan Tirmidhi, no. 657; Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1650). Evidence: (4) The saying of a companion to establish that the owner may pay to each one of them: From Hudhayfah who said: 'If he gives it to one category from the eight categories that Allah Most High mentioned, it suffices him.' (Mussannaf Ibn Shaybah, no. 10445). Evidence: (5) The hadith to establish that it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi nor to build a mosque with it: From Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, who said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'Allah has prescribed upon them five prayers every day and night. If they obey you in that, then inform them that Allah has prescribed upon them a charity taken from their rich and given back to their poor.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on taking charity from the rich and giving it to the poor wherever they are, 1496; Sahih Muslim, chapter on inviting to the two testimonies and the laws of Islam, no. 19). Evidence: (6) The saying of a tabi'i to establish that it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi nor to build a mosque with it: From al-Thawri who said: 'A man should not give the zakat of his wealth to one who is imprisoned for maintenance from his relatives, nor give it for the shroud of a deceased, nor for the debt of a deceased, nor for building a mosque, nor for buying a mushaf, nor perform hajj with it, nor give it to his mukatab, nor purchase with it a soul to free it, nor give it to Jews or Christians, nor hire with it from it someone to carry it from one place to another.' (Mussannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter on to whom zakat is given, no. 1770). Evidence: (7) The hadith to establish that it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi nor to build a mosque with it: From Asma', she said: 'My mother came to me during the covenant of Quraysh, she was averse and a polytheist. I said: O Messenger of Allah, my mother came to me, and she is averse and a polytheist, should I maintain ties with her? He said: 'Yes, maintain ties with your mother.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on charity to the People of the Book, no. 1668). Principle: Giving zakat to people for reconciliation of hearts was permissible in the time of the Prophet, peace be upon him, then later when Allah gave strength to Islam, this ruling was discontinued. Principle: The ruler may give to the collectors from the zakat funds according to the effort of their work.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn is a ruling with proof on the recipients of zakat (مصاريف الزكاة). It begins by citing the Quranic verse from Surah At-Tawbah (9:60) which specifies eight categories: the poor (fuqara'), the needy (masakin), the workers (al-'amilun 'alayha), those whose hearts are to be reconciled (mu'allafatu qulubuhum), the slaves (riqab), the debtors (gharimun), in the path of Allah (fi sabil Allah), and the wayfarer (ibn al-sabil). The text then states that the category of mu'allafatu qulubuhum has been dropped (saqata minha al-mu'allafah). The faqir is defined as one who possesses at least a little something (adna shay'), while the miskin is one who possesses nothing. This reverses the common understanding (often miskin is considered worse off). The worker (al-'amil) is compensated by the Imam from the zakat funds according to his work. Regarding slaves (fi al-riqab), the text specifies that mukatabun (slaves under contract of manumission) are assisted in freeing themselves. The gharim is one who is burdened by debt without sufficient means. Fi sabil Allah refers to the stranded warrior (munqati' al-ghuzat). Ibn al-sabil is one who has wealth in his hometown but is traveling and has nothing with him. The text then gives the owner of wealth the option to distribute zakat to all eight categories or to confine it to a single category. This flexibility is based on the understanding that the Quranic enumeration is not a mandatory equal distribution. Finally, the passage lists impermissible uses: zakat cannot be given to a dhimmi (non-Muslim protected citizen), nor used to build a mosque, shroud a deceased, or purchase a slave to free (except according to some views). These prohibitions are supported by hadith and the practice of the Companions. The Urdu notes explain two principles: first, the discontinuation of the mu'allaf category after Islam became strong; second, the ruler's authority to pay zakat collectors from the fund.

Key Terms
الْفَقِيرُ (al-faqīr): One who possesses a little something (adnā shay'), i.e., has less than nisab or barely enough to meet basic needs.
الْمِسْكِينُ (al-miskīn): One who has nothing (lā shay'a lahu), i.e., absolutely penniless.
الْمُؤَلَّفَةُ قُلُوبُهُمْ (al-mu'allafatu qulūbuhum): Non-Muslims or new Muslims whose hearts are to be won over to Islam or to secure their support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the difference between a faqir (فقير) and a miskin (مسكين)?
A) Faqir has nothing, miskin has a little.
B) Faqir has a little, miskin has nothing.
C) Both are the same but used interchangeably.
D) Faqir is below the poverty line, miskin is above.

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given to the eight Quranic categories, but the mu'allaf category is abrogated; the faqir has a little, the miskin has nothing, and the owner may give to one category only.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
10 min
Eight Categories of Zakat Recipients and Prohibited Disbursements
Ruling with proof listing eight categories and prohibitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight categories of zakat recipients according to the Hanafi school, identify prohibited uses of zakat funds, and apply the ruling to determine valid disbursement.

Core Idea
Zakat must be given to specific recipients; it can be confined to one category, but cannot be used for non-recipient purposes like building mosques or giving to dhimmī.

This lesson unpacks the foundational passage from al-Quduri on the disbursement (masārif) of zakat. We will examine the eight recipient categories with their Hanafi-specific definitions, the ruling that distribution among categories is recommended but not obligatory, and the explicit prohibitions against spending zakat on non-recipients such as dhimmīs, building mosques, shrouding the dead, or buying slaves to free. Understanding these rules ensures that zakat is discharged correctly, fulfilling its purpose as a right of specific beneficiaries.

Guided Path
1
List the eight recipient categories
Identify each of the eight categories mentioned in the verse (9:60) and as defined by the Hanafi school: fuqarā', masākīn, 'āmilīn, mu'allafat al-qulūb, riqāb (mukātabūn), ghārimūn, fī sabīl Allāh (stranded mujāhidūn), and ibn al-sabīl.
The Hanafi school narrows 'riqāb' to mukātab slaves only.
2
Analyze the ruling on distribution scope
Note the phrase 'wa lahu an yaqtasira 'alā sinf wāhid' — the owner may confine zakat to one category. This is the Hanafi position: distribution across all categories is mustahabb, not wājib.
Other schools like Shāfi'ī require distribution to at least three categories.
3
Identify prohibited disbursements
The text explicitly prohibits paying to a dhimmī, building a mosque, shrouding a dead person, or buying a slave to free. Understand why: these are not among the eight categories; zakat is a specific right, not general charity.
Giving to a dhimmī from voluntary charity (sadaqa) is allowed, but not from mandatory zakat.
4
Examine the evidence (dalīl)
The passage cites several proofs: the hadīth of Mu'ādh (zakat from rich to poor of Muslims), the practice of al-Thawrī, and the hadīth of Asmā' distinguishing zakat from voluntary charity. Understand how each supports the ruling.
The hadīth of Asmā' about her mother shows voluntary charity to non-Muslims is permissible, but zakat is restricted to Muslims.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given a specific scenario (e.g., a donor wants to use zakat to build a mosque), determine whether it is valid or invalid by checking if the use matches one of the eight categories.
Building a mosque is not a category; thus the disbursement is invalid.

Source Text

بَابُ مَصَارِفِ الزَّكَاةِ وفي الرّقَابِ يُعَانُ الْمُكَاتَبُونَ فِي فَكِ رِقَاهِمْ ٥. وَالْغَارِمُ مَنْ لَزِمَهُ دَيْنٌ لا وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مُنْقَطِعُ الْغُزَاةِ ك وَابْنِ السَّبِيلِ مَنْ كَانَ لَهُ مَالٌ فِي وَطَنِهِ وَهُوَ فِي مَكَان آخَرَ لَا شَيْءَ لَهُ فِيهِ وَلِلْمَالِكِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ وَلَهُ أَنْ يَقْتَصِرَ عَلَى صِنْفٍ وَاحِدٍ
ووَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمِّي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ وَلَا يُكَفَّنُ بِمَا مَيِّتٌ وَلَا يَشْتَرِي بِمَا رَقَبَةً تَعْتِقُ مَوْلَى ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: «بَعَثَنِي أَبِي إِلَى النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي إِبِلٍ، أَعْطَاهَا إِيَّاهُ مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ» ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ عَلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ، نمبر 1653)
د. وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلِلْمَالِكِ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى كُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ \ عَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ، قَالَ: «إِذَا أَعْطَاهَا فِي صِنْفِ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَصْنَافِ الثَّمَانِيَةِ الَّتِي سَمَّى اللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَجْزَأَهُ»،» (مصنف ابن شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ إِذَا وَضَعَ الصَّدَقَةَ فِي صِنْفٍ وَاحِدٍ، نمبر 10445)
و وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمِي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِهَا مَسْجِدٌ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ عنهما قَالَ: «قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِمُعَاذِ بْنِ جَبَلٍ، أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ خَمْسَ
صَلَوَاتٍ فِي كُلّ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ، فَإِنْ هُمْ أَطَاعُوا لَكَ بِذَلِكَ، فَأَخْبِرْهُمْ أَنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُؤْخَذُ مِنْ أَغْنِيَائِهِمْ فَتُرَدُّ عَلَى فُقَرَائِهِمْ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ أَخْذِ الصَّدَقَةِ مِنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ وَتُرَدَّ فِي
الْفُقَرَاءِ حَيْثُ كَانُوا، 1496/مسلم شریف ، باب الدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الشَّهَادَتَيْنِ وَشَرَائِعِ الإِسْلَامِ، نمبر 19) وجه : (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إلَى ذِمّي وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ \ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «الرَّجُلُ لَا يُعْطِي زَكَاةَ مَالِهُ مَنْ يُحْبَسُ عَلَى النَّفَقَةِ مِنْ ذَوِي أَرْحَامِهِ، وَلَا يُعْطِيهَا فِي كَفَنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا دَيْنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا بِنَاءِ مَسْجِدٍ، وَلَا شِرَاءِ مُصْحَفِ ، وَلَا يَحُجُّ بِهَا، وَلَا تُعْطِيهَا مُكَاتِبَكَ، وَلَا تَبْتَاعُ بِمَا نَسَمَةً تُحَرِّرُهَا، وَلَا تُعْطِيهَا فِي الْيَهُودِ، وَلَا النَّصَارَى، وَلَا تَسْتَأْجِرُ عَلَيْهَا مِنْهَا مَنْ يَحْمِلُهَا لِيَحْمِلَهَا مِنْ مَكَانٍ إِلَى مَكَانٍ»، مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ لِمَنِ الزَّكَاةُ، نمبر 1770)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يَدْفَعَ إِلَى ذِمَيَ وَلَا يُبْنَى بِمَا مَسْجِدٌ \ عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ، قَالَتْ: قَدِمَتْ عَلَيَّ أُمِّي رَاغِبَةً فِي عَهْدِ قُرَيْشٍ وَهِيَ رَاغِمَةٌ مُشْرِكَةً، فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّ أُمِّي قَدِمَتْ عَلَيَّ، وَهِيَ رَاغِمَةٌ مُشْرِكَةٌ، أَفَأَصِلُهَا؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ، فَصِلِي أُمَّكِ»(،سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الصَّدَقَةِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الذِّمَّةِ، نمبر 1668) اصول : حاکم وقت ، زکوۃ وصول کرنے والوں کو اس کی محنت کے بقدر، زکوہ کی رقم میں سے دے سکتا ہے۔
Chapter on the disbursement of zakat: And concerning slaves (riqab): the mukatibin are helped in freeing their bondage. And al-gharim: one on whom a debt is due without [means]. And fi sabil Allah: the stranded mujahid. And ibn al-sabil: one who has wealth in his homeland but is in another place with nothing. And the owner may pay to each of them, and he may confine himself to one category. And it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi, nor to build a mosque with it, nor to shroud a dead person with it, nor to buy a slave to free with it. [Hadith of Ibn Abbas from his father]. Evidence: (1) the saying of a Companion to prove the owner may pay to each of them: from Hudhayfah: 'If he gives it in one of the eight categories Allah mentioned, it suffices.' And evidence: (1) the hadith to prove it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi nor build a mosque with it: from Ibn Abbas: the hadith of Mu'adh; and evidence: (2) the saying of a Tabi'i: from al-Thawri: 'A man does not give his zakat to those of his relatives who are held for maintenance...' And evidence: (3) the hadith to prove it is not permissible to pay to a dhimmi nor build a mosque: from Asma' regarding her mother. Principle: The ruler may give from zakat funds to the collectors according to their effort.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn begins the chapter on the disbursement of zakat. It first mentions the eight recipient categories with specific interpretations: under 'riqab' (slaves) it means helping mukatibin (slaves with contracts of manumission); 'gharim' is a debtor who cannot pay; 'fi sabil Allah' refers to stranded mujahidin; 'ibn al-sabil' is a traveler who has wealth at home but none with him. The text then states the owner may distribute zakat among all categories or restrict to one — this is the Hanafi position that distribution among categories is recommended but not obligatory. Then it lists prohibited uses: giving to a dhimmi (non-Muslim citizen of the Islamic state), building a mosque, shrouding a dead person, or buying a slave to free. These are invalid because zakat is a right of specific recipients, not a general charity. The commentary provides as evidence: the hadith of Mu'adh where zakat is taken from the rich and given to the poor (indicating Muslim poor), the practice of the Salaf (al-Thawri's statement), and the hadith of Asma' about giving to a non-Muslim mother (which is about voluntary charity, not zakat). Finally, a principle: the ruler may compensate zakat collectors from zakat funds.

Key Terms
مَصَارِف (masārif): The categories of recipients entitled to zakat.
ذِمِّي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim living under the protection of the Islamic state.
رَقَبَة (raqabah): A slave; in zakat context, specifically a mukatab slave.
غَارِم (ghārim): A debtor who cannot pay his debts.
سَبِيل اللَّهِ (sabīl Allāh): Literally 'the path of Allah'; in Hanafi zakat, specifically the stranded mujāhid (fighter) who has no means.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving zakat to a dhimmī (non-Muslim citizen)?
A) Permissible if he is a poor relative
B) Not permissible under any circumstances
C) Permissible only if he does not have any Muslim relatives
D) Permissible if he is a poor neighbor

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be disbursed strictly to the eight categories defined in the Quran and interpreted by the Hanafi school; any use outside these is invalid and does not fulfill the obligation.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Giving Zakat to the Wealthy and Relatives
Prohibition of giving zakat to specific categories with intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of people to whom zakat cannot be given and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on a wife giving zakat to her husband.

Core Idea
Zakat cannot be given to the wealthy, dependents, or one's own slaves.

This lesson continues the chapter on zakat disbursement by detailing who cannot receive zakat. It covers the absolute prohibition of giving to wealthy individuals, ascendants, descendants, and one's spouse, with an important intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a wife may give to her husband. Understanding these prohibitions ensures that zakat is correctly placed and fulfills the obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited recipients
Read the source text and list all categories explicitly mentioned: wealthy, father, grandfather, child, grandchild, wife, mukatab, slaves, wealthy slave, minor child of wealthy.
The list includes both direct and indirect recipients.
2
Classify the relatives by obligation
Note that ascendants (father, grandfather) and descendants (child, grandchild) are people on whom the giver must spend if they are in need. This is the principle of 'iyal (dependents).
The prohibition applies regardless of whether they are actual dependents.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Compare Abu Hanifa's view (woman cannot give to husband) with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view (she can). Identify the dalil used by each side.
The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's position.
4
Examine the dalil
Look at the hadith and athar quoted: the hadith 'La tahillu al-sadaqatu li ghani' and the hadith of Zaynab show the basis for the rulings.
The proofs include both Prophetic hadith and sayings of Companions.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
Determine the operative ruling for fatwa: a woman may give zakat to her husband; giving to ascendants/descendants is prohibited even if poor.
This affects real-life zakat distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ مَصَارِفِ الزَّكَاةِ
وَلا تُدْفَعُ إلَى غَنِيّ الوَلَا يَدْفَعُ الْمُزَكِّي زَكَاتَهُ إِلَى أَبِيهِ وَجَدِهِ وَإِنْ عَلَا وَلَا إِلَى وَلَدِهِ وَوَلَدِوَلَدِهِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَ وَلَا إلَى امْرَأَتِهِ ١٣ وَلَا تَدْفَعُ الْمَرْأَةُ إلَى زَوْجِهَا عِنْدَأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ تَدْفَعُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَى مُكَاتَبِهِ وَلَا إلَى مَلُوكِهِ ١٣ وَلَا إلَى مَمْلُوكٍ غَنِيْ وَلَا إِلَى وَلَدِغَنِيَ إِذَا كَانَ صَغِيرًا وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا تُدْفَعُ إِلَى غَنِيّ اعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِي إِلَّا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، أَوِ ابْنِ السَّبِيلِ، أَوْ جَارٍ فَقِيرٍ يُتَصَدَّقُ عَلَيْهِ، فَيُهْدِي لَكَ أَوْ يَدْعُوكَ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَخْذُ الصَّدَقَةِ وَهُوَ غَنِيٌّ، نمبر 1637)
ال وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَدْفَعُ الْمُزَكَّي زَكَاتَهُ إِلَى أَبِيهِ وَجَدِهِ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ، قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَجْعَلَ زَكَاتَكَ فِي ذَوِي قَرَابَتِكَ مَا لَمْ يَكُونُوا فِي عِيَالِكَ»،»(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، ما قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ يَدْفَعُ زَكَاتَهُ إِلَى قَرَابَتِهِ، 10531/مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ لِمَنِ الزَّكَاةُ ، نمبر 7162)
١٢ وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلا تَدْفَعُ الْمَرْأَةُ إلَى زَوْجِهَا \ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِي : قَالَتْ: يَا نَبِيَّ اللَّهِ، إِنَّكَ أَمَرْتَ الْيَوْمَ بِالصَّدَقَةِ، وَكَانَ عِنْدِي حُلِيٌّ لِي، فَأَرَدْتُ أَنْ أَتَصَدَّقَ بِهِ، فَزَعَمَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ: أَنَّهُ وَوَلَدَهُ أَحَقُّ مَنْ تَصَدَّقْتُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِمْ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ : صَدَقَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ، زَوْجُكِ وَوَلَدُكِ أَحَقُّ مَنْ تَصَدَّقْتِ بِهِ عَلَيْهِمْ»، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ الزَّكَاةِ عَلَى الأقارب، نمبر 1462)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَلَا يَدْفَعُ إِلَى مُكَاتَبِهِ \ عَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «الرَّجُلُ لَا يُعْطِي زَكَاةَ مَالِه مَنْ يُحْبَسُ عَلَى النَّفَقَةِ مِنْ ذَوِي أَرْحَامِهِ، وَلَا يُعْطِيهَا فِي كَفَنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا دَيْنِ مَيِّتٍ، وَلَا بِنَاءِ مَسْجِدٍ، وَلَا شِرَاءِ مُصْحَفٍ، وَلَا يَحُجُّ بِهَا، وَلَا تُعْطِيهَا مُكَاتِبَكَ، وَلَا تَبْتَاعُ بِمَا نَسَمَةً تُحَرِّرُهَا،مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ لِمَنِ الزَّكَاةُ ، نمبر 7170)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا إلَى مَمْلُوكٍ غَنِيْ وَلَا إلَى وَلَدِغَنِيَ إِذَا كَانَ صَغِيرًا \ عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ يَسَارٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةِ: لِغَازِ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، لِغَازِ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، أَوْ لِعَامِلٍ عَلَيْهَا، أَوْ لِغَارِمٍ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ كَانَ لَهُ جَارٌ مِسْكِينٌ فَتُصُدِّقَ عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ، فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ لِلْغَنِيّ " ،(سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَخْذُ
الصَّدَقَةِ وَهُوَ غَنِيٌّ ، نمبر 1635 /سنن ابن ماجه ، بَابُ مَنْ تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ ، نمبر 1841)
اصول: نابالغ بچہ باپ کے تابع ہوتا ہے، لہذا مالدار کا بچہ بھی مالدار ہی شمار ہو گا۔
And it is not given to a wealthy person, and the giver of zakat does not give his zakat to his father and grandfather, even if high, nor to his child and grandchild, even if low, nor to his wife. And the woman does not give to her husband according to Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said she gives to him. And he does not give to his mukatab, nor to his slaves, nor to a wealthy slave, nor to the child of a wealthy person if he is a minor. Evidence: (1) hadith to prove it is not given to a wealthy: from Abu Sa'id... Evidence: (1) saying of a Companion: from Ibn Abbas: 'There is no harm in putting your zakat among your relatives as long as they are not your dependents.' Evidence: (1) hadith to prove the woman does not give to her husband: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... Evidence: (1) saying of a Tabi'i: from al-Thawri... Evidence: (1) hadith to prove not to a wealthy slave nor to the child of a wealthy if minor: from 'Ata' ibn Yasar. Principle: A minor child is dependent on his father, so the child of a wealthy person is considered wealthy.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on zakat disbursement with rulings on who cannot receive zakat. First, zakat cannot be given to a wealthy person, defined as one who possesses the nisab or more. Then it lists relatives to whom the giver is prohibited from giving: ascendants (father, grandfather upward) and descendants (child, grandchild downward), and one's spouse. The ruling for the wife giving to her husband is disputed: Abu Hanifa says she cannot, analogizing that a husband is like a wife in being entitled to maintenance; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say she can, based on the hadith of Zaynab that the husband is most deserving. The relied-upon position is the latter. Also prohibited: giving to one's own mukatab (slave under contract), one's own slaves, a wealthy slave, and the minor child of a wealthy person (because the minor is considered wealthy by dependency). The proofs include the hadith prohibiting zakat to the wealthy, the athar of Ibn Abbas allowing it for relatives not dependents, and the hadith of the five exceptions for the wealthy (fighter, worker, debtor, purchaser, neighbor's gift). The final principle states that a minor child follows the father's wealth status.

Key Terms
غَنِيّ (ghaniyy): A person who possesses wealth equal to or exceeding the nisab (minimum threshold for zakat liability).
مُكَاتَب (mukātab): A slave who has a contract of manumission (kitabah) with his master, paying in installments.
عِيَال (iyāl): Dependents whom one is obliged to support financially.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, can a woman give her zakat to her husband?
A) Yes, she can
B) No, she cannot
C) Only if he is poor
D) Only with the permission of her father

Key Takeaway
Zakat must be given only to non-dependent, non-wealthy recipients, and cannot be given to one's own ascendants, descendants, spouse (with exception for wife giving to husband), or slaves.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate

Prohibition of Giving Zakat to Banu Hashim
Ruling with proofs: prohibition of zakat for Banu Hashim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to Banu Hashim and their mawali, and identify the three hadith proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Zakat is prohibited for Banu Hashim and their freed slaves because it is considered impure and they are purified by Allah.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that zakat cannot be given to the Prophet's family (Banu Hashim) and their clients. The ruling is supported by multiple hadith cited in the text. Understanding this ruling clarifies the category of those who cannot receive zakat and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening line: 'Zakat is not given to Banu Hashim'. Note that this is a prohibition. Also note that it includes their freed slaves (mawali).
The ruling is absolute, not conditional on wealth.
2
Analyze the first hadith proof
The first hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr states that charity is not permissible for the rich or the strong. Consider how this applies to Banu Hashim.
This hadith is general; the specific application to Banu Hashim comes from other texts.
3
Analyze the second hadith proof
The second hadith from Abu Rafi explicitly states: 'Charity is not permissible for us, and the freed slaves of a people are from themselves.' This directly includes mawali.
This is the strongest direct evidence.
4
Analyze the third hadith proof
The hadith of Barirah shows that what is charity for others becomes a gift for the Prophet, indicating that charity cannot be taken directly by the family.
This distinction reinforces the prohibition.
5
Understand the definition of Banu Hashim
The passage defines Banu Hashim as the descendants of four sons of Abd al-Muttalib: the Prophet, Abbas, Abu Talib's sons (Ali, Ja'far, 'Aqil), and Harith.
This excludes others like the descendants of Abu Lahab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ مَصَارِفِ الزَّكَاةِ
وَلَا يُدْفَعُ إِلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ وَهُمْ آلُ عَلِي وَآلُ عَبَّاسٍ إِلَى آخِرِهِ وَمَوَالِيهِمْ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُدْفَعُ إِلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ قَالَ: «لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِي، وَلَا لِذِي مِرَّةٍ سَوِي» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ يُعْطِي مِنَ الصَّدَقَةِ، وَحَدُّ الْغِنَى، نمبر 1634 / سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَنْ لا تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ، نمبر 652)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُدْفَعُ إِلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ عَنْ ابْنِ أَبِي رَافِعٍ، عَنْ أَبِي رَافِعٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَعَثَ رَجُلًا مِنْ بَنِي مَخْزُومٍ عَلَى الصَّدَقَةِ، فَقَالَ لِأَبِي رَافِع : اصْحَبْنِي كَيْمَا تُصِيبَ مِنْهَا، فَقَالَ: لَا، حَتَّى آتِي رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَأَسْأَلَهُ، فَانْطَلَقَ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ، فَسَأَلَهُ فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ لَا تَحِلُّ لَنَا، وَإِنَّ مَوَالِيَ القَوْمِ مِنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ» (ترمذى، مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الصَّدَقَةِ لِلنَّبِيِّ وَأَهْلِ بَيْتِهِ وَمَوَالِيهِ، 657)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يُدْفَعُ إِلَى بَنِي هَاشِمٍ عَنْ أَنَسٍ: «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أُتِيَ بِلَحْمٍ تُصُدِّقَ بِهِ عَلَى بَرِيرَةَ، فَقَالَ: هُوَ عَلَيْهَا صَدَقَةٌ، وَهُوَ لَنَا هَدِيَّةٌ» (بخاري : إذَا تَحَوَّلَتِ الصَّدَقَةُ، 1495)
اصول : خاندان نبوت صلی اللہ کو زکوۃ جائز نہیں ہے ، کیونکہ زکوۃ ایک قسم کا میل کچیل ہے ، لہذا ان کو نہ دیں۔
اصول: ہاشمی سے مراد: عبد المطلب بن ہاشم کے صرف چار بیٹے ہیں (۱) خود حضور صلی اللہ کی اولاد (۲) حضرت عباس کی اولاد (۳) ابو طالب کی اولاد میں (حضرت علی، حضرت جعفر، حضرت عقیل) (۴) حارث کی اولاد۔
Chapter on the categories of zakat
Zakat is not given to Banu Hashim, and they are the family of Ali and the family of Abbas to the end, and their freed slaves.
Proof (1): Hadith for establishing that zakat is not given to Banu Hashim: From Abdullah ibn Amr, from the Prophet (ﷺ) who said: 'Charity is not permissible for a rich person, nor for one who is strong and sound.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on who is given charity and the definition of wealth, no. 1634; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on those for whom charity is not permissible, no. 652)
Proof (2): Hadith for establishing that zakat is not given to Banu Hashim: From Ibn Abi Rafi, from Abu Rafi, that the Prophet (ﷺ) sent a man from Banu Makhzum to collect charity. He said to Abu Rafi: 'Accompany me so that you may get some of it.' He said: 'No, until I go to the Messenger of Allah and ask him.' So he went to the Prophet and asked, and he said: 'Charity is not permissible for us, and the freed slaves of a people are from themselves.' (Tirmidhi, no. 657)
Proof (3): Hadith for establishing that zakat is not given to Banu Hashim: From Anas: 'The Prophet (ﷺ) was brought meat that had been given in charity to Barirah. He said: It is charity for her, and for us it is a gift.' (Bukhari, no. 1495)
Principle: The family of the Prophet (ﷺ) is not permissible to receive zakat, because zakat is a kind of filth; therefore do not give to them.
Principle: Hashimi means the descendants of only four sons of Abd al-Muttalib bin Hashim: (1) the offspring of the Prophet himself (ﷺ), (2) the offspring of Abbas, (3) the offspring of Abu Talib (including Ali, Ja'far, 'Aqil), (4) the offspring of Harith.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on the categories of zakat states a clear ruling: zakat cannot be given to Banu Hashim, the clan of the Prophet (ﷺ), including their freed slaves. The commentator provides three hadith proofs: (1) the general hadith that charity is not permissible for the rich or the strong – Banu Hashim are considered honorable and not needy in the sense of zakat; (2) the specific hadith of Abu Rafi where the Prophet explicitly says charity is not permissible for his family; (3) the hadith of Barirah showing that what is charity for others becomes a gift for the Prophet, indicating the distinction. The commentator then explains the usul: zakat is considered a kind of filth (due to being taken from people's wealth), so it is not appropriate for the noble lineage of the Prophet. The second usul clarifies the definition of Hashimi: only the descendants of four sons of Abd al-Muttalib (the Prophet, Abbas, Abu Talib's sons, and Harith). Others, like the descendants of Abu Lahab, are not included and may receive zakat. This is a Hanafi ruling with scriptural proof.

Key Terms
بَنُو هَاشِمٍ (Banu Hashim): The clan of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), specifically the descendants of Hashim ibn Abd Manaf. Here defined as the four lines: the Prophet's progeny, Abbas, Abu Talib's sons, and Harith.
مَوَالِي (mawali): Freed slaves or clients of Banu Hashim; they are treated as part of the family in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, to whom of the following is it permissible to give zakat?
A) A descendant of Abbas who is poor
B) A freed slave of a Hashimi
C) A descendant of Abu Lahab who is poor
D) The Prophet's daughter Fatimah

Key Takeaway
Zakat is absolutely prohibited for Banu Hashim and their mawali; it is not based on poverty but on lineage.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Giving Zakat to a Person Thought Poor but Turns Out Undeserving
Ruling on zakat validity when recipient is later found undeserving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) on zakat given under mistaken assumption of poverty and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Zakat given in good faith suffices even if recipient later proves undeserving—intention after investigation is key.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in zakat: you give to someone you genuinely believe is poor, but later discover they were rich, a Hashimi, a disbeliever, or even your own father. Does your zakat count? The Hanafi school has an internal debate between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other. Let’s dissect the proofs and the practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Read the passage and locate the two positions: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad vs Abu Yusuf. What is the specific scenario?
Focus on the key phrase 'فَلَا إِعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ' vs 'عَلَيْهِ الْإِعَادَةُ'.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad)
Analyze the hadith of Ma'n bin Yazid: how does the Prophet's ruling support their view? What principle does it establish?
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 1422.
3
Examine Abu Yusuf's proof
Look at the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i cited by Abu Yusuf. How does it conflict with the hadith?
Consider that Ibrahim's view is a qawl al-tabi'i, not a direct prophetic text.
4
Understand the special case of slave/mukatab
Note the exception: if the recipient turns out to be one's own slave or mukatab, the zakat is invalid for all Imams. Why does ownership block validity?
This is because the giver would indirectly benefit.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two positions? Which one is mufta bihi (operative)?
The usul note indicates the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا دَفَعَ الزَّكَاةَ إِلَى رَجُلٍ يَظُنُّهُ فَقِيرًا ثُمَّ بَانَ أَنَّهُ غَنِيٌّ أَوْ هَاشِمِيٌّ أَوْ كَافِرٌ أَوْ دَفَعَ فِي ظُلْمَةٍ إِلَى فَقِيرٍ ثُمَّ بَانَ أَنَّهُ أَبُوهُ أَوِ ابْنُهُ فَلَا إِعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ
وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْإِعَادَةُ
وَلَوْ دَفَعَ إِلَى شَخْصٍ يَظُنُّهُ فَقِيرًا ثُمَّ بَانَ أَنَّهُ عَبْدُهُ أَوْ مُكَاتَبُهُ لَمْ يَجْزْ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ إِذَا دَفَعَ الزَّكَاةَ ... أَنَّ مَعْنَ بْنَ يَزِيدَ حَدَّثَهُ قَالَ: «بَايَعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَا وَأَبي وَجَدِي، وَخَطَبَ عَلَيَّ فَأَنْكَحَنِي، وَخَاصَمْتُ إِلَيْهِ: كَانَ أَبِي يَزِيدُ أَخْرَجَ دَنَانِيرَ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِهَا، فَوَضَعَهَا عِنْدَ رَجُلٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ، فَجِئْتُ فَأَخَذْتُهَا، فَأَتَيْتُهُ بِهَا، فَقَالَ: وَاللهِ مَا إِيَّاكَ أَرَدْتُ، فَخَاصَمْتُهُ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ : لَكَ مَا نَوَيْتَ يَا يَزِيدُ، وَلَكَ مَا أَخَذْتَ يَا مَعْنُ.»، (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ : إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ عَلَى ابْنِهِ وَهُوَ لَا يَشْعُرُ ،نمبر 1422)
وجه (۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ ... عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، فِي الرَّجُلِ يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ إِلَى فَقِيرٍ لَمْ يَتَبَيَّنْ لَهُ أَنَّهُ غَنِيٌّ؟ قَالَ: «أَجْزَى عَنْهُ»، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ لِغَنِي وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ ،نمبر 10543)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ ... عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، فِي الرَّجُلِ يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ الْغَنِيَّ وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ؟ قَالَ: «لَا يُجْزِيهِ»، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ لِغَنِي وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ ،نمبر 10544)
اصول: تحقیق کے بعد بھی اگر کسی غیر مستحق کو زکوۃ دیدی گئی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی۔
And Abu Hanifa and Muhammad said: When one gives zakat to a man whom he thinks is poor, then it becomes apparent that he is rich, or a Hashimi, or a disbeliever, or he gave in darkness to a poor person and then it becomes apparent that he is his father or his son, then there is no repetition required upon him.
And Abu Yusuf said: It is not valid and repetition is required.
And if he gives to a person thinking him poor then it becomes apparent that he is his slave or his mukatab, it does not suffice.
Proof (1): Hadith for establishing the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad regarding giving zakat... That Ma'n bin Yazid narrated: 'I gave allegiance to the Messenger of Allah, I and my father and my grandfather... (the story)... He said: For you is what you intended, O Yazid, and for you is what you took, O Ma'n.' (Bukhari, no. 1422)
Proof (2): Saying of a tabi'i for establishing the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: From al-Hasan regarding a man who gives his zakat to a poor person without it being clear to him that he is rich? He said: 'It suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10543)
Proof (1): Saying of a tabi'i for establishing the position of Abu Yusuf: From Ibrahim regarding a man who gives his zakat to a rich person without knowing? He said: 'It does not suffice him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10544)
Principle: Even after investigation, if zakat is given to someone undeserving, the zakat is fulfilled.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of zakat when the recipient later turns out to be undeserving. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that if the giver had a reasonable belief (zann) that the recipient was poor, and it later transpires that he was rich, Hashimi, a disbeliever, or even the giver's own father or son given in darkness, the zakat is valid and no repetition is required. Their proof is the hadith of Ma'n bin Yazid, where the Prophet ruled that the giver gets what he intended when the charity went to his own son unknowingly. They also cite the view of al-Hasan al-Basri. Abu Yusuf, however, requires repetition if the recipient is not deserving at the time of giving, based on the view of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The commentator then adds a separate rule: if one gives to a person thinking him poor but he turns out to be his own slave or mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission), the zakat does not suffice according to all Imams (presumably the same ruling as Abu Yusuf's general position, but the text attributes it to no one specifically, so it is likely the relied-upon position). The concluding usul principle reaffirms that after proper investigation, if the zakat reaches a non-eligible person, the obligation is discharged. This is a nuanced area where the intention and reasonable diligence matter.

Key Terms
إِعَادَة (i'adah): Repetition or re-giving of zakat; required if the original payment is considered invalid.
ظُلْمَة (zulmah): Darkness; refers to giving zakat at night or in a dark place where the giver cannot identify the recipient.
مُكَاتَب (mukatab): A slave who has contracted with his master to earn and pay for his freedom; he is a slave but with special rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if a person gives zakat to someone he believes is poor but later discovers the recipient was his father, what must he do?
A) Repeat the zakat
B) The zakat is valid and no repetition is needed
C) Give additional charity to compensate
D) Seek forgiveness but still repeat the zakat

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat given under a reasonable belief of the recipient's eligibility is valid even if the recipient later proves undeserving, based on the prophetic hadith prioritizing intention.

Zakat — Almsgiving
beginner
6 min
Zakat Prohibited for Nisab Owners with Exceptions
Ruling that zakat is not given to one who owns a nisab of any wealth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general ruling that zakat may not be given to a nisab owner and identify the five exceptions from the hadith.

Core Idea
Zakat is for the poor; giving it to a nisab owner is prohibited unless they are one of five exempted types.

Zakat is a pillar of Islam meant to purify wealth and support the needy. But what if the potential recipient himself owns wealth? This passage establishes that a person who owns a nisab (minimum zakatable amount) cannot receive zakat, with clear exceptions from the Sunnah. Understanding this ruling prevents misallocation of zakat funds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of giving zakat (دفع الزكاة) to a person who owns a nisab. The ruling is 'la yajuz' (not permissible), indicating prohibition (haram).
The prohibition is general; exceptions are listed separately.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith from Ata' ibn Yasar: 'Charity is not permissible for a rich person except for five...' This hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and Ibn Majah, classified as ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
The hadith uses the word 'sadaqah' which includes zakat, as per scholarly consensus.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'la tahillu al-sadaqatu li-ghaniyy' (charity is not permissible for a rich person) establishes the general prohibition. The term 'ghaniyy' (rich) is interpreted as one who owns a nisab, as per Hanafi usul. The exceptions confirm the rule.
The exceptions are: fighter, zakat collector, debtor, purchaser of charity, and recipient of a gift from a poor neighbor.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this ruling. The exceptions are agreed upon. Cross-madhhab, the ruling is universally accepted (muttafaq alayh).
Some schools may define 'rich' differently (e.g., having 200 dirhams or being self-sufficient), but the principle is the same.
5
Apply to contemporary cases
Today, a person who owns 85g of gold or its cash equivalent (nisab) cannot receive zakat, unless they fall under one of the five exceptions (e.g., a student fighter, a zakat administrator, a person in debt).
The nisab is based on current value of gold/silver.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ نِصَابًا مِنْ أَيِّ مَالٍ كَانَ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ ... عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ يَسَارٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةٍ: لِغَازٍ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، أَوْ لِعَامِلٍ عَلَيْهَا، أَوْ لِغَارِمٍ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ كَانَ لَهُ جَارٌ مِسْكِينٌ فَتُصْدِقَ عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ، فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ لِلْغَنِي" (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَخْذُ الصَّدَقَةِ وَهُوَ غني، نمبر 1635 / سنن ابن ماجه، بَابُ مَنْ تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ، نمبر 1841)
And it is not permissible to give zakat to one who owns a nisab of any kind of wealth.
Proof (1): Hadith establishing that zakat is not given to one who owns a nisab... From Ata' ibn Yasar that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Charity is not permissible for a rich person except for five: a fighter in the way of Allah, or a collector of it (zakat), or a debtor, or a man who buys it with his wealth, or a man who has a poor neighbor and gives charity to the poor person then the poor person gifts it to the rich person.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1635; Sunan Ibn Majah, no. 1841)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that zakat cannot be given to a person who owns a nisab (the minimum amount of wealth subject to zakat) of any kind of property. The proof is a hadith listing exceptions to the general prohibition of giving charity to the rich: zakat may be given to the rich in specific circumstances such as a fighter, zakat collector, debtor, etc. The commentator uses this hadith to establish the general rule. Note that the nisab for zakatable items varies (e.g., gold, silver, trade goods), but ownership of any nisab makes one rich for the purpose of receiving zakat. This is a straightforward ruling with scriptural support.

Key Terms
نِصَاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth (e.g., 85g gold or 595g silver) that makes one obligated to pay zakat and also disqualified from receiving it.
غَنِيّ (ghaniyy): A rich person; in this ruling, one who owns a nisab of any zakatable wealth.
غَازٍ (ghazi): A fighter in the cause of Allah; one of the five exceptions allowed to receive zakat despite being rich.
عَامِل (aamil): A zakat collector or administrator; one of the five exceptions who may receive zakat as compensation.
غَارِم (gharim): A debtor who cannot pay his debts; one of the five exceptions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following persons may NOT receive zakat if they own a nisab?
A) A person fighting in jihad without salary
B) A person who is in debt and unable to pay
C) A person who owns a car worth the nisab and has no other major expenses
D) A person who collects zakat on behalf of the state

Key Takeaway
Zakat is prohibited for a nisab owner unless they fall under one of the five exceptions from the hadith.

Zakat Permissible for a Healthy but Poor Earner
Ruling on zakat recipient eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a healthy earner and apply the criterion that zakat eligibility depends on not owning a nisab, not on earning ability.

Core Idea
Zakat is for those who lack a nisab, not for those who lack a job.

A common assumption is that zakat should only be given to those who are unable to work. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the key criterion for zakat eligibility is the absence of a nisab (minimum wealth threshold), regardless of earning capacity. The passage cites two statements from the tabi'un (successors) to support this, emphasizing that even a healthy, earning individual who does not own a nisab may receive zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text begins with a clear ruling: it is permissible to give zakat to one who owns less than a nisab. Note that this applies even if the recipient is healthy and able to earn.
The ruling overrides the assumption that only the physically incapacitated qualify.
2
Examine the first proof from Hammad
The commentator cites Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman, who states: 'One who does not have wealth reaching the zakat threshold is given from zakat.' This directly links eligibility to the absence of a nisab.
Hammad's statement is a clear precedent from the tabi'un.
3
Examine the second proof from 'Amir
The second proof from 'Amir al-Sha'bi adds a practical caution: give only enough so that the recipient does not themselves reach the nisab. This reinforces that the nisab is the boundary.
This also implies that zakat should not make the recipient wealthy enough to become a zakat payer.
4
Derive the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school adopts this view: the definition of poor (faqir) or needy (miskin) for zakat eligibility is one who does not own a nisab. Earning ability is irrelevant.
This is consistent with the broader Hanafi definition of need.
5
Apply the ruling to a modern scenario
Consider a healthy freelancer who earns but has no savings. Since he owns less than a nisab, he qualifies for zakat despite being able to work.
This demonstrates the practical difference from other schools that may require physical inability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُهَا إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَحِيحًا مُكْتَسِبًا
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُهَا إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ أَقَلَّ ... سَمِعْتُ حَمَّادًا، يَقُولُ: «مَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عِنْدَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُغُ فِيهِ الزَّكَاةَ أُعْطِيَ مِنَ الزَّكَاةِ»، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: لَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ إِذَا مَلَكَ خَمْسِينَ دِرْهَماً، نمبر 10435)
وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُهَا إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ أَقَلَّ ... عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «أَعْطِ مِنَ الزَّكَاةِ مَا دُونَ أَنْ يَحِلَّ عَلَى مَنْ تُعْطِيهِ الزَّكَاةَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الزَّكَاةِ قَدْرُ مَا يُعْطِي مِنْهَا، نمبر 10430)
And it is permissible to give it (zakat) to one who owns less than that (i.e., less than a nisab), even if he is healthy and earning.
Proof (1): Saying of a tabi'i establishing that it is permissible to give to one who owns less... I heard Hammad saying: 'One who does not have wealth that reaches the zakat threshold is given from zakat.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10435)
Proof (2): Saying of a tabi'i establishing that it is permissible to give to one who owns less... From 'Amir, he said: 'Give from zakat (to such an extent) that does not make the recipient reach the zakat threshold.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10430)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage states the permissibility of giving zakat to a person who possesses wealth less than a nisab, even if he is physically healthy and able to earn a living. The key point is that the eligibility criterion for receiving zakat is the absence of a nisab, not the inability to work. The commentator provides two proofs from the tabi'un (successors): Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman and 'Amir al-Sha'bi. Hammad's statement indicates that anyone who does not own a nisab (the minimum threshold for zakat) qualifies. 'Amir's statement even warns not to give so much that the recipient becomes rich himself. Thus, a poor earning person can receive zakat to meet his needs, as long as he does not own a nisab. This is consistent with the Hanafi view that zakat is for the poor (fuqara) and needy (masakin), defined as those who do not own a nisab.

Key Terms
مُكْتَسِب (muktasib): A person who is able to earn a living, but still does not own a nisab; they are eligible for zakat despite earning ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, to whom is it permissible to give zakat?
A) A healthy person who owns 100g gold
B) A healthy person who owns 50 silver dirhams (less than nisab)
C) A rich debtor
D) A rich fighter

Key Takeaway
Zakat eligibility depends solely on not owning a nisab, not on the ability to earn.

Disliking Transfer of Zakat from One Town to Another
Ruling with hadith proof against transferring zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transferring zakat from one town to another and explain the evidence from the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
Zakat should be distributed locally; transferring it to another town is disliked but valid.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on transferring zakat from one locality to another. The passage clearly states it is disliked (makruh) and provides the hadith of Mu'adh as proof. Understanding this ruling helps ensure zakat distribution aligns with the Sunnah while allowing flexibility when needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states 'it is disliked to transfer zakat from one town to another.' Note the hukm level: makruh tanzih (disliked but not haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'take from their rich and give back to their poor.' The imperative is tied to the same locality.
Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 1496
3
Analyze the dalil's implication
The instruction to give to local poor implies that local distribution is preferred; transferring elsewhere goes against the default.
The dalala (indication) is zanni, allowing for exceptions.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
The definition of 'balad' (town) and the condition of need: if there is no local poor or greater need elsewhere, the dislike is lifted and transfer becomes permissible.
This is based on istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ نَقْلُ الزَّكَاةِ مِنْ بَلَدٍ إِلَى بَلَدٍ
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ نَقْلُ الزَّكَاةِ مِنْ بَلَدٍ إِلَى بَلَدٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم لِمُعَاذِ بْنِ جَبَلٍ: إِنَّ اللَّهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ خَمْسَ صَلَوَاتٍ فِي كُلِّ يَوْمٍ وَلَيْلَةٍ، فَإِنْ هُمْ أَطَاعُوا لَكَ بِذَلِكَ، فَأَخْبِرْهُمْ أَنَّ اللهَ قَدْ فَرَضَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَدَقَةً تُؤْخَذُ مِنْ أَغْنِيَائِهِمْ فَتُرَدُّ عَلَى فُقَرَائِهِمْ، (بخاري شريف بَابُ أَخْذِ الصَّدَقَةِ مِنَ الْأَغْنَاءِ وَتُرَدَّ فِي الْفُقَرَاءِ حَيْثُ كَانُوا، نمبر 1496)
And it is disliked to transfer zakat from one town to another.
Proof (1): Hadith for establishing that it is disliked to transfer zakat from one town to another: From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them) who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal: Indeed Allah has prescribed upon them five prayers every day and night; if they obey you in that, then inform them that Allah has prescribed upon them a charity (zakat) taken from their rich and given back to their poor.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 1496)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage states that it is makruh (disliked) to transfer zakat from one town (balad) to another town. The proof is the famous hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) instructs Mu'adh in Yemen to take zakat from the rich and distribute it to the poor of that same locality. This indicates that the default is local distribution. The ruling is one of dislike (tanzihan, not tahriman), meaning it is better not to transfer but if done, the zakat is still valid. The Hanafi school holds that transferring is permissible if there is a need (e.g., no deserving recipients locally, or greater need elsewhere), but it is usually makruh without a valid reason.

Key Terms
نَقْل الزَّكَاةِ (naql al-zakat): Transferring the zakat amount from the town where it was collected to another town for distribution.
بَلَد (balad): A town or locality; the area where the zakat is collected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on transferring zakat from one town to another according to this passage?
A) It is haram
B) It is makruh (disliked)
C) It is wajib
D) It is mustahab

Key Takeaway
Zakat should ideally be distributed locally; transferring it to another place is disliked but valid, and permissible if there is a genuine need.

Ruling on Giving Zakat to One's Own Slave or Mukatab
Matn ruling with Abu Yusuf's opinion and athar proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when zakat is given to one's own slave or mukatab, explain the evidence from the athar of Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i, and apply the rule to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Zakat given to your own slave or mukatab is invalid and must be repeated.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Quduri's Matn: if a person gives his zakat to someone he believes is poor, but later discovers the recipient was his own slave or mukatab, the zakat is not valid. Abu Yusuf explicitly adds that the payment must be repeated. The proof is drawn from an athar (statement) of the Tabi‘i Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i regarding giving zakat to a wealthy person unknowingly. Understanding this ruling clarifies the strict requirement that zakat must reach a legitimate recipient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving zakat to a person believed to be poor, but who turns out to be the giver's own slave or mukatab. The ruling is that it is not valid (lam yajz).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i, who was asked about giving zakat to a wealthy person unknowingly; he replied: 'It does not suffice him.'
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (no. 10544).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation of sufficiency (لا يُجْزِيهِ) shows that valid zakat requires the recipient to be eligible. By qiyas (analogy), giving to one's own slave or mukatab—who are ineligible—renders the zakat invalid.
The effective cause (illa) is the ineligibility of the recipient.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf agrees with the ruling and emphasizes that repetition (i‘ādah) is required. This is consistent with the general Hanafi position.
No intra-madhhab dispute exists; all agree on the outcome.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that the zakat is invalid and must be repeated, regardless of the giver's good faith.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَجُوزُ وَعَلَيْهِ الْإِعَادَةُ وَلَوْ دَفَعَ إِلَى شَخْصٍ يَظُنُّهُ فَقِيرًا ثُمَّ بَانَ أَنَّهُ عَبْدُهُ أَوْ مُكَاتَبُهُ لَمْ يَجْزْ ١٨
وجه: (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، فِي الرَّجُل يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ الْغَنِيَّ وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ؟ قَالَ: «لَا يُجْزِيهِ»» ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الرَّجُلِ يُعْطِي زَكَاتَهُ لِغَنِيٍّ وَهُوَ لَا يَعْلَمُ ، غبر 10544)
And Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible and he must repeat. And if he pays to a person whom he thinks is poor, then it becomes apparent that he is his slave or his mukatab, it is not valid. [18] Evidence: Statement of a Tabi‘i: from Ibrahim, concerning a man who gives his zakat to a wealthy person while he does not know? He said: ‘It does not suffice him.’ (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri along with the opinion of Abu Yusuf. The ruling states that if a person gives his zakat to someone he believes to be poor, but later discovers the recipient was his own slave or mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission), the zakat is not valid and must be repeated. Abu Yusuf affirms this and emphasizes the need to repeat it. The evidence is an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i, a leading Tabi‘i, who was asked about a man who gives his zakat to a wealthy person unknowingly; he ruled that it does not suffice. This underscores the Hanafi principle that zakat must reach a legitimate recipient (one who is not rich and not a dependent) for the obligation to be fulfilled.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukātab): A slave who has contracted with his master to purchase his freedom, paying in installments.
غني (ghanī): A person who owns a nisab (minimum threshold of wealth) or sufficient property that makes him ineligible for zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person gives his zakat to someone he believes is poor, but later finds out the recipient was his own slave, the zakat is:
A) Valid and no repeat needed
B) Invalid and must be repeated
C) Valid if the slave was a mukatab
D) Valid because the giver acted in good faith

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, zakat given to an ineligible recipient—even unknowingly—is invalid and must be repeated; knowledge of eligibility is not a condition, but actual eligibility is.

Prohibition of Giving Zakat to a Nisab Owner with Hadith Proof
Ruling with hadith proof on zakat eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on giving zakat to a nisab-owner, identify the five exceptions from the hadith, and apply the ruling to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Zakat is forbidden for one who owns nisab, except five specific cases.

This lesson presents a core ruling from the matn of al-Quduri: it is not permissible to give zakat to anyone who owns a nisab of any property. The proof is a hadith listing five exceptions. Understanding this rule ensures zakat reaches its rightful recipients and is a key discrimination skill for the mufti.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Extract the direct ruling from the matn: 'It is not permissible to pay zakat to one who owns a nisab.' Note the absolute prohibition (lā yajūz).
The ruling is clear and unconditional.
2
Define the criterion: nisab
Identify that 'owns a nisab' is the threshold. Nisab varies by wealth type (e.g., 200 dirhams of silver, 85g of gold). Ownership of a full nisab makes a person 'rich' for zakat distribution.
The matn says 'from any property.'
3
Identify the five exceptions from the hadith
Read the hadith and list the five exceptions: the fighter (ghāzin), the zakat collector ('āmil), the debtor (ghārim), the buyer of zakat items, and the case of a gift from a poor neighbour.
The exceptions are exhaustive; no others.
4
Connect the hadith to zakat
The hadith says 'charity (ṣadaqah) is not permissible for a rich person.' Zakat is a type of obligatory charity, so the ruling applies directly to zakat.
The word ṣadaqah includes both obligatory and voluntary charity.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a person who owns nisab, determine if any exception applies. If none, giving zakat to him is haram.
Example: a wealthy debtor may receive zakat to repay his debt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ دَفْعُ الزَّكَاةِ إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ نِصَابًا مِنْ أَيِّ مَالٍ كَانَ 19
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ يَسَارٍ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: " لَا تَحِلُّ الصَّدَقَةُ لِغَنِيّ إِلَّا لِخَمْسَةٍ لِغَازٍ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، أَوْ لِعَامِلٍ عَلَيْهَا، أَوْ لِغَارِمٍ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ اشْتَرَاهَا بِمَالِهِ، أَوْ لِرَجُلٍ كَانَ لَهُ جَارٌ مِسْكِينٌ فَتُصْدِقَ عَلَى الْمِسْكِينِ، فَأَهْدَاهَا الْمِسْكِينُ لِلْغَنِيِّ (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ يَجُوزُ لَهُ أَخْذُ الصَّدَقَةِ وَهُوَ غني، غير 1635/ سنن ابن ماجه ، بَابُ مَنْ تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ، غمبر 1841)
And it is not permissible to pay zakat to one who owns a nisab of any property whatsoever. [19] Evidence: Proof by hadith from ‘Ata’ ibn Yasar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: “Charity is not permissible for a rich person except for five: a fighter in the way of Allah, or a collector of it, or a debtor, or a man who buys it with his own money, or a man who has a poor neighbour and gives charity to the poor neighbour and then the poor neighbour gifts it to the rich.” (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 1635; Sunan Ibn Majah, no. 1841)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage provides a clear ruling: it is absolutely impermissible (lā yajūz) to give zakat to a person who owns a full nisab of any kind of wealth, be it cash, goods, livestock, etc. The proof is the well-known hadith that explicitly states that charity (including zakat) is not permissible for a wealthy person except in five specific situations: the fighter in jihad, the zakat collector, the debtor, the person who purchases the zakat items with his own money, and the case where a poor person receives charity and then gives it as a gift to a rich person. This ruling protects the objective of zakat, which is to provide for the needy, not to increase the wealth of the rich.

Key Terms
نصاب (niṣāb): The minimum amount of wealth (e.g., gold, silver, merchandise, livestock) that makes a person liable to pay zakat and also makes him ineligible to receive it.
غاز (ghāzin): A person engaged in military expedition in the path of Allah (jihad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, giving zakat to a rich person is permissible in how many exceptional cases?
A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Giving zakat to anyone who owns a nisab is haram unless one of the five exceptions from the hadith applies.

6 min
Giving Zakat to a Healthy Earner Below Nisab
Matn ruling with athar proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving zakat to a healthy earner whose wealth is below nisab and cite the athar evidence.

Core Idea
Zakat eligibility depends on actual wealth below nisab, not on earning capacity.

Zakat is an obligatory charity given to specific categories of recipients, primarily the poor. A common question is whether a healthy, working person can receive zakat if their savings are low. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling based on the matn of Al-Quduri and supporting statements from the Tabi'un.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn states that it is permissible (jā'iz) to give zakat to someone who owns less than nisab, even if they are healthy and earning. The key point is that eligibility hinges on actual wealth, not on ability to work.
The term 'muktasib' refers to someone who earns a livelihood, but earning alone does not make them rich.
2
Locate the evidence (athar)
Two statements from the Tabi'un are cited: Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman says that one who does not have nisab should be given zakat; 'Amir al-Sha'bi says to give zakat without making the recipient reach nisab. These are recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
In Hanafi usul, sayings of the Companions and successors are valid proofs (qawl sahabi/tabi'i).
3
Understand the legal basis (wajh al-dalalah)
Hammad's statement directly links eligibility to the absence of nisab. 'Amir's statement implies that the giver should not give so much that the recipient attains nisab, confirming nisab as the threshold.
Thus, a healthy earner with less than nisab is still considered poor and eligible for zakat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ دَفْعُهَا إِلَى مَنْ يَمْلِكُ أَقَلَّ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ صَحِيحًا مُكْتَسِبًا ۲۰
وجه: (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت سَمِعْتُ حَمَّادًا، يَقُولُ: «مَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عِنْدَهُ مَالٌ يَبْلُغُ فِيهِ الزَّكَاةَ أُعْطِيَ مِنَ الزَّكَاةِ»، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: لَا تَحِلُّ لَهُ الصَّدَقَةُ إِذَا مَلَكَ خَمْسِينَ دِرْهَماً ، نمبر 10435)
وجه:(۲) قول التابعي لثبوت عَنْ عَامِرٍ، قَالَ: «أَعْطِ مِنَ الزَّكَاةِ مَا دُونَ أَنْ يَحِلَّ عَلَى مَنْ تُعْطِيهِ الزَّكَاةَ» مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الزَّكَاةِ قَدْرُ مَا يُعْطِي مِنْهَا ، نمبر 10430)
And it is permissible to pay it to one who owns less than that (i.e., less than nisab), even if he is healthy and earning. [20] Evidence: (1) Statement of a Tabi‘i: I heard Hammad say: ‘One who does not have wealth that reaches the zakat threshold should be given from zakat.’ (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...) (2) Statement of a Tabi‘i: From ‘Amir, he said: ‘Give from zakat (to one) as long as it does not make the recipient (rich) such that zakat becomes prohibited for him.’ (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage clarifies a key point: the eligibility to receive zakat is based solely on whether one owns the nisab threshold. Even if a person is physically healthy and earns a living, as long as his total wealth is below the nisab, he is still considered poor and may receive zakat. Two athar from prominent Tabi‘un – Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman and ‘Amir al-Sha‘bi – are cited as evidence. Hammad explicitly says that one who does not have a nisab should be given zakat. ‘Amir’s statement warns not to give so much that the recipient becomes wealthy, implying that the criterion is the nisab, not physical ability or employment. This distinction prevents the misconception that only the physically disabled or unemployed may receive zakat.

Key Terms
مكتسب (muktasib): A person who works and earns a living, not dependent on charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a healthy individual earns a daily wage but his total savings are less than the nisab, can he receive zakat according to this passage?
A) Yes, it is permissible
B) No, because he is earning
C) Only if he is sick
D) Only if he owns no property

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the sole criterion for zakat eligibility is actual wealth below nisab, not earning capacity or health.

Zakat Given to an Ineligible Recipient After Investigation
A Hanafi principle on zakat validity after investigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zakat is considered fulfilled if given after due investigation to a person later found to be ineligible.

Core Idea
Zakat is valid after reasonable investigation even if recipient is later found ineligible.

The first principle derived from the chapter on zakat recipients addresses a common concern: what if you give zakat to someone you believe is eligible, but later discover they were not? This lesson explains the Hanafi view based on acting on apparent circumstances and the difficulty of perfect knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act in question is giving zakat after performing an investigation (tahqiq) into the recipient's eligibility.
2
Recognize the condition
Note that the key condition is that the giver conducted a reasonable investigation. Without this condition, the ruling differs.
Tahqiq is the due diligence required.
3
State the ruling
The zakat is considered valid (sahih) and the obligation is discharged, even if the recipient later proves ineligible.
4
Understand the rationale
The ruling is based on the principle of acting on apparent circumstances (al-umur bi-maqasidiha) and the difficulty of attaining perfect knowledge.
This avoids undue hardship for the giver.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: تحقیق کے بعد بھی اگر کسی غیر مستحق کو زکوۃ دیدی گئی تو زکوۃ ادا ہو جائے گی۔
اصول : کسی ایک مستحق زکوۃ کو اتنی رقم دینا کہ وہ خود نصاب کا مالک ہو جائے یا اس سے زائد رقم دینا مکروہ ہے، البتہ ضرورۃ جائز ہے۔
اصول : اموال زکوۃ کو بلا کسی ضرورت ایک شہر سے دوسرے شہر منتقل کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
Principle: Even after investigation, if zakat is given to an ineligible person, the zakat will be considered fulfilled. Principle: Giving so much zakat to a single eligible recipient that he himself becomes the owner of nisab or more than that is disliked, but permissible in necessity. Principle: Transferring zakat wealth from one city to another without any necessity is disliked.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This section presents three important principles (usul) derived from the preceding rulings and hadith. First: if a person gives zakat to someone he believes is eligible after proper investigation (tahqiq), but it later turns out the recipient was ineligible, the zakat is still considered valid (i.e., the obligation is discharged). This is based on the principle of acting on apparent circumstances and the difficulty of perfect knowledge. Second: it is makruh to give such a large amount to a single recipient that he crosses the nisab threshold, because that defeats the purpose of zakat (making the poor self-sufficient only to the point of need). However, if necessity dictates (e.g., a large debt of a poor person), it becomes permissible. Third: as stated earlier, transferring zakat from one city to another without a legitimate reason (like transferring to needy relatives or a more destitute community) is disliked. These usul encapsulate the practical takeaways for the payer of zakat.

Key Terms
تحقیق (taḥqīq): Due diligence in ascertaining the eligibility of a potential zakat recipient.
مستحق (mustaḥiq): A person eligible to receive zakat (the eight categories mentioned in the Quran).
ضرورت (ḍarūrat): Necessity – a situation that necessitates departing from the normal ruling to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first usul, if a person investigates and gives zakat to someone he believes is eligible, but later it turns out the recipient was ineligible, what is the ruling on the zakat?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated
B) It is valid and the obligation is fulfilled
C) It is valid only if the giver is wealthy
D) It depends on the amount given

Key Takeaway
Zakat given after reasonable investigation is valid even if the recipient is later found ineligible.
